Ambiguous Manumission in Terminal Illness: The One-Third Limitation
Explains the effect of terminal illness on share distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the effect of terminal illness on the distribution of freedom in ambiguous manumission and apply the rule that manumission is valid only up to one-third of the estate without heirs' consent.

Core Idea
Manumission in terminal illness is treated as a bequest: valid up to one-third of the estate without heirs' consent.

We previously examined ambiguous manumission (e.g., 'one of you is free') when the master is healthy. Now we extend the case to the master being terminally ill (marad al-mawt) and the heirs not consenting. The shares become subject to the one-third limit for bequests, but the intra-Hanafi dispute over the internal slave's share remains. This lesson clarifies the interplay between the manumission rules and the law of wills.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the healthy and sick scenarios
Identify that in health, the full shares apply regardless of estate value. In terminal illness, manumission is analogous to a will and limited to one-third.
This changes the ruling from absolute to conditional.
2
Identify the agreed shares for established and external
Three-quarters of the established slave and half of the external are freed by agreement, based on the two assignments (first and second).
These shares are derived from the logic of the assignments, not from the one-third rule.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute over the internal slave
Imam Muhammad holds that only a quarter of the internal is freed, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that half is freed. Understand their reasoning: Muhammad argues consistency with the established case; the two argue the second assignment aims for half but the established has a prior claim.
This dispute is the same as in the healthy case.
4
Apply the one-third limitation from bequest rules
Add the total value of freed shares. If they exceed one-third of the estate, heirs' consent is needed. If they are within one-third, it is valid without consent.
The passage notes that the issue is framed exactly when the shares exceed one-third.

And if he says it while sick and the heir does not consent. Likewise half of the external is freed; because he is included only in the first assignment, which necessitated freeing half of each of the two included in it: i.e., the established and the internal. Its detail will come, God willing, in its place. If they equal or are less than one-third of the manumitter's wealth, even if he has other property besides these slaves, then there is no need for the heir's permission.

Commentary
This passage extends the previous scenario to the case where the master is terminally ill (marad al-mawt) and the heirs do not consent to the manumission. It restates the agreed-upon shares: three-quarters of the established, half of the external, and then reasserts the dispute over the internal (half according to Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf, quarter according to Muhammad). The commentator explains that the answer from the two (Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf) is that the second assignment intends half for each, but the established has a prior claim, so only a quarter is added; however, the internal has no claim, so the full half applies. The passage then notes that the entire distribution is subject to the one-third rule for bequests: if the total freed value exceeds one-third of the estate, the heirs' permission is needed. If it is within one-third or less, no permission is required. The commentator also clarifies that the condition of non-permission applies only when the freed shares exceed one-third.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): Terminal illness that likely leads to death, where legal actions are treated as bequests.
إجازة (ijāzah): Permission given by heirs for a bequest that exceeds one-third of the estate.

Key Takeaway
In terminal illness, ambiguous manumission is valid but limited to one-third of the estate without heirs' consent, and the intra-Hanafi dispute over the internal slave's share continues.

The Dākhil Slave in Terminal Illness: The Ṣāḥibayn vs. Muhammad al-Shaybānī
Intra-Hanafi dispute on emancipation of an ambiguous slave in terminal illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the emancipation of the dākhil slave, derive the share calculations for each opinion, and identify the underlying principle of the preventer (māniʿ).

Core Idea
The preventer of full freedom for one slave does not apply to another not included in an earlier statement.

This lesson dives into a classic intra-Hanafi debate from ʿUmdat al-Riʿāya. When a master in terminal illness ambiguously declares 'one of you is free' twice among three distinct slaves – the fixed (thābit), the incoming (dākhil), and the outgoing (khārij) – the amount of freedom for the dākhil becomes contested. The Ṣāḥibayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that half of the dākhil is freed, while Imam Muhammad al-Shaybānī insists on only a quarter. Understanding their reasoning will sharpen your ability to analyze how conflicting claims (muzāḥam) affect the distribution of shares in manumission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Three slaves: thābit (always owned), dākhil (entered later), khārij (left later). The master says 'one of you is free' twice. The first statement includes thābit and dākhil (excluding khārij), freeing half of each. The second statement includes all three.
Only the dākhil is disputed; the freed shares for thābit and khārij are agreed (3/4 and 1/2 respectively).
2
State the Positions
Ṣāḥibayn (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf): half of dākhil is freed. Imam Muhammad: only quarter is freed.
Both views are within the Hanafi school; the dispute is about the application of the second statement.
3
Trace the Ṣāḥibayn's Reasoning
The second statement obligates freeing half of both thābit and dākhil. For thābit, only a quarter actually frees because half was already freed by the first statement and the remaining half conflicts with that first half (muzāḥam). For dākhil, no such conflict exists because he was not covered by the first statement, so the second statement's full half applies.
The preventer (māniʿ) of half is specific to thābit.
4
Trace Imam Muhammad's Reasoning
The second statement, when applied to thābit, only frees a quarter due to the conflict. By analogy (qiyās), the same second statement should also free only a quarter of dākhil, because the statement itself has limited effect.
Muhammad sees the second statement's effect as uniform across all included slaves, not individually influenced.
5
Compute the Practical Consequence
According to Ṣāḥibayn: total freed shares = 7 (3/7 thābit, 2/7 dākhil, 2/7 khārij). According to Muhammad: total freed shares = 6 (3/6 thābit, 1/6 dākhil, 2/6 khārij). Each slave works for the remaining unfreed portion for the heirs.
The difference affects the amount each slave must earn to compensate the heirs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بالاتفاق.

أزيد منه.
والجواب عنه من قبلهما : إنّ الإيجاب الثاني يوجب عتق نصف كلّ من الثابت والداخل، وإنما عتق به ربع الثابت ؛ لوجود المزاحم وشيوع هذا النصف في نصفيه ، وقد عتق أحدهما بالإيجاب الأول ولا مزاحم في الداخل ؛ لعدم دخوله في الإيجاب الأول، فيعمل في حقه بما هو مقتضى الإيجاب الثاني، وهو عتق نصفه. [١]قوله : إن المانع ؛ وهو عتق نصفه بالإيجاب الأول، وشيوع نصفه الواجب
عتقه بالإيجاب الثاني في نصفيه. [٢] قوله : وإن قاله ؛ أي إن قال ذلك القول : أي أحدكما حرّ على التفصيل المذكور، حال كون المولى مريضاً بمرض الموت. (۳) قوله : ولم يجز ؛ مضارع معروف من الإجازة، وإنما قيد به لأن العتق في مرض الموتِ في حكم الوصيّة، والوصيّة تنفذ من الثلث من دون توقف على إجازة الورثة، فإن زادت على ثلث مال الموصي فوقف نفاذه على إجازة الورثة ، فإن أجازوا نفذت، وإلا بطل ما زاد على الثلث، وسيأتي تفصيله إن شاء الله في موضعه.
وبه يعلم أن المسألة مفروضة فيما إذا لم تخرج السهام التي حكم بعتقها في الصورة المذكورة ؛ أي ثلاثة أرباع الثابت ونصف الخارج ، وربع الداخل أو نصفه على اختلاف قولين من الثلث، فإنّها إن كانت بقدر ثلث مال المعتق أو أقل منه بأن كان له مال له سوى هذه العبيد أيضاً ، فلا حاجة إلى إجازة الوارث.

٦٣٨
عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية
جُعِل كل عبد سبعة كسهام عتق عندهما ، وعتق من ثَبَتَ تُلْتُه ، ومن كلِّ من غيرِهِ سهمان، وعند محمد الله كل ستة كسهام عتق عنده، وعتق ممن خرج سهمان ،
[۱]
[٢]
وممن ثبت ثلثه ، وممن دخلَ سهم وسعى كل في باقيه على القولين جُعِل كل عبد سبعة كسهام عتق عندهما ، وعتق من ثبت ثلثه ، ومن كلِّ من غيره سهمان، وعند محمد له كل ستة كسهام عتق عنده ، وعتق ممن خرج سهمان ، وممن ثبت ثلثه ، وممن دخل سهم وسعى كل في باقيه على القولين وإلى هذا أشار الشارح له حيث قيّد بقوله : «ولا مال له سوى العبيد الثلاثة»، والحاصل : إنه لو كان له مال آخر بحيث تخرج سهام العتق من الثلاث ولا يطيق الثلاث
فحكم المرض حينئذ كحكم الصحة، وكذا لو زادت على الثلاث وأجازت الورثة. [ 1 ] قوله : جعل كلّ عبد ...الخ ؛ قال الشارح الهروي ه ؛ لأنَّ عندهما ترفع سهام العتق إلى سبعة ؛ ليصير من جنس واحد، وذلك لحاجتنا إلى ثلاثة الأرباع في الثابت، ومخرجه أربعة ؛ لأنه أقل عددٍ يخرج منه الربع، ولكلّ واحدٍ من الخارج والداخل ربعان، فالمجموع سبعة، وهي من جنس واحد ترفعُ من أربعة إلى سبعة، يعني تؤخذ سبعة أرباع من ثلاثة نفر. ثم يعتبر مجموع الثلاثةِ واحداً فيسند الربع إلى المجموع بالسبع، ثم يجعل كل عبد سبعة أسهم ؛ لأنّ قيمتهم متساوية، فتصير سهام قيمة كلّ واحدٍ مساوية لسهام العتق ، ويصير المال ؛ أي العبيد الثلاث أحد وعشرون سهماً ، يعني تصير ثلاثة أمثال سهام العتق ، فتخرج سهام العتق ، وهي سبعة عن الثلاثة. [٢] قوله : كسهام عتق عنده ؛ فإنّ سهام العتق عنده ستة ؛ لأنه يعتق من الداخل عنده سهم واحد لا سهمان.
[٣] قوله : وسعى كل ... الخ ؛ أي سعى كل واحد من العبيد الثلاثة للورثة في باقيه ؛ أي السهم الذي بقي منه رقيقاً على القولين أي قولهما وقول محمد، فعلى قولهما : يسعى الثابت في أربعة أسباع قيمته ، فإنّه عُتِقَ منه ثلاثة أسباعه، ويسعى كلّ من الداخل والخارج في خمسة أسباع قيمته فإنّه عتق من كل واحد منهما سبعان. وعلى قول محمد ه: يسعى الثابتُ في نصف قيمته ؛ لأنَّ سهام عتقه ثلاثة ، وهي نصف الستة، ، ويسعى الخارج في ثلثي قيمته ؛ لأنَّ سهام عتقه اثنان ؛ أي سدسان،
Book of Emancipation: Ambiguous Emancipation. And if he said it while ill and the heir did not permit. 637. And the two (Sahibayn) say: The preventer of emancipating half is specific to the fixed (thabit) slave, and there is no preventer for the incoming (dakhil) slave, so half of him is freed. (And if he said it while ill and the heir did not permit.) Similarly, half of the outgoing (kharij) slave is freed because he is included only in the first statement, and it required emancipation of half of each of the two included in it: i.e., the fixed and the incoming. But the third quarter was added in the fixed due to his inclusion in the second statement, and the outgoing was not covered by the second statement. This is agreed upon. As for the incoming (dakhil), according to Muhammad al-Shaybani, only his quarter is freed because his emancipation is by the second statement, and that statement obligated the emancipation of a quarter of the fixed as we said, so likewise it obligates the emancipation of a quarter of the incoming, not more. The response from the two (Sahibayn) is: The second statement obligates the emancipation of half of both the fixed and the incoming; only a quarter was freed of the fixed because of the existence of a conflicting claim (muzahim) and the distribution of this half over its two halves, and one of them had already been freed by the first statement, and there is no conflicting claim for the incoming because he was not included in the first statement, so what the second statement requires is applied in his case, which is emancipation of half of him. [1] His saying: the preventer is the emancipation of his half by the first statement and the distribution of his half that is obligated by the second statement over its two halves. [2] His saying: and if he said it – i.e., if he said that saying: one of you two is free according to the detailed description, while the master is ill with a mortal illness. (3) His saying: and did not permit – known from permission; it is qualified because emancipation during mortal illness is treated as a bequest, and a bequest is executed from one-third without needing the permission of the heirs; if it exceeds one-third of the testator’s wealth, its execution depends on the heirs’ permission; if they permit, it is executed; otherwise, the excess over one-third is void. Details will come later, God willing. From this it is known that the case is assumed when the shares that are ruled to be emancipated in the mentioned scenario – i.e., three-quarters of the fixed, half of the outgoing, and a quarter or half of the incoming according to the two opinions – do not come out of one-third of the deceased’s estate. If they are equal to or less than one-third of the deceased’s wealth, i.e., if he has other property besides these slaves, then there is no need for the heir’s permission. 638. ʿUmdat al-Riʿāya ʿalā Sharḥ al-Wiqāya. Each slave is made into seven shares of emancipation according to the two (Sahibayn), and a third of the fixed is freed, and from each of the other two slaves two shares are freed. According to Muhammad, each slave is made into six shares of emancipation according to him, and from the outgoing two shares are freed, from the fixed one-third (three shares), and from the incoming one share. And each slave works to earn the rest according to both opinions. The commentator alluded to this when he qualified by saying: “he has no wealth except these three slaves.” The summary: If he had other wealth such that the emancipatory shares come out of the three and do not exceed them, then the ruling of illness is like the ruling of health in that case. Similarly, if they exceed and the heirs permit. [1] His saying: each slave is made into seven shares… The commentator al-Harawi said: because according to them, the emancipatory shares are raised to seven to make them of one kind; we need three-quarters for the fixed, and its denominator is four, and for each of the outgoing and incoming there are two quarters, so the total is seven, which is one kind, raised from four to seven. Then the total of three is considered as one unit and the quarter is attributed to the total as one-seventh. Then each slave is made into seven shares because their values are equal. Thus the value shares of each become equal to the emancipatory shares, and the total wealth (i.e., the three slaves) becomes twenty-one shares. [2] His saying: emancipation shares according to him: because his emancipatory shares are six, since he frees only one share of the incoming, not two. [3] His saying: and each works… i.e., each of the three slaves works for the heirs for the rest, i.e., the share that remains as a slave according to both opinions, i.e., their (Sahibayn) and Muhammad’s. According to them, the fixed works for four-sevenths of his value, since three-sevenths of him are freed; each of the incoming and outgoing works for five-sevenths of his value, since two-sevenths of each are freed. According to Muhammad, the fixed works for half of his value because his emancipatory shares are three, which is half of six; the outgoing works for two-thirds of his value because his emancipatory shares are two, i.e., two sixths.
Source pages p. 637

Commentary
This passage from ʿUmdat al-Riʿāya deals with an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the emancipation of slaves when a master in terminal illness makes an ambiguous statement: 'one of you is free' referring to three slaves: the fixed (thābit – the one who is already owned continuously), the incoming (dākhil – a slave who enters ownership later), and the outgoing (khārij – a slave who leaves ownership). The master says this twice in close succession, resulting in two pronominal statements (ījāb). The first statement covers the fixed and the incoming (since the outgoing is not included), freeing half of each. The second statement is interpreted by the two (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and al-Shaybānī according to the context? Actually here 'the two' and 'Muhammad' indicate an intra-Hanafi split: the two are Abu Yusuf and al-Shaybānī? Wait: the text says 'عند محمد الله' meaning according to Muhammad (al-Shaybānī), and 'وهما' refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf? In Hidayah, 'qāla' is Quduri, 'wa lahu' is Abu Hanifa, 'wa lahuma' is Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. But here 'وهما' likely refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and 'Muhammad' is separate. So it's an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The passage explains that the outgoing slave is agreed: half is freed because he is only in the first statement. The dispute is about the incoming slave. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), half of the incoming is freed because the second statement applies to both fixed and incoming, but the fixed is prevented from getting half due to the first statement's share, while the incoming has no such prevention. According to Imam Muhammad, only a quarter of the incoming is freed because the second statement only frees a quarter of the fixed (due to the conflict), and it analogically frees a quarter of the incoming. The two respond that the conflict (muzāḥam) only exists for the fixed, not the incoming. The passage then explains the mathematical computation of shares: according to the two, each slave is conceptually divided into 7 shares, resulting in 3/7 freed for the fixed, 2/7 for each of the others; according to Muhammad, each slave is divided into 6 shares, freeing 3/6 for the fixed, 2/6 for the outgoing, and 1/6 for the incoming. The slaves then work to earn the remaining value for the heirs. The discussion also clarifies that if the master has additional wealth covering the shares from one-third, the heirs' permission is not needed.

Key Terms
ثابت (thābit): The slave who is fixed in ownership, i.e., already owned at the time of the first statement.
داخل (dākhil): The incoming slave who enters ownership after the first statement.
خارج (khārij): The outgoing slave who is only included in the first statement and not the second.
إجازة الوارث (ijāzat al-wārith): Permission of the heir to allow the emancipation that exceeds one-third of the estate.
مزاحم (muzāḥam): A conflicting claim that prevents full application of a second statement.
مانع (māniʿ): A preventer that blocks the full effect of the second statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, how much of the dākhil slave is freed?
A) One-half
B) One-quarter
C) One-third
D) Three-quarters

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on the dākhil slave hinges on whether the second statement's effect is limited by the presence of a conflicting claim (muzāḥam) only for the thābit or uniformly for all slaves.

6 min
Two Hanafi Methods for Ambiguous Manumission Shares
Intra-Hanafi dispute on computing shares in ambiguous manumission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi methods (companions vs. Muhammad) for calculating manumission shares in ambiguous manumission and apply them to compute sa'y for each slave.

Core Idea
Two valid Hanafi methods exist for dividing manumission shares, both yielding the same one-third freed value but differing in slaves' earnings (sa'y).

This passage addresses a specific scenario: a terminally ill man has three slaves of equal value, no other assets, and ambiguously frees them. The Hanafi school has two valid methods (companions and Muhammad) for calculating the shares of freedom and the required sa'y (earnings) for each slave. Understanding this intra-madhhab dispute shows how Hanafi jurists derive solutions that are both mathematically consistent and legally sound.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the two positions
Identify the facts: three slaves of equal value, no other assets, ambiguous manumission in terminal illness. Note that the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold one view, while Imam Muhammad alone holds another.
Both views are considered valid (yusuq) in the school.
2
Examine the companions' method
Each slave is assigned 7 shares of manumission. The established slave gets 3 shares (3/7), the exiting and entering each get 2 shares (2/7). Total manumission shares = 7, total value shares = 21, so freed value = 7/21 = 1/3.
They raise the denominator from 4 to 7 to handle fractions uniformly.
3
Examine Muhammad's method
Each slave is assigned 6 shares of manumission. The established slave gets 3 shares (3/6 = 1/2), the exiting gets 2 shares (1/3), the entering gets 1 share (1/6). Total manumission shares = 6, total value shares = 18, freed value = 6/18 = 1/3.
Muhammad treats the entering slave differently, giving only one share.
4
Compare the sa'y calculations
Under the companions: established works for 4/7 of his value, exiting and entering each work for 5/7. Under Muhammad: established works for 1/2, exiting works for 2/3, entering works for 5/6.
The sa'y differs per slave even though total freed value is the same.
5
Confirm the legal outcome
Both methods result in one-third of total slave value freed (21 dinars out of 63) and two-thirds (42 dinars) belonging to the heirs. Thus both methods are valid and yield the same ultimate distribution.
The practical difference lies in the amount each slave must earn for the heirs.

جُعِل كل عبد سبعة كسهام عتق عندهما ، وعتق من ثَبَتَ ثُلْتُه ، ومن كلِّ من غيرِهِ سهمان، وعند محمد جُعِل كل ستة كسهام عتق عنده، وعتق ممن خرج سهمان ، وممن ثبت ثلثه ، وممن دخل سهم وسعى كل في باقيه على القولين. وإلى هذا أشار الشارح له حيث قيّد بقوله : «ولا مال له سوى العبيد الثلاثة»، والحاصل : إنه لو كان له مال آخر بحيث تخرج سهام العتق من الثلاث ولا يطيق الثلاث فحكم المرض حينئذ كحكم الصحة، وكذا لو زادت على الثلاث وأجازت الورثة. [ 1 ] قوله : جعل كلّ عبد ...الخ ؛ قال الشارح الهروي : لأنَّ عندهما ترفع سهام العتق إلى سبعة ؛ ليصير من جنس واحد، وذلك لحاجتنا إلى ثلاثة الأرباع في الثابت، ومخرجه أربعة ؛ لأنه أقل عددٍ يخرج منه الربع، ولكلّ واحدٍ من الخارج والداخل ربعان، فالمجموع سبعة، وهي من جنس واحد ترفعُ من أربعة إلى سبعة، يعني تؤخذ سبعة أرباع من ثلاثة نفر. ثم يعتبر مجموع الثلاثةِ واحداً فيسند الربع إلى المجموع بالسبع، ثم يجعل كل عبد سبعة أسهم ؛ لأنّ قيمتهم متساوية، فتصير سهام قيمة كلّ واحدٍ مساوية لسهام العتق ، ويصير المال ؛ أي العبيد الثلاث أحد وعشرون سهماً ، يعني تصير ثلاثة أمثال سهام العتق ، فتخرج سهام العتق ، وهي سبعة عن الثلاثة. [٢] قوله : كسهام عتق عنده ؛ فإنّ سهام العتق عنده ستة ؛ لأنه يعتق من الداخل عنده سهم واحد لا سهمان. [٣] قوله : وسعى كل ... الخ ؛ أي سعى كل واحد من العبيد الثلاثة للورثة في باقيه ؛ أي السهم الذي بقي منه رقيقاً على القولين أي قولهما وقول محمد، فعلى قولهما : يسعى الثابت في أربعة أسباع قيمته ، فإنّه عُتِقَ منه ثلاثة أسباعه، ويسعى كلّ من الداخل والخارج في خمسة أسباع قيمته فإنّه عتق من كل واحد منهما سبعان. وعلى قول محمد : يسعى الثابتُ في نصف قيمته ؛ لأنَّ سهام عتقه ثلاثة ، وهي نصف الستة، ويسعى الخارج في ثلثي قيمته ؛ لأنَّ سهام عتقه اثنان ؛ أي سدسان، وهو ثلث ستة، ويسعى الداخل في خمسة أسداس قيمته ؛ لأنّه عتق منه سهم واحد، وهو السدس. كذا في «شرح الفصيح الهروي».

[1]قوله : ويصح ؛ قال الهروي : أي يصح الثلث، وهو سهام العتق الخارج من ثلث ماله بالوصيّة، والثلثان وهما سهامُ الورثة على القولين ، فإنه إذا كانت قيمة كلّ عبد إحدى وعشرين ديناراً مثلاً يعتق من الثابت ثلاثة أسباعه ، وهي : تسعة دنانير ويسعى في أربعة أسباعه وهي اثنا عشر. ومن الخارج يعتق السبعان ، الستة ، وهي ويسعى في خمسة أسباعه ، وهي خمسة عشر، وكذلك من الداخل ، فسهامُ العتق أحد وعشرون، وسهام السعي اثنان وأربعون، فيصح الثلث والثلثان على قولهما. وأما على قول محمد : يعتق من الثابت نصفه ، وهو عشرة ونصف من واحد ، ويسعى في نصفه، ويعتق من الخارج ثلثه وهو سبعة، ويسعى في ثلثيه وهو أربعة عشر، ويعتق من الداخل سدسه، وهو ثلاثة ونصف، ويسعى في خمسة أسداسه ، وهي سبعة عشر ونصف فسهام العتق أحد وعشرون وسهام السعي اثنان وأربعون ، فيصح الثلث والثلثان على قوله أيضاً. انتهى. (٢) قوله : في مرض الموت ؛ أشار به إلى أن المراد بالمرض هو المرض الذي مات به، وهو الذي لا تنقذ وصاياه فيه إلا في الثلث، وأما المرض الذي صح منه ولم يمت فحكمه كحكم الصحة. [٣] قوله : وقيمتهم مساوية ؛ هذا القيد ليس بلازم، فإنه لو اختلفت قيمتهم فالحكم لا يختلف وإنما اعتبر التساوي لكون الحساب سهلاً متيسراً حينئذ. (٤) قوله : لأن مخرج الكسور أربعة ؛ المخرج أقل عددٍ يمكن أن يؤخذ منه كلّ فردٍ
Each slave is made seven shares of manumission according to them (the two companions), and freed is the one whose third is established, and from each other two shares. And according to Muhammad, each slave is made six shares of manumission according to him, and freed is the one who goes out with two shares, and the one whose third is established, and the one who enters with one share, and each works for the heirs for his remainder according to the two opinions. The commentator indicated this where he restricted by saying: 'And he has no wealth besides the three slaves.' The summary: if he had other wealth such that the shares of manumission could be taken from the three and they do not exceed one-third, then the ruling of illness is like health; likewise if it exceeded one-third and the heirs consented. [1] His saying: 'Each slave is made...' The commentator al-Harawi said: Because according to them, the shares of manumission are raised to seven to become of one type. That is because we need three-quarters for the established one, and its denominator is four, as it is the smallest number from which a quarter can be taken. For each of the exiting and entering, there are two quarters, so the total is seven, which are of one type, raised from four to seven, meaning seven quarters are taken from three persons. Then the total of the three is considered as one, so the quarter is attributed to the total as a seventh. Then each slave is made seven shares because their values are equal, so the value shares of each become equal to the manumission shares, and the wealth (i.e., the three slaves) becomes twenty-one shares, meaning three times the manumission shares, so the manumission shares (which are seven) come from the three. [2] His saying: 'As shares of manumission according to him' – because the shares of manumission according to him are six, since he frees from the entering one share, not two. [3] His saying: 'And each works...' – meaning each of the three slaves works for the heirs for his remainder, i.e., the share that remains as property, according to the two opinions, i.e., their opinion and Muhammad's opinion. According to their opinion: the established one works for four-sevenths of his value, for three-sevenths of him have been freed; and each of the entering and exiting works for five-sevenths of his value, for two-sevenths of each have been freed. According to Muhammad's opinion: the established one works for half his value, because his manumission shares are three, which is half of six; and the exiting works for two-thirds of his value, because his manumission shares are two, i.e., two sixths, which is one-third of six; and the entering works for five-sixths of his value, because from him one share (one-sixth) has been freed. Thus in Sharh al-Fasih al-Harawi. [1] His saying: 'And it is valid'; al-Harawi said: meaning the one-third is valid, which is the shares of manumission coming from one-third of his wealth by will, and the two-thirds are the shares of the heirs according to the two opinions. For example, if the value of each slave is twenty-one dinars, then from the established one three-sevenths are freed, which is nine dinars, and he works for four-sevenths, which is twelve dinars. From the exiting, two-sevenths are freed, which is six dinars, and he works for five-sevenths, which is fifteen dinars. Likewise from the entering. So the manumission shares are twenty-one, and the working shares are forty-two. Thus the one-third and two-thirds are valid according to their opinion. As for Muhammad's opinion: from the established one half is freed, which is ten and a half; he works for half. From the exiting, one-third is freed, which is seven; he works for two-thirds, which is fourteen. From the entering, one-sixth is freed, which is three and a half; he works for five-sixths, which is seventeen and a half. So the manumission shares are twenty-one and the working shares are forty-two. Thus the one-third and two-thirds are valid according to his opinion also. End. (2) His saying: 'In fatal illness' – he indicated that what is meant by illness is the illness from which he died, and that is the one in which his bequests are not executed except within one-third. As for the illness from which he recovered and did not die, its ruling is like health. [3] His saying: 'And their values are equal' – this condition is not necessary; if their values differ, the ruling does not differ. Equality is assumed only for ease of calculation. (4) His saying: 'Because the denominator of fractions is four' – the denominator is the smallest number from which each individual can be taken.
Source pages p. 638

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute explanation concerning the calculation of shares when a man dying of illness says something ambiguous about freeing his three slaves, with no other assets, and the heirs do not consent. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and Imam Muhammad have two methods. The passage first states the two views: according to the companions, each slave is made 7 shares of manumission (total 21 shares for 3 slaves), while according to Muhammad, each slave is made 6 shares (total 18 shares). The commentator then explains the reasoning: the companions need to represent three-quarters (for the slave whose freedom is established) and two quarters (for each of the other two) making a total of seven quarters, so they raise the denominator from 4 to 7. Then they assign 7 shares per slave so that the total value shares (21) equal three times the manumission shares (7). Muhammad, however, uses 6 shares per slave because he sees the entering slave receiving only one share (one-sixth) rather than two shares (two-sevenths). The passage then details the 'earning' (sa'y) that each slave must do for the heirs for the portion that remains property. Practical examples with values confirm that in both methods the total manumitted value equals one-third of the total slave value and the heirs receive two-thirds. The commentator also clarifies that the equality of values is not essential, and that the condition of 'no other wealth' is crucial for this calculation to apply.

Key Terms
سهام العتق (siḥām al-ʿitq): The shares representing the portion of each slave that becomes free; in this context, each slave is assigned a number of shares (7 under the companions, 6 under Muhammad) and the freed portion corresponds to the shares of manumission allocated.
السعي (al-saʿy): The portion of a slave's value that he must earn (work) for the heirs after being partially freed, corresponding to the share that remains in ownership of the heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario of three slaves of equal value with no other assets, according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), how many shares of manumission are there in total?
A) 6 shares
B) 7 shares
C) 21 shares
D) 18 shares

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows multiple valid computational methods for distributing manumission shares, as long as the underlying legal principle (one-third freed) is preserved.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on 'Awl in Manumission of Three Slaves
Calculating manumission shares of three slaves using 'awl with two Hanafi views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the manumission shares of three slaves using 'awl and distinguish the positions of the two companions (Sahibayn) and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
When shares exceed the base, 'awl reduces each proportionally; Hanafis differ on the internal slave's share, affecting the denominator.

This passage examines a specific case where a master declares 'one of my three slaves is free' without specification. Since the master owns only these slaves of equal value, each slave represents one-third of the wealth. The calculation involves assigning fractional shares to each slave's manumission, but the total exceeds the whole, necessitating 'awl. Within the Hanafi school, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani jointly) and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani individually differ on the share of the internal slave, leading to different base denominators and final distributions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three slaves and their shares
The fixed slave (the one referred to) gets a share of manumission; the external and internal slaves also get shares. According to the Sahibayn: fixed 3/4, external 1/2, internal 1/2. According to Muhammad: fixed 3/4, external 1/2, internal 1/4.
The shares reflect the master's statement's ambiguity: the fixed slave is certainly a slave, so he gets the largest share.
2
Sum the shares and determine the need for 'awl
Add the fractions: Sahibayn: 3/4 + 1/2 + 1/2 = 7/4. This exceeds 1, so the denominator 4 is increased to 7. Muhammad: 3/4 + 1/2 + 1/4 = 6/4, denominator increases to 6.
'Awl increases the denominator proportionally so that the sum of shares equals 1 after reduction.
3
Apply 'awl to distribute the shares
Under Sahibayn: each slave's share is now a fraction of 7. Under Muhammad: fraction of 6. Determine what fraction of each slave is freed and what fraction they must pay for their remaining freedom (sai'ah).
For example, under Sahibayn, the fixed slave: freed 3/7, pays 4/7.
4
Contrast the practical outcomes
For the internal slave: Sahibayn: freed 2/7, pays 5/7. Muhammad: freed 1/6, pays 5/6. The fixed slave: Sahibayn: freed 3/7, pays 4/7. Muhammad: freed 1/2, pays 1/2.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the amount each slave must pay to earn their freedom.

So according to both of them, the shares of manumission are made seven, and they are one third of the wealth, as a whole number from fractions: the denominator of half is two, the denominator of a quarter is four, and the denominator of a seventh is seven. And analogize to similar cases. [1] His statement: By way of 'awl; 'awl linguistically is used in the sense of injustice and inclination towards it. It is said: so-and-so 'awala against me, meaning he inclined unjustly. And in the sense of overcoming: it is said 'ayila sabruhu, meaning it was overcome. And in the sense of raising: it is said 'aala al-mizan if he raised it. As for its technical meaning in Sacred Law: it is that something of its parts is added to the denominator, like a sixth or a third or other fractions, when the denominator is insufficient to cover the shares. Its summary: when the denominator is insufficient to fulfill the collected shares, the sum is raised to a number greater than that denominator, then divided so that the deficiency enters into the shares of all heirs in one proportion. Thus in 'al-Fara'id al-Sharifiyyah'. If you know this, then know that the shares of manumission according to both of them were seven quarters: three quarters from the fixed one, and two quarters from each of the external and internal. And it is known that the denominator of a quarter is four, so the case undergoes 'awl from four to seven due to the denominator's insufficiency to fulfill the mentioned shares, for four only suffices for four quarters. And according to Muhammad: when the shares of manumission were six quarters: three quarters from the fixed, two quarters from the external, and one quarter from the internal, the case undergoes 'awl from four to six. [2] His statement: one third of the wealth, etc., because it is assumed that he has no wealth besides the three slaves and their values are equal, so one slave is one third of the wealth. So each slave is made seven shares, since the shares of manumission are seven, and taken from the total. (1) 'Awl: it is an increase in the number of shares and a decrease in their amount. See al-Tanwir (6:786) and Masa'il min al-Fiqh al-Muqaran (p. 60). (2) In simplified arithmetic: 3/4 + 1/2 + 1/2 = 7/4. (3) In simplified arithmetic: 3/4 + 1/2 + 1/4 = 6/4. [Page 641] Book of Manumission: Indeterminate Manumission. [2] And each slave is made seven, because the value of each slave equals one third of the wealth. So from the external, two sevenths are freed, which is two, and from the fixed, three are freed, which is three sevenths of him, and he must work for four sevenths of his value. According to Muhammad, the shares of manumission are made six shares, which is one third of the wealth. So each slave is made six. So from the external, two are freed, which is one third of six, and he must work for two thirds of his value. And he must work for five sevenths of his value, and similarly the internal. And from the fixed, three are freed, and he is half of six, and he must work for half, and from the internal, one, which is a sixth, and he must work for five sixths of his value. [1] His statement: equals, because the one slave is one third of three, and the values of the three are equal, so the value of each slave equals one third of the wealth. He mentioned it. [2] His statement: so it is freed, etc., an explanation of the division of seven upon the three slaves according to what has passed. [3] His statement: and it is two sevenths, because the amount that is freed from him, although it is half (two out of four), when the case became seven by way of 'awl, the two out of seven are two sevenths, so what is freed from him is to the extent of two sevenths, and he is obliged to work for five sevenths of his value. And analogize to the internal. [4] His statement: and it is three sevenths of him, because the case undergoes 'awl from four to seven, and it is known that three relative to four is three quarters, and relative to seven is three sevenths, for when the reference increases, the relative decreases. [0] His statement: one third of the wealth, because according to him, the manumission shares are six: three quarters from the fixed, half from the external, which is two quarters or a quarter from the internal. [6] His statement: two; and it, although relative to four is half, or if you will say two quarters, but relative to six which the case underwent 'awl to, it is two sixths, or if you will, one third of six, for the sixth is half of one third, and the sum of the two sixths is one third. [7] His statement: half of six; or if you will, three sixths of six.
Source pages p. 640

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani himself, concerning the application of 'awl (proportional increase of the denominator) in manumission shares when a master owns three slaves of equal value and says 'one of you is free' without specifying which. The commentary first defines 'awl linguistically and technically, then applies it to the case. According to the two companions, the shares of manumission are 3/4 (from the fixed slave who is certainly a slave) + 1/2 + 1/2 = 7/4, so the base denominator of 4 is increased to 7 ('awl). Each slave is assigned 7 shares, and the distribution is explained: from the external slave, 2/7 is free (he works for 5/7), from the fixed slave, 3/7 is free (works for 4/7), etc. According to Muhammad, the shares are 3/4 + 1/2 + 1/4 = 6/4, so the base 4 becomes 6. Each slave gets 6 shares, with the external slave freed to 1/3 (works 2/3), the fixed slave freed to 1/2 (works 1/2), and the internal slave freed to 1/6 (works 5/6). The key difference lies in the share assigned to the internal slave: the companions give him a one-half share, while Muhammad gives him one-quarter. This affects the final distribution. The passage emphasizes that 'awl ensures proportional loss to all slaves. The commentary also notes that the values are equal so each slave is 1/3 of the total wealth.

Key Terms
العول (al-‘awl): In this passage: increasing the base denominator (makhraj) from 4 to 7 or 6 to accommodate the sum of shares (7/4 or 6/4) that exceeds the original denominator, resulting in proportional reduction of each share.
سهام العتق (siham al-‘itq): The fractional shares of manumission allocated to each slave, representing the portion of each slave that becomes free.
مخرج (makhraj): The denominator of a fraction; in this passage, the base number (4) used as the starting point for division before ‘awl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad's view, what fraction of the external slave is freed?
A) 1/2
B) 1/3
C) 2/7
D) 1/6

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school applies 'awl to proportionally reduce shares when the sum of fractions exceeds the whole; intra-school disagreement on the internal slave's share changes the base from 7 to 6.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Share Calculation in Ambiguous Emancipation
Explaining the dispute between Abu Hanifa/Yusuf and Muhammad on dividing emancipation shares

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi methods for dividing emancipation shares in ambiguous emancipation and calculate the freed and saya amounts for each slave under both methods.

Core Idea
Two valid Hanafi methods: base 7 (Abu Hanifa/Yusuf) vs base 6 (Muhammad) for dividing emancipation shares in ambiguous bequests.

In ambiguous emancipation (ʿitq al-mubham), when a testator frees a portion of his property without specifying which slave, the Hanafi school has two transmitted methods for distributing the freedom shares among the slaves. This lesson unpacks the calculation logic of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, using the principle of ʿawl (increase) to determine the freed fraction and the required saya for each slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem and the two positions
We have three slaves of equal value. The testator frees one-third of his property (i.e., one slave's worth, but ambiguous which). The Hanafi school has two methods: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf use a base of 7 shares per slave; Muhammad uses a base of 6 shares per slave. Understand why these bases arise: the base 7 comes from ʿawl: originally 4 shares, increased to 7; Muhammad directly uses the total shares as 6 (since one-third of property freed, and with three slaves, each gets 2 shares of emancipation).
The base 7 arises because the emancipation shares are originally from a base of 4 (fractions 1/2 + 1/4 + 1/4?), and ʿawl increases to 7. Muhammad's base 6 comes from considering the actual share of emancipation: one-third of property among three slaves yields 2 shares each, total 6.
2
Understand the fractions freed for external, internal, and fixed slaves
Under each method, the fractions freed differ. For Abu Hanifa/Yusuf: external and internal have 2/7 freed, fixed has 3/7 freed. For Muhammad: external and internal have 1/3 freed, fixed has 1/6 freed. Work through why these fractions result from the base: for Abu Hanifa/Yusuf, the freed portion from external is originally half of the base 4 (2 shares), but after ʿawl to 7, it's 2/7; the fixed originally gets 3/4 of the base (3 shares) becoming 3/7. For Muhammad, the shares are 6 total, so external gets 2/6 = 1/3, fixed gets 1/6.
The fractions reflect the ratio of the original fixed shares to the new base after ʿawl or direct assignment.
3
Apply to a numerical example with 42 dirhams per slave
The passage provides an example: each slave worth 42 dirhams, total property 126 dirhams. Under Abu Hanifa/Yusuf: external freed 12 dirhams (2/7 of 42), saya 30 dirhams; internal same; fixed freed 18 dirhams (3/7), saya 24 dirhams. Under Muhammad: external freed 14 dirhams (1/3 of 42), saya 28 dirhams; internal same; fixed freed 7 dirhams (1/6 of 42), saya 35 dirhams.
From the passage, under Muhammad, the external freed is explicitly stated as 14; we infer the internal and fixed similarly.
4
Compare the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference in base numbers leads to different freed fractions: under Abu Hanifa/Yusuf, external and internal slaves have 2/7 freed (approx 28.6%), while under Muhammad they have 1/3 freed (33.3%). The fixed slave has 3/7 freed (42.9%) under the first method, but only 1/6 freed (16.7%) under Muhammad. This affects the saya amount and thus the economic burden on each slave.
The method chosen can significantly impact the slave's financial obligation. The text does not prefer one method, presenting both as valid Zahir al-Riwayah transmissions.

yؤكل.

Book of Emancipation: Ambiguous Emancipation. [2] And he makes every slave seven (shares) because the value of every slave equals one third of the property. So from the external (slave) two sevenths are freed, two (shares), and from the fixed (slave) three are freed, that is three sevenths, and he must work (saya) for four sevenths of his value. According to Muhammad, he makes the shares of emancipation, which are six shares, one third of the property, so every slave is made six (shares). So from the external two (shares) are freed, which is one third of six, and he works for two thirds of his value. And he works for five sevenths of his value. Likewise the internal. And from half of six? And he works for half, and from the internal one, the fixed three, which is one sixth, and he works for five sixths of his value. [1] His saying: 'equals'; because one slave is three [?], and the values of the three are equal, so the value of each slave is equal to one third of the property. Mentioned. [2] His saying: 'then is freed...etc.'; explanation of the division of seven among the three slaves according to what has passed, and it is [3] His saying: 'it is two sevenths'; because the amount that is freed from him, although it is half (two out of four), but when the problem becomes seven by means of 'awl, two out of seven are two sevenths, so the freed portion from him is two sevenths, and he must perform saya for five sevenths. And apply the same to the internal. [4] His saying: 'which is three sevenths'; because the problem is increased from four to seven, and it is known that three relative to four is three quarters, and relative to seven is three sevenths, because when the denominator increases, the ratio decreases. [0] His saying: 'one third of the property'; because in his view the shares of emancipation are six, three quarters from the fixed, and half from the external, which is two quarters or one quarter from the internal. [6] His saying: 'two'; although it is half relative to four, or if you wish two quarters, but relative to six to which the problem has increased, it is two sixths, or if you wish one third of six, for a sixth is half of a third, and the total of the two sixths is one third. [7] His saying: 'half of six'; or if you wish three sixths of six. Then if the value of each slave were forty-two dirhams, which is one third, so all the property is one hundred twenty-six. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), from the external two sevenths are freed: twelve (dirhams), and he works for five sevenths which is thirty (dirhams). Likewise the internal. And from the fixed three sevenths are freed, which is eighteen, and he works for four sevenths, which is twenty-four. According to Muhammad, from the external of forty-two its third is freed, which is fourteen. [1] His saying: 'if it were...etc.'; beginning to illustrate the problem by way of example, after mentioning its proof and related matters. [2] His saying: 'so all the property...etc.'; because it is assumed that he has no property except the three slaves, and the value of each is equal, if the value of each is forty-two dirhams, which is one third of the property, then the total value of the three is one hundred twenty-six, obtained by multiplying forty-two by three, which is all the property. And by this it becomes clear to you that 'all' in the commentator's saying 'so all the property' is a collective all, not an individual all. How not, when they have stated that 'all' when it enters upon an indefinite noun applies to every individual of its members, and when it enters upon a definite noun it applies to all its parts. Hence they said that the statement 'every pomegranate is edible' is true, meaning every individual of its members is edible, but the statement 'all the pomegranate is edible' is false, meaning all its parts are edible. [3] His saying: 'likewise the internal'; because the amount of emancipation from them according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is one, and it is four, and after 'awl it becomes two out of seven, which are two sevenths relative to it. Two out of... And it is known that one seventh of forty-two which is the value of each slave is six, and its two sevenths are twelve. So from the internal and from the external each has seven freed, meaning the amount of twelve dirhams, and they must work for five sevenths of each, which is the amount of thirty dirhams each. [4] His saying: 'three sevenths'; because the freed portion from him is three out of four, and after 'awl to seven it becomes three sevenths, so an amount of eighteen dirhams is freed, and he must work for the remainder, which is four sevenths. [0] His saying: 'its third'; because the freed portion from him is two out of four, and after 'awl from six, because the total shares of emancipation in his view are six as mentioned earlier, and the ratio of two to six is one third.
Source pages p. 641

Commentary
This passage addresses the intra-Hanafi dispute on calculating emancipation shares in ambiguous emancipation (ʿitq al-mubham) when three slaves of equal value are involved. The core issue is how to distribute the freed portion when the testator frees a part of his property (here one-third) without specifying individual slaves. The commentator explains two methods: one from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and another from Muhammad al-Shaybani. The method of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf sets the base as 7 shares per slave, because the original shares (4) are increased (ʿawl) to 7. From the external slave, 2/7 are freed (saya required for 5/7), from the internal similarly, and from the fixed slave 3/7 are freed (saya for 4/7). Muhammad sets the base as 6 shares per slave, reflecting that the shares of emancipation are considered 6. From the external slave, 1/3 is freed (saya for 2/3), from the internal similarly, and from the fixed slave 1/6 is freed (saya for 5/6). The commentary then provides a concrete numerical example: each slave worth 42 dirhams (total 126). Under Abu Hanifa/Yusuf: external freed 12, saya 30; internal same; fixed freed 18, saya 24. Under Muhammad: external freed 14, saya 28 (since 2/3 of 42 = 28). The passage also clarifies linguistic points about the word 'all' (al-kull) in the phrase 'all the property', noting it means collective totality, not individual. The dispute is purely within the Hanafi school, both positions being valid transmissions, but the text does not explicitly prefer one.

Key Terms
العتق المبهم (al-ʿitq al-mubham): Emancipation where the testator does not specify which slave is to be freed, e.g., 'free one of my slaves'.
العول (al-ʿawl): The increase in the base denominator of shares (e.g., from 4 to 7) when the total prescribed shares exceed the base, common in faraid but applied here to emancipation shares.
السعاية (al-saʿāyah): The work or payment required from a partially freed slave to earn the remaining value of his freedom.
الثابت (al-thābit): The slave whose emancipation is fixed in the original bequest (the 'fixed' one, as opposed to the external and internal which are ambiguous).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in the method of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what fraction of the external slave's value is freed?
A) 1/3
B) 2/7
C) 3/7
D) 1/6

Key Takeaway
In ambiguous emancipation, the Hanafi school has two transmitted methods for calculating shares; both are valid, and the choice affects the freed fraction for each slave.

Calculating Shares in Ambiguous Manumission: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Commentary on calculating freedom shares in ambiguous manumission with analogy to divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the freedom and working shares for slaves in an ambiguous manumission under both Hanafi views and explain the role of 'awl'.

Core Idea
When a master says 'one-third of my slaves is free,' the freedom is distributed proportionally using 'awl,' not equally.

This passage dives into a practical example of ambiguous manumission, where a master declares that 'one-third of my slaves' is free without specifying which slave. The commentator works through the calculation with three slaves of equal value, revealing a subtle intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) on one side, and a solitary transmission from Muhammad on the other. Understanding this calculation is crucial for correctly apportioning the slaves' freedom and their obligation to work (sa‘ayah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and values
Three slaves each valued at 42 dirhams. Master says 'one-third of my slaves is free.' Total wealth = 126 dirhams.
Assume no other assets.
2
Determine initial shares based on number of slaves
Since there are three slaves, each initially represents one-third of the total. But the master's statement is ambiguous: it applies to the group, not each individual.
This is where the dispute begins.
3
Apply 'awl' to adjust fractions (majority view)
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: initial shares are 1/4, 1/4, 1/2 (based on number of slaves in each utterance? Actually the commentary says external and internal each get 2/7, fixed gets 3/7. This comes from an initial distribution of 1/4, 1/4, 1/2 which is then adjusted by 'awl' to common denominator 7.
'Awl' ensures the total freed fraction equals one-third of total value.
4
Convert fractions to dirhams
For each slave, multiply their fraction by 42 dirhams. External and internal: 2/7 × 42 = 12 dirhams freed, must work for 30 dirhams. Fixed: 3/7 × 42 = 18 dirhams freed, works for 24 dirhams.
The sum of freed values is 12+12+18 = 42, which is one-third of 126.
5
Compare with Muhammad's alternative view
Muhammad alone: external gets 1/3 of 42 = 14 dirhams freed, internal 1/6 = 7, fixed 1/2 = 21. Total freed = 42 dirhams. But this distribution is not proportional to the number of slaves involved in each utterance.
The mufta bihi view is the majority position.
6
Note the analogy to divorce
The same fractional logic applies to ambiguous divorce with multiple wives, affecting mahr reduction. For example, 'one of you is divorced' followed by another ambiguous statement leads to shares like 1/4, 3/8, 1/8 for the wives.
This illustrates the broader principle of handling ambiguity in legal utterances.

[٣]قوله: وكذلك الداخل؛ فإن مقدار العتق منهما عندهما واحد، وهوا أربعة، وبعد العول اثنان من سبعة، وهما سبعان بالنسبة إليه. ومن المعلوم: أن سبعه اثنين وأربعين الذي هو قيمة كل عبد ستة، وسبعاه اثنا عشر، فيعتق من الداخل ومن الخارج سبعاً كل منهما؛ أي مقدار اثني عشر درهماً، ويجب عليهما أن يسعيا في خمسة أسباعهما، وهو مقدار ثلثين ثلثين درهماً. [0]قوله: وثمن من دخلت؛ قال أبو القاسم أحمد بن محمد العتابي في شرحه لكتاب «الزيادات» لمحمد: هاهنا حكمان: حكم المهر، وحكم الميراث. أما حكم المهر فللخارجة ثلاثة أرباع المهر؛ لأن بالإيجاب الأول يسقط نصف الصداق بين الخارجة والثابتة، فيسقط من مهر الخارجة الربع ويبقى ثلاثة أرباع المهر، (1) أي مات بلا بيان ففي المسألة أحكام ثلاثة: المهر والميراث والعدة أما حكم الميراث فللداخلة نصف والنصف بين الخارجة والثابتة نصف وعلى كل منهن عدة الوفاة احتياطاً. ينظر: «مجمع الأنهر» (١: ٥٢٣)
If the value of each slave is forty-two dirhams, which is one-third, then all the wealth is one hundred twenty-six. According to both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), from the 'external' slave, two-sevenths are freed, i.e., twelve, and he works for five-sevenths, which is thirty; similarly for the 'internal' slave; and from the 'fixed' slave, three-sevenths are freed, i.e., eighteen, and he works for four-sevenths, i.e., twenty-four. According to Muhammad, from the 'external' slave, one-third of forty-two is freed, i.e., fourteen. [1] His statement: 'if it were...etc.' is a start in depicting the question by way of example, after mentioning its proof and related matters. [2] His statement: 'all the wealth...etc.' means that it is assumed he has no wealth except these three slaves, and that each is of equal value, so the total is one hundred twenty-six, being the product of multiplying forty-two by three, and that is all the wealth. From this it is clear that 'all' in the commentator's phrase means the collective whole, not each individual. [3] His statement: 'similarly for the internal' means the amount of freedom from both according to them is one, and it is four, and after adjustment (awl) it becomes two out of seven, i.e., two-sevenths. It is known that one-seventh of forty-two (the value of each slave) is six, and two-sevenths is twelve, so from the internal and external each, two-sevenths are freed, i.e., twelve dirhams, and they must work for five-sevenths of their value, i.e., thirty dirhams. [4] His statement: 'three-sevenths' because what is freed from it is three out of four, and after adjustment to seven it becomes three-sevenths, so eighteen dirhams are freed, and he must work for the remaining four-sevenths. [0] His statement: 'one-third of it' because what is freed from it is two out of four, and after adjustment from six (since the total shares of freedom according to him are six, and the ratio of two to six is one-third). And if he divorces similarly before intercourse, one-fourth of the dowry of the one who left falls, three-eighths of the one who stayed, and one-eighth of the one who entered. And from the fixed one, half of it, i.e., twenty-one; from the internal one, one-sixth, i.e., seven. So the total shares of freedom according to the two views are forty-two, which is one-third of the wealth, and the shares of working (sa'aya) are eighty-four, which is two-thirds of the wealth. (And if he divorces similarly before intercourse) one-fourth of the dowry of the one who left falls, three-eighths of the one who stayed, and one-eighth of the one who entered. (5): (1) Then from the external slave, the amount freed is one-third of forty-two, i.e., fourteen, because one-sixth is seven, and one-third is twice one-sixth. He must work for the remainder, i.e., two-thirds, i.e., twenty-eight. [1] His statement: 'half of it' because what is freed from it is three out of four, and after adjustment from six, so the freed amount is twenty-one dirhams, and he must work for the remaining half. [2] His statement: 'one-sixth' because what is freed from it is one share, i.e., one-sixth relative to six, so the freed amount is seven dirhams, and he must work for five-sixths of his value, i.e., thirty-five dirhams. [3] His statement: 'and the shares of the working' i.e., the shares in which the three slaves work for the heirs. [4] His statement: 'similarly' means that he said, addressing his two wives, 'one of you is divorced,' and one of them left and a third entered, then he said, addressing the first (the fixed) and the third (the entering), 'one of you is divorced,' and he did not clarify what he meant by his ambiguity in the two utterances. [0] His statement: 'and one-eighth of the one who entered' – Abu al-Qasim Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-‘Attabi said in his commentary on the book 'al-Ziyadat' by Muhammad: Here are two rulings: the ruling of dowry and the ruling of inheritance. As for the ruling of dowry: for the one who left, three-fourths of the dowry, because by the first utterance, half of the dowry is dropped between the one who left and the fixed one, so one-fourth of her dowry falls and three-fourths remain. (1) i.e., he died without clarification, so there are three rulings: dowry, inheritance, and waiting period. As for inheritance: the entering one gets half, and half between the one who left and the fixed one; each of them must observe a waiting period for death (iddat al-wafat) as a precaution. See 'Majma' al-Anhur' (1:523).
Source pages p. 642

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling about ambiguous manumission (al-‘itq al-mubham). The author uses an example with three slaves of equal value (42 dirhams each, total 126). The master says 'one-third of my slaves is free' without specifying which. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani), the freedom is distributed proportionally: the 'external' and 'internal' slaves each have two-sevenths freed (because initially they each had one-quarter but via 'awl' the shares rise to two-sevenths each), while the 'fixed' slave has three-sevenths freed (initial three-quarters adjusted to three-sevenths). According to Muhammad alone (in a different transmission), the 'external' slave gets one-third freed (i.e., 14 dirhams worth). The commentary then explains each step, including the linguistic point that 'all the wealth' means the collective total. The passage then analogizes to divorce: if a man ambiguously divorces one of his wives, and then another similar ambiguous divorce involving a third wife, the mahr (dower) is reduced proportionally: the wife who 'left' loses one-quarter, the 'fixed' loses three-eighths, and the 'entering' loses one-eighth. The same fractional logic applies. Finally, the commentary quotes al-‘Attabi regarding the combined rulings of mahr and inheritance when the husband dies without clarification.

Key Terms
العتق المبهم (al-‘itq al-mubham): Manumission that is ambiguous, such as 'one of my slaves is free' without specification.
السعاية (al-sa‘ayah): The work or earning that a partially freed slave must do to pay the remaining value to the master's heirs.
العول (al-‘awl): Proportional reduction of shares when the total of fractions exceeds unity, used here to adjust freedom shares.
الإبهام (al-ibham): Ambiguity or lack of specification in a legal utterance, e.g., 'one of you is free' or 'one of you is divorced.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example with three slaves of equal value (42 dirhams each), what is the freedom share (in dirhams) for the 'external' slave according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?
A) 14 dirhams
B) 12 dirhams
C) 18 dirhams
D) 21 dirhams

Key Takeaway
In ambiguous manumission, freedom is distributed proportionally using 'awl' to ensure the total freed value matches the stated fraction.

Clarification of Ambiguous Manumission Through Subsequent Actions
Explains how actions indicating ownership resolve ambiguous manumission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which actions clarify ambiguous manumission and explain the legal reasoning based on ownership indicators.

Core Idea
Actions that show continued ownership clarify that the other slave is freed; intercourse does not.

When a master says 'one of you is free' without specifying, ambiguity arises. The Hanafi school resolves this ambiguity by looking at the master's later actions. Actions that presuppose ownership of a particular slave indicate that the other was the intended one. This lesson examines which actions qualify and why.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous statement
The master declares 'one of you is free' to two slaves. We need to determine which one becomes free.
Ambiguity can also occur in divorce (one of you is divorced).
2
Recognize the general principle
Any subsequent action that indicates continued ownership over one slave clarifies that the other was intended for freedom.
Manumission removes ownership; inconsistent actions show the slave was not freed.
3
Apply to specific actions
Sale, gift, charity, making mudabbar, and claiming child from a slave woman all indicate ownership, so the other slave is freed.
Death also clarifies because the dead cannot be a subject of a legal act.
4
Distinguish the exception
Intercourse does not clarify because it is not exclusive to ownership of the slave's person; it can occur with a wife or a slave.
The text explicitly states intercourse is not a bayan.
5
Understand the proof
The proof is logical: manumission removes ownership; if the master later deals with a slave as owner, that slave must not have been freed.
This reasoning is derived from the nature of ownership and manumission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب العتاق العتق المبهم

[١] قوله : أو ماتت إحداهما؛ ولو طلّق إحداهما هل يكون ذلك بياناً؛ لأنَّ المراد في الإيجاب المبهم هو الأخرى، فإن كان الأوّلُ رجعياً لا يكون ذلك بياناً؛ لأنَّ المطلقة يقع عليها الطلاق ما دامت في العدة، سواء كان الثاني بائناً أو رجعياً. وإن كان الأول بائناً، فإن كان الثاني رجعياً فاعلم كذلك، وإن كان بائناً كان بياناً، وذلك لما عرف أن البائن يلحق الرجعي، ولا يلحق البائن، وهذا كله إذا كان الطلاق المعين قبل مدة صالحة لانقضاء العدّة. هي الأخرى.

[٢] قوله : أما الوطء فلان... الخ؛ حاصله : أن بين النكاح والطلاق منافاة شرعاً، فإنّ الأول موضوع شرعاً لحل الاستمتاع، والطلاق لإزالته، فلما وطئ إحداهما دلّ ذلك على أنها ليست بمطلقة، فإنّه يبعد من شأن المسلم ارتكاب الوطء مع صدور ما يزيله منه، فيعلم منه أنّ المطلقة هي الأخرى.

[٣] قوله : وأما الموت... الخ؛ حاصله : أنه قد تقرّر في مقرّه أنَّ البيان في الإيجاب المبهم إنشاء من وجه، فإنّه من حيث أنه مظهر للمراد من إيجابه السابق ومخبر لما قصده بمبهمه إخبار، ومن حيث أنَّ الإيجاب السابق الإنشائي لا يتم حكمه ولا يظهر أثره إلا بهذا البيان إنشاء، كأنه صدرَ منه الإيجاب في الحال والإنشاء لا بد له حين صدوره من الموجب من محل قابل. ولذا لو قال للميت : أعتقته يكون لغواً، فلا بد حين البيان من كون كل واحدٍ منهما محلاً، فإذا ماتت إحداهما خرجت عن المحلية، فلم تبق محلاً إلا الأولى، فتعينت هي لوقوع أثر إيجابه فيها، وقس عليه كون الموتِ بياناً في العتق المبهم على ما سيأتي.

[٢] وإن قال : أحدكما حرّ، فباعَ أحدهما، أو مات أحدهما، أو دبر أحدهما، أو استولد إحداهما، أو وهب أحدهما أو تصدق به وسلم، فكل ذلك بيان أن المراد هو الآخر. أما إن وَطِئ إحداهما لا يكون بياناً؛ لأن الاعتاق إزالة الملك، فالبيع ونحوه يدلُّ على أن الملك باق في المبيع، فلا يكون مراداً بالاعتاق.

[١] قوله : أو مات؛ سواءً كان موته حتف أنفه، أو بقتل العبد نفسه أو بقتل المولى والأجنبي. كذا في «النهر».

[٢] قوله : أو دبر أحدهما؛ جعله مدبّراً، وعلّق عتقه بموت نفسه، وكذا لو أعتقه منجزاً أو معلقاً، أو مضافا إلى زمان كإن دخلت الدار فأنت حر أو أنت حرّ غداً أو نحو ذلك، فيعتق هذا بالعتق المستأنف، ويتعين الآخر للمبهم السابق، فيعتق به. ولو قال لأحدهما : أعتقتك، ولم يرد به الإنشاء بل الإخبار عما مضى بإيجابه المبهم، تعين هذا ديانة، وصدق قضاء. كذا في «البحر» و«النهر».

[٣] قوله : أو استولد؛ بأن كان العتق المبهم خطاباً إلى أمتيه، فوطئ إحداهما وولدت ولداً فادعى نسبه منه.

[٤] قوله : أو وهب؛ ومثله كلُّ تصرُّف يكون دليلاً على بقاء الملك فيه كالإجارة والتزويج والكتابة والإيصاء والرهن ونحو ذلك. كذا في «شرح الكنز» للزَّيْلَعِي.

[٥] قوله : فكل ذلك بيان؛ وذلك لأنَّ ارتكاب مثل بهذه التصرفات دليل على بقاء ملكه فيه، فيدل ذلك على أنَّ المراد بالمبهم الآخر.

[٦] قوله : باق في المبيع؛ توضيحه : إِنَّ الإعتاق وُضِعَ شرعاً لإزالة ملك الرقبة، فإذا تصرف في أحدهما بعد الإعتاق المبهم تصرّفاً يختص بالملك دلّ ذلك على بقاء الملك في التصرف فيه، كالبيع والموهوب له، فدل ذلك على أنه لم يكن مراد بالمبهم، بل المراد هو الآخر، فيتعيّن للعتق. وأما الوطء فليس تصرّفاً مختصاً بملك الرقبة، بدليل وجوده في المنكوحة، بل هو تصرف في البضع، فلا يدل على بقاء ملك الرقبة، فلا يكون بياناً.
Book of Manumission: Ambiguous Manumission.

[1] His saying: 'or one of them dies': And if he divorces one of them, does that serve as clarification? Because the intended meaning in the ambiguous obligation is the other. If the first divorce is revocable, it does not serve as clarification because the divorce falls upon her as long as she is in her waiting period, whether the second divorce is irrevocable or revocable. If the first is irrevocable, then if the second is revocable, it is likewise; but if the second is irrevocable, it serves as clarification, because it is known that an irrevocable divorce can follow a revocable one, but an irrevocable does not follow an irrevocable. All this applies if the specified divorce occurred before a period sufficient for the completion of the waiting period. The other is the intended.

[2] His saying: 'As for intercourse...' The summary: Between marriage and divorce there is legal contradiction, for marriage is legally instituted for the permissibility of intercourse, and divorce is instituted to remove it. So when he has intercourse with one of them, that indicates that she is not divorced, because it is unlikely for a Muslim to engage in intercourse while having issued that which removes it. So it is known that the divorced one is the other.

[3] His saying: 'As for death...' The summary: It has been established that clarification in an ambiguous obligation is, in one aspect, a creative act, because it manifests the intended meaning of his previous obligation and informs of what he intended by his ambiguous expression. In another aspect, the previous creative obligation is not completed in its ruling nor does its effect appear except by this clarification as a creative act, as if the obligation were issued at that moment. A creative act requires, at the time of its issuance from the obligator, a subject capable of receiving it. Hence, if one says to a dead person 'I have freed you,' it is meaningless. So at the time of clarification, each of the two must be a subject. When one of them dies, she exits from being a subject, so only the first remains as a subject, and she becomes specified for the effect of his obligation to fall upon her. Apply the same principle to death being clarification in ambiguous manumission, as will come.

[2] And if he says: 'One of you is free' and then he sells one of them, or one of them dies, or he makes one a mudabbar, or he has a child with one of them, or he gifts one of them or gives it in charity and delivers it, then all of that is clarification that the intended is the other. However, if he has intercourse with one of them, it is not clarification, because manumission is removal of ownership; sale and the like indicate that ownership remains in the sold item, so it cannot be intended for manumission.

[1] His saying: 'or dies': Whether his death is natural, or by the slave killing himself, or by the master or a stranger killing him. Thus in al-Nahr.

[2] His saying: 'or makes one a mudabbar': He makes him a mudabbar, attaching his freedom to his own death. Likewise, if he frees him immediately or conditionally, or attaches it to a time, like 'if you enter the house you are free' or 'you are free tomorrow' or the like. This one becomes free by the fresh manumission, and the other becomes specified for the previous ambiguous one, so he becomes free by it. And if he says to one of them 'I freed you' not intending a new action but rather informing about what occurred from his ambiguous obligation, this one is specified in terms of religious obligation, and he is truthful in court. Thus in al-Bahr and al-Nahr.

[3] His saying: 'or has a child': That is, if the ambiguous manumission was addressed to his two slave women, and he had intercourse with one and she gave birth and he claimed paternity.

[4] His saying: 'or gifts': And similar is every action that indicates the continuation of ownership over it, such as leasing, marriage, kitaba, bequest, pledge, and the like. Thus in Sharh al-Kanz by al-Zayla'i.

[5] His saying: 'all of that is clarification': Because undertaking such actions indicates the continuation of his ownership over it, so that indicates that the intended one in the ambiguous statement is the other.

[6] His saying: 'remains in the sold item': Elucidation: Manumission is legally instituted to remove ownership of the slave's person. So if he performs an action over one of them after the ambiguous manumission, an action that is exclusive to ownership, that indicates the continuation of ownership in the item of that action, like sale and gift. Thus it indicates that it was not intended by the ambiguous statement, rather the intended is the other, so he becomes specified for manumission. As for intercourse, it is not an action exclusive to ownership of the slave's person, evidenced by its existence with a married woman; rather it is an action over the sexual organ, so it does not indicate continuation of ownership of the slave's person, and thus is not clarification.
Source pages p. 651

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah deals with how ambiguous manumission or divorce can be clarified by subsequent events or actions. The core principle is that any action indicating continued ownership (like sale, gift, or testament) of one slave shows that the other was intended for freedom. Conversely, actions not specific to ownership, like intercourse, do not clarify. The author first relates a discussion from divorce, where similar principles apply: if a husband says 'one of you is divorced' and then has intercourse with one, it indicates she is not the intended, because intercourse is inconsistent with divorce. Death also clarifies, since the dead cannot be a subject of a legal action. The passage then lists clarifying actions in manumission: sale, death, making a mudabbar, having children, gift, charity, etc. All these show that the slave's ownership remains, so he is not freed. The commentary also clarifies that if the master later says 'I freed you' meaning the original ambiguous declaration, that also specifies. The reasoning is that manumission removes ownership; if you later deal with the slave as owner, it contradicts freedom. The only exception is intercourse, which can occur with a wife or slave, so it does not prove ownership of the person.

Key Terms
العتق المبهم (al-itq al-mubham): An ambiguous manumission where the master says 'one of you is free' without specifying which slave.
بيان (bayan): Clarification of an ambiguous statement by a later action or event that reveals the intended referent.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose freedom is contingent upon the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sold slave becomes free.
B) The unsold slave becomes free.
C) Both become free.
D) Neither becomes free until the master specifies.

Key Takeaway
Actions indicating continued ownership specify which slave is not freed; the other automatically becomes free.
