Ambiguous Emancipation: Which Actions Clarify the Intended Slave?
Explains why selling clarifies but intercourse does not in ambiguous emancipation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between actions that serve as bayan (clarification) in ambiguous emancipation and those that do not, and apply the Hanafi tarjih between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding intercourse.

Core Idea
Actions that prove continued ownership of the slave's essence clarify; intercourse does not because it only proves usufruct ownership.

When a master says 'one of you is free' to two slaves, ambiguity arises. Later actions by the master can resolve this ambiguity. This passage explores which actions serve as clarification (bayan) and which do not, focusing on the specific case of intercourse and the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Recall the ambiguous emancipation (al-‘itāq al-mubham): the master says 'one of you is free' to two slaves without specifying which. The master then performs an action on one slave. We want to know if that action clarifies that the other slave was the intended one.
The action is done after the statement.
2
List Actions That Are Bayan
From the passage, list actions that the author declares as bayan: sale, death, tadbir, istilad, gift, charity (with delivery). Identify the common thread: these actions are only valid if the master still owns the slave (milk al-raqaba). Thus, performing them on a slave shows that slave was not freed, so the other is the intended one.
Death is a natural event, not an action, but it also clarifies because a dead slave cannot be the intended free one.
3
Understand Why Intercourse Differs (Abu Hanifa's View)
Abu Hanifa argues that emancipation removes ownership of the neck (milk al-raqaba), not ownership of usufruct (milk al-mut‘a). Intercourse is based on milk al-mut‘a, which can exist without milk al-raqaba (e.g., with a wife). Therefore, intercourse does not prove that the slave is still owned; it is inconclusive.
The text says 'فلا يكون مجرد الوطء بياناً' - mere intercourse is not a bayan.
4
Compare with Sahibayn and Identify the Mufta Bihi
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that intercourse is also a bayan because it is an act of ownership that indicates continued dominion. Later authorities (al-Hidayah, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, al-Durr al-Mukhtar) adopt the Sahibayn's view for the sake of caution (ihtiyat) to resolve ambiguity. The mufta bihi position is that intercourse does serve as bayan.
The text does not give the Sahibayn's full dalil, but the tarjih is mentioned in later sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قال : أحدكما حرّ، فباعَ أحدهما ، أو مات أحدهما، أو دبر أحدهما، أو استولد إحداهما ، أو وهب أحدهما أو تصدق به وسلم، فكل ذلك بيان أن المراد هو الآخر. أما إن وَطِئ إحداهما لا يكون بياناً ؛ لأن الاعتاق إزالة الملك، فالبيع ونحوه يدلُّ على أن الملك باق في المبيع، فلا يكون مراداً بالاعتاق. وأما الوطء فلأنَّ الإعتاق لم يوضع لإزالة حلّ الوطء، بل حل الوطء إنما يزولُ بتبعية زوالِ الرّق، أو زوالِ ملكِ الرقبة ، ولم يَزَلْ شيء منهما، وهذا قول أبي حنيفة. وأما الوطء فلأنَّ الإعتاق لم يوضع لإزالة ملك المتعة، بل قد يزول ملك المتعة مع إزالة ملك الرقبة تبعاً، كما في عتق الأمة، وقد لا توجد إزالة ملك المتعة مع إزالة ملك الرقبة كما في عتق العبد، فلا يكون مجرّد الوطء بياناً، بخلاف الوطء في صورة الطلاق، فإن الطلاق موضوع لإزالة ملك المتعة، فالوطء المنبئ عن بقاء ملك المتعة يكون بياناً لكون المطلقة غير الموطوءة.
If he said: one of you two is free, then he sold one of them, or one of them died, or he made one of them a mudabbar, or he had intercourse with one of them and she bore a child, or he gifted one of them or gave it in charity and delivered it, then all of that is a clarification that the intended is the other. As for if he had intercourse with one of them, it is not a clarification, because emancipation is removal of ownership. So sale and the like indicate that ownership remains in the sold item, so it is not intended by the emancipation. As for intercourse, because emancipation was not instituted to remove the permissibility of intercourse; rather, the permissibility of intercourse is only removed by the removal of slavery, or by removal of ownership of the neck, and neither of them has been removed. And this is the statement of Abu Hanifah.
Source pages p. 652

Commentary
This passage deals with ambiguous emancipation ('itq mubham), where a master says to two slaves 'one of you is free' without specifying. The master then performs an action with one of them. The question is whether that action clarifies which slave was intended for freedom. The author explains that actions like sale, death, tadbir, istilad (intercourse resulting in a child), gift, and charity all serve as clarifications (bayan) that the slave upon whom the action was performed was NOT the intended one, meaning the other slave is the one who becomes free. The reasoning: emancipation removes the master's ownership of the slave's head (milk al-raqaba). Actions like sale are only valid if ownership still exists; hence performing such an action on a slave proves that the master still owned that slave at the time of the action, so that slave could not have been the one freed by the ambiguous statement. Thus the intended slave is the other one. However, intercourse (wat') does not serve as clarification, and this is the position of Abu Hanifa. The reason is that intercourse is not an action specific to ownership of the neck; it is permitted by ownership of the right to enjoy (milk al-mut'a), which can exist without ownership of the neck (as in the case of a wife). Emancipation removes ownership of the neck, not the right to enjoyment directly. So intercourse does not indicate that ownership of the neck remains; it only indicates that the right to enjoyment remains, but that right can persist even after emancipation in certain ways? Actually, the text explains: in the case of an ambiguous emancipation, the ambiguous expression is directed at an unspecified slave. When the master later has intercourse with a specific slave, that action does not tell us which slave was meant by the previous ambiguous statement because both slave women were halal for him to have intercourse with (since he owned both). So it is not decisive. The author contrasts this with the case of ambiguous divorce (talaq mubham), where if a man tells one of his wives 'one of you is divorced' and then has intercourse with one, that does serve as clarification that the other is divorced, because divorce removes the right to enjoy (milk al-mut'a), and intercourse shows that the right to enjoy is still present in the one with whom he had intercourse. So there the logic is opposite.

Key Terms
العتاق المبهم (al-‘itāq al-mubham): Emancipation of a slave without specification, e.g., saying 'one of you is free' to two slaves.
بيان (bayān): An action that clarifies which slave was intended in the ambiguous emancipation.
ملك الرقبة (milk al-raqaba): Ownership of the slave's head (the essence of slavery), which is removed by emancipation.
ملك المتعة (milk al-mut‘a): Ownership of the right to enjoy, i.e., the right to have intercourse with a female slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does selling one slave after an ambiguous emancipation clarify that the other slave is the intended free one?
A) Because sale is a stronger act of ownership than intercourse.
B) Because sale is only valid if the seller owns the item sold, so it shows the sold slave was still owned.
C) Because the Prophet (PBUH) said sale clarifies emancipation.
D) Because the buyer cannot own a free person.

Key Takeaway
In ambiguous emancipation, actions that depend on ownership of the slave's essence (milk al-raqaba) serve as clarification; intercourse does not because it only proves ownership of usufruct (milk al-mut‘a).

Intercourse as Clarification in Ambiguous Manumission
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether intercourse clarifies ambiguous manumission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether intercourse clarifies ambiguous manumission and identify the mufta bihi position with its reasoning.

Core Idea
Intercourse does not clarify ambiguous manumission according to Abu Hanifa, but the relied-upon view of his two disciples treats it as clarification.

This lesson examines a classical Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding whether the act of intercourse (wat') serves as a legal clarification (bayan) in a case of ambiguous manumission. The disagreement hinges on the relationship between ownership, the legality of intercourse, and the nature of the manumission pronouncement. Understanding this dispute illuminates how the Hanafi school handles conflicts between general legal principles and practical caution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario of ambiguous manumission
A man says to his two slave women: 'One of you is free,' without specifying which. This is called 'itq mubham. The master then has intercourse with one of them. Does this act clarify which woman was freed?
The ambiguity is essential; if he had specified, there would be no dispute.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
According to Abu Hanifa, intercourse does not serve as clarification. His reasoning: manumission is not designed to remove the legality of intercourse; that removal follows only from the removal of slavery or ownership. In ambiguous manumission, neither has been removed from the specific woman, so ownership remains, making intercourse permissible and thus not a clarifying act.
He distinguishes this from divorce, where intercourse does clarify because divorce directly removes the right of enjoyment.
3
State the two companions' position and reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that intercourse does clarify. Their argument: intercourse is only permissible in ownership. By having intercourse with a specific woman, the master demonstrates she remains his property, thereby indicating that the other woman was the one freed.
Thus, according to them, intercourse with each woman becomes forbidden because one of them is free, and intercourse with a free person is unlawful.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, the master may lawfully have intercourse with both women. Under the two companions, intercourse with either is forbidden (since the freed one is unknown and intercourse with her would be zina).
This has significant implications for the master's actions post-manumission.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its basis
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of the two companions. Later Hanafi authorities (al-Marghinani, al-Haskafi, Ibn Abidin) give preponderance to their view due to caution (ihtiyat). Fatwa is given accordingly.
Note that Abu Hanifa's view is not entirely discarded but is considered less cautious.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب العتاق العتق المبهم
وأما الوطء فلأنَّ الإعتاق لم يوضع لإزالة حلّ الوطء، بل حل الوطء إنما يزولُ بتبعية زوالِ الرّق، أو زوالِ ملكِ الرقبة ، ولم يَزَلْ شيء منهما، وهذا قول أبي حنيفة (1)
فرغ لملك المتعة، والإعتاقُ لم يوضع لإزالة ملك المتعة، بل قد يزول ملك المتعة مع إزالة ملك الرقبة تبعاً، كما في عتق الأمة، وقد لا توجد إزالة ملك المتعة مع إزالة ملك الرقبة كما في عتق العبد، فلا يكون مجرّد الوطء بياناً، بخلاف الوطء في صورة الطلاق، فإن الطلاق موضوع لإزالة ملك المتعة، فالوطء المنبئ عن بقاء ملك المتعة يكون بياناً لكون المطلقة غير الموطوءة.
(۱) قوله : زوال الرق؛ بأن جعله معتقاً حراً ، فلا يملكه أحد، ولا ينفذ تصرف أحد فيه ، لا الوطء ولا البيع ونحوه.
(٢) قوله : أو زوال ملك الرقبة ؛ أي مع بقاء الرق بأن باعه أو وهبه أو تصرف تصرفاً آخر أخرجه من ملكه إلى ملك غيره.
(۳) قوله : ولم يزل شيء منهما ؛ أي في العتق المبهم، فيكون ملكه قائماً في التي توطأ منهم أيتهما كانت، وإذا كان الملك قائماً كان الوطء حلالاً ، أما أنّ الملك قائم فلان إيقاع العتق إنّما هو في المنكرة المبهمة، وهي أي الموطوءة غير منكرة بل معينة، فلا يكون الإيقاع فيها ، وإذا لم يكن الإيقاع فيها لم يزل الملك عنها.
وأما إنه إذا كان الملك قائماً فالوطء حلال، فهو ظاهر، وإذا كان الوطء حلالاً لم يكن بياناً ؛ لأن كل واحد منهما على هذه الصفة. كذا في «العناية»(۲) و«النهاية» وغيرهما.
[٤] قوله : وهذا قول أبي حنيفة له ؛ أي عدم كون الوطء في العتق المبهم بياناً عنده، ومبناه على أن وطء كل منهما حلال عنده لما مر من أنَّ الإيقاع في المبهم ، والوطء محله المعين.
(1) لأن الملك قائم في الموطوءة؛ لأن الإيقاع في المنكرة، وهي معينة، فكان وطؤها حلالاً، فلا يجعل بياناً ؛ ولهذا حلّ وطؤهما على مذهبه إلا أنه لا يفتي به. كما في «الهداية»(٢ : ٦٢)، ورجح صاحب «الفتح» (٤) : ٥٠٢) و(البحر ) (٤) (۲۷۰) قولهما، وقالوا: لا يفتى بقول الإمام لترك الاحتياط. وفي (الدر المختار (۳) : ۲۳): وعليه الفتوى.
(۲) (العناية» (٤) : ٥٠٠).
وأما عندهما فالوطء في العتقِ المبهم بيان أيضاً ، لأنَّ الوطء لا يحل إلا في الملك، فيدل على أنَّ الموطوءة ملكه ، فلم تكن مرادة بالإعتاق.
وعندهما الوطء بكل منهما حرام، وهو الذي وجه صاحب «الفتح»، وفي «البحر» : الحاصل : إنّ الراجح قولهما، وأنه لا يفتى بقول الإمام كما في «الهداية))) وغيرها، لما فيه من ترك الاحتياط، مع أن الإمام ناظر إلى الاحتياط في أكثر المسائل. [ ١ ] قوله : لأن الوطء...الخ ; حاصله : إنَّ حلّ الوطء مختص بالملك في المملوك، وبدونه لا يحلّ، فإذا وطئ لأحد الأمتين دلّ ذلك على بقاءِ ملكه فيها، فتتعين الأخرى بكونها مرادة بالمبهم. والسر فيه : أن أحدهما حرّة بيقين، والوطء إنّما يَحِلُّ فيمَن له الملك فيه ، فلو لم يكن وطء أحدهما بياناً لتخصيص العتق بالأخرى ، لَزِمَ وقوع الوطء في غير الملك.
Book of Manumission: Ambiguous Manumission. As for intercourse, because manumission was not placed to remove the legality of intercourse; rather, the legality of intercourse is removed only by the consequence of the removal of slavery, or the removal of ownership of the slave body, and none of these has been removed. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa. He turned to the right of enjoyment, and manumission was not placed to remove the right of enjoyment; rather, the right of enjoyment may be removed along with removal of ownership of the slave body incidentally, as in the manumission of a female slave, and it may not occur with removal of ownership of the slave body as in the manumission of a male slave. So mere intercourse is not a clarification, unlike intercourse in the case of divorce, because divorce is placed to remove the right of enjoyment, so intercourse that indicates the continuation of the right of enjoyment becomes a clarification that the divorced woman is not the one with whom intercourse occurred. (1) He said: Removal of slavery: by making him a free man, so no one owns him, and no one's disposal is effective regarding him, neither intercourse nor sale nor the like. (2) He said: Or removal of ownership of the slave body: i.e., with the continuation of slavery, by selling him, gifting him, or another disposal that removes him from his ownership to the ownership of another. (3) He said: And none of these has been removed: i.e., in ambiguous manumission, so his ownership remains in the one he has intercourse with, whichever she is, and when ownership remains, intercourse is permissible. As for ownership being established, it is because the occurrence of manumission is only regarding the indefinite ambiguous one, and she—the one with whom intercourse occurs—is not indefinite but specific, so the occurrence is not upon her, and if the occurrence is not upon her, ownership is not removed from her. And as for if ownership remains, then intercourse is permissible; that is apparent, and if intercourse is permissible, it is not a clarification, because each of them is in this state. Thus in al-'Inayah and al-Nihayah and others. [4] He said: This is the statement of Abu Hanifa: i.e., that intercourse is not a clarification in ambiguous manumission according to him, and its basis is that intercourse with each of them is permissible according to him, based on what passed: that the occurrence is upon the ambiguous, and intercourse is upon the specific. (1) Because ownership remains in the one with whom intercourse occurs; because the occurrence is upon the indefinite, and she is specific, so her intercourse was permissible, thus it is not made a clarification. Therefore, intercourse with both is permissible according to his school, except that he does not issue fatwa accordingly. As in al-Hidayah (2:62), and the author of al-Fath (4:502) and al-Bahr (4:270) gave preponderance to the statement of the two companions, and they said: Fatwa is not given according to the imam's statement due to abandoning caution. And in al-Durr al-Mukhtar (3:23): Fatwa is upon it. (2) al-'Inayah (4:500). And according to the two of them, intercourse in ambiguous manumission is also a clarification, because intercourse is only permissible in ownership, so it indicates that the one with whom intercourse occurs is his property, thus she is not intended by the manumission. And according to them, intercourse with each of them is forbidden, and this is what the author of al-Fath directed. And in al-Bahr: The summary is that their statement is preponderant, and fatwa is not given according to the imam's statement, as in al-Hidayah and others, because it abandons caution, even though the imam looks to caution in most issues. [1] He said: Because intercourse... etc. Its gist: That the permissibility of intercourse is specific to ownership in the owned, and without it, it is not permissible. So if he has intercourse with one of the two slave women, that indicates the continuation of his ownership in her, so the other becomes determined as the one intended by the ambiguous. The secret in it is that one of them is definitely free, and intercourse is only permissible with the one in whom he has ownership. So if intercourse with one of them were not a clarification to specify the manumission for the other, it would necessitate the occurrence of intercourse in what is not owned.
Source pages p. 653

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (Ikhtilaf) regarding whether the act of sexual intercourse (wat') can serve as a clarification (bayan) in a case of ambiguous manumission ('itq mubham). The scenario: a man says to one of his two slave women, 'One of you is free,' without specifying which. If he then has intercourse with one of them, does that indicate she is not the one he intended to free? According to Imam Abu Hanifa, intercourse does not serve as clarification. His reasoning: manumission is not designed to remove the legality of intercourse; rather, that legality is removed only as a consequence of removing slavery itself or removing ownership of the slave's body. In ambiguous manumission, neither slavery nor ownership has been removed from the specific woman with whom intercourse occurred, because the manumission was pronounced upon the indefinite (munkarah mubhamah), not upon the specific individual. Therefore, ownership remains, making intercourse permissible, and thus it cannot be taken as an indication that she is not the freed one. He distinguishes this from divorce, where intercourse does serve as clarification because divorce is specifically aimed at removing the right of marital enjoyment. According to Abu Hanifa, intercourse with both women is permissible, but this ruling is not the basis for fatwa. His two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold the opposite view: intercourse does function as clarification in ambiguous manumission. Their argument: intercourse is lawful only within one's ownership. By having intercourse with one particular woman, the master demonstrates that she remains in his ownership, thereby clarifying that the other woman was the one intended for manumission. Consequently, intercourse with each of them becomes unlawful. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of the two companions, as preponderated by later authorities like al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah and others, because it aligns with caution (ihtiyat). The fatwa is given accordingly.

Key Terms
العتق المبهم (al-'itq al-mubham): Manumission of one of two or more slaves without specifying which one; the slave to be freed is left ambiguous.
البيان (al-bayan): A clarifying action that resolves the ambiguity, indicating which slave was intended for manumission.
الوطء (al-wat'): Sexual intercourse with a slave woman; its legal status depends on ownership and is used as a potential indicator in ambiguous manumission.
ملك المتعة (milk al-mut'ah): The right to sexual enjoyment of a slave; a component of ownership that can be removed separately.
ملك الرقبة (milk al-raqabah): Ownership of the slave's body; full proprietary ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on sexual intercourse (wat') in the case of ambiguous manumission ('itq mubham)?
A) Intercourse with each slave woman is permissible and does not serve as clarification.
B) Intercourse with each slave woman is forbidden and serves as clarification of which one is free.
C) Intercourse is permissible with the one intended to be freed and forbidden with the other.
D) Intercourse is forbidden only if the master explicitly states his intention.

Key Takeaway
In ambiguous manumission, the relied-upon Hanafi view holds that intercourse with any of the slaves is forbidden because it clarifies that the one with whom intercourse occurred is still owned, thus the other is free.

Half-Freedom When the Firstborn's Order is Unknown
Conditional manumission ruling with ambiguity resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional manumission when the firstborn's gender order is unknown, and explain the reasoning behind the half-freedom rule.

Core Idea
Uncertainty in condition triggers split ruling: half freedom, half slavery.

The Hanafi school recognizes conditional manumission as valid. But what happens when the condition is ambiguous, such as when twins are born and the order is unknown? In this lesson, we examine a ruling from al-Hidayah that resolves the uncertainty by granting half-freedom to the mother and daughter. We will also explore a minority view within the school and understand why the majority position is preferred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The master's statement: 'If your first child is a son, you are free.' This creates a conditional right to freedom tied to the firstborn's gender.
The condition must be a clear future event.
2
Analyze the straightforward cases
If the first child is a son (agreed upon), the mother is free. If the first child is a daughter (agreed upon), she remains a slave.
Agreement between master and slave removes ambiguity.
3
Evaluate the ambiguous case
When twins are born (son and daughter) and the order is unknown, the condition is partially fulfilled. The law splits the difference.
Uncertainty leads to proportional freedom.
4
Understand the split ruling
Half of the mother and half of the daughter are freed. Both must work (sa'y) for the remaining half of their value.
This avoids total loss of either right.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Imam Muhammad in al-Kaysaniyyat held that no freedom is granted; the master takes an oath. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is the half-freedom ruling.
Both views have reasoning, but the majority follows al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبأول ولد تلدينه ابناً، فأنت حرّة، إن ولدت ابناً وبنتاً، ولم يُدْرَ الأوّلُ عُتِقَ نصف الام والبنت
[٢] قوله : وبأوّل ولد...الخ ; هذه المسألة وإن كانت من مسائل الحلف بالطلاق ،وموضوعها الباب الآتي ، لكن لما كان يثبت فيها عتق البعض أدرجها في هذا الباب. (۳) قوله : وبأوّل ولد ... الخ ; تفصيله أنه قال رجل لأمته : إن كان أوّل ولد تلدينه ذكراً فأنت حرة، فما لم تلد فهي أمة ، وإذا ولدت فإن ولدت ذكراً فهي حرة ؛ لوجود الشرط المعلّق عليه إذا تصادقا على أنه أوّل ولد ، وإن تصادقا على أنَّ الأوّل البنت فهي على الرق كما كانت ؛ لعدم وجود الشرط، فإن ولدت ابناً وبنتاً ولم يعلم أيهما أوّل عتق نصفُ الأم ونصفُ البنت ويسعيان في النصف الباقي.
[٤] قوله : ولم يُدر ; بصيغة المجهول، وذلك بأن لم يتصادقا على أحد الشقين. [0]قوله : عتق نصفُ الأم والبنت ; هذا هو المذكورُ في «الهداية» وغيرها، وذكر محمد له في «الكيسانيات»: إنّه لا يحكم في هذه الصورة بعتق واحد منهم، ولكن يحلف
(۱) «فتح القدير» (٤ : ٥٠٠).
(۲) «البحر الرائق (٤) : ٢٧٠).
(۳) «الهداية» (٤) : ٥٠٠).
And by the first child you give birth to, if it is a son, you are free. If she gives birth to a son and a daughter, and the first is not known, half of the mother and half of the daughter are freed. [2] He said: 'And by the first child...' etc. This issue, although it is from the issues of oaths by divorce and its subject is in the coming chapter, but because the manumission of a part is established in it, it is included in this chapter. (3) He said: 'And by the first child...' etc. Its detail: that a man said to his slave woman: 'If the first child you give birth to is a male, you are free.' As long as she does not give birth, she is a slave. When she gives birth, if she gives birth to a male, she is free, due to the existence of the condition upon which it is suspended, if they agree that it is the first child. If they agree that the first is a female, she remains in slavery as before, due to the non-existence of the condition. If she gives birth to a son and a daughter, and it is not known which is first, half of the mother and half of the daughter are freed, and they work (serve) for the remaining half. [4] He said: 'And it is not known' — in the passive voice, meaning that they do not agree on either side. [0] He said: 'Half of the mother and the daughter are freed' — this is what is mentioned in al-Hidayah and others. Muhammad mentioned for him in al-Kaysaniyyat: that in this case, no judgment of manumission is made for any of them, but he takes an oath.
Source pages p. 654

Commentary
This passage presents a specific ruling in the chapter on manumission: a conditional manumission tied to the gender of the firstborn child. The scenario: a master says to his slave woman, 'If the first child you give birth to is a son, you are free.' If she gives birth to only a son and both agree it is the first, she becomes free. If she gives birth to only a daughter, she remains a slave. The problematic case occurs when she gives birth to both a son and a daughter, and it is unknown which was born first. In that situation, according to the relied-upon view in al-Hidayah, half of the mother and half of the daughter become free. This is because the condition (firstborn being a son) is only partially fulfilled — it may be that the son was first, making the mother free, or the daughter was first, in which case the mother remains a slave. To resolve the uncertainty, the law treats the mother as half-free and half-slave. The daughter's status also splits: she is half-free as a consequence of her mother's partial freedom. Both must then work (sa'y) to earn the remaining half of their value for the master. An alternative view attributed to Muhammad in al-Kaysaniyyat holds that no one is judged free in such a case; instead, the master is put under oath to clarify, but the text does not fully detail this. The passage notes that although this issue belongs to the chapter on oaths by divorce, it is included here because it involves partial manumission.

Key Terms
أول ولد (awwalu walad): The first child born to a slave woman; used as a condition for manumission.
العتق المعلق (al-'itq al-mu'allaq): Manumission that is suspended upon a future condition; it takes effect when the condition is fulfilled.
السعي (al-sa'y): The act of a partially freed slave working to earn the remaining portion of their value for the master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a man tells his slave woman 'If your first child is a son, you are free,' and she gives birth to both a son and a daughter with unknown order, what is the ruling according to the relied-upon view in al-Hidayah?
A) The mother and daughter both remain fully enslaved.
B) The mother and daughter each become half-free and must work for the remaining half.
C) Only the son is freed, while the mother remains enslaved.
D) The master must take an oath, and no freedom is granted.

Key Takeaway
When a condition for manumission is partially fulfilled due to uncertainty, the Hanafi school splits the difference: half freedom, half slavery.

Ruling on Offspring in Ambiguous Emancipation
Ruling on offspring status in ambiguous emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the freedom status of a umm walad and her twin children when the birth order is uncertain, and explain the condition that leads to partial freedom.

Core Idea
The son is always a slave; the mother and daughter are half-free only if the boy was born first.

In cases of ambiguous emancipation, where a master frees one of his slaves without specification, the status of the offspring can become complex, especially when the mother is a umm walad and gives birth to twins. This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya clarifies the ruling: the son is always a slave, and the mother and daughter are each partially freed depending on the birth order. Let's trace the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The master frees one of his two slaves ambiguously; the slave woman is an umm walad and gives birth to a boy and a girl. Determine the order of birth.
2
Apply the condition
The mother's freedom depends on the boy being born first. If the boy is first, mother and daughter are free; if the girl is first, neither is free.
The daughter's freedom is derivative of the mother's freedom at the time of her birth.
3
Resolve uncertainty
Since the order is unknown, treat each as half-free, with a sa'y to earn the other half.
This is a practical solution for uncertainty.
4
Determine the son's status
The son is always a slave because he was born while the mother was a slave; the condition for freedom (boy first) does not affect him.
The son's status is independent of the condition.

Source Text

الوفاة
فإن قلت : ينبغي أن تقبل الشهادة هاهنا إذا ادّعى العبد أن ذلك لوجود الدعوى والمدعي. قلت : صاحب الحق أي العتق أحدهما لا بعينه، فدعـواهـمـا دعـوى مـن غـيـر صاحب الحق فلا تعتبر مع أن الشهادة حينئذ لا تكون موافقة للدعوى ؛ لأنّ الشهادة على أحد العبدين لا على العبدين. كذا في «العناية». [١]قوله : في مرض موته ; فإنّ العتق في مرض الموت في حكم الوصية ; ولهذا لا يجوز بما زاد على الثلث، بخلاف العتق في الصحة، فإنّه ليس في حكم الوصية. [۲] قوله : في الصحة أو المرض ; فإنّ التدبيرَ لَمَّا كان عتقاً بعد موت المولى صار في حكم الوصية مطلقاً، سواء صدر من المولى في حال صحته أو حال مرض موته ، بخلاف العتق المنجز ; فإنّه لا يكون في حكم الوصيّة إلا إذا صدرَ في مرض موته، وبهذا ظهر وجه تعميم الشارح له في التدبير وتخصيصه في العتق.
[٣] قوله : وأداء الشهادة ... الخ ؛ هذا صريح في أنَّ الشهادة على العتق المبهم في
العتق في مرض موته، وكذا على التدبير المبهم في صحته أو مرضه تقبلُ مطلقاً، سواء كان أداؤها في مرض موت المولى، أو بعد وفاته، وبه صرّح في «الهداية»، وكثير من
شروحها وغيرها.
وهو مخالف لما في «شرح مختصر الطحاوي للاسبيجابي من قوله : إذا شهد على رجل أنه قال لعبديه : أحدكما حرّ، والعبدان يدعيان ذلك، أو يدعى أحدهما، ففي قولهما تقبلُ هذه الشهادة ويجبر على البيان، وأما على قول أبي حنيفة له إن كان بهذا في حال الحياة فلا تقبل، وإن شهدا بعد الوفاة، فإن قال : إنّه كان في حال الصحة فهو على هذا الاختلاف أيضاً.
وإن قالا : إنه كان ذلك في المرض تقبل استحساناً، ويعتق من كل واحد نصفه، على اعتبار الثلث، ولو أشهدا أنه قال لعبديه: أحدهما مدبّر، فإن شهدا في حال الحياة
Book of Emancipation: Ambiguous Emancipation. And the son is a slave. And if two witnesses testify to the emancipation of one of his two slaves, the testimony is invalid except in a will. And the son is a slave; because if the first is the son, then the mother and daughter are free, and if the first is the daughter, none is freed; so half of the mother and daughter is freed, and the son is a slave in both cases. [2] (And if two testify to the emancipation of one of his two slaves, the testimony is invalid except in a will): i.e., they testify that he emancipated one of his two slaves; so the testimony is invalid according to Abu Hanifa... and there is no claimant... the master by Allah knows that she gave birth to the boy first; if he refuses the oath, his refusal is like his confession; if she swears, they are slaves. And in al-Nihaya it is said: This is the correct view because doubt arose concerning the condition of emancipation, which is the birth of the boy first, and the condition whose existence is not certain, the saying is that of the one who denies its existence. [1] His saying: And the son is a slave; i.e., whether he is born first or second; because his being born first is the condition for the mother’s freedom, so she is freed after his birth and does not follow him in freedom when he is first, but when he is last the matter is apparent. [2] His saying: Because the first... etc.; its summary: Each of the mother and daughter is freed in one situation, which is when she gives birth to the boy first; the mother’s neck is freed due to the existence of the condition, and the girl’s neck is freed because she is a dependent of her; since the mother is free when she gave birth to her; and neither is freed in the other situation, which is when she gives birth to the girl first, due to the absence of the condition; therefore we rule that half of each is freed, and they work to earn the other half. [3] His saying: is invalid; meaning if two witnesses testify against a man that he emancipated one of his two slaves ambiguously, this testimony is not accepted; because testimony in the rights of people is based on the precedence of a claim, so its acceptance must be preceded by a claim from a claimant. And here there is no claim because the emancipated one is one of the two slaves, so he is not specific, so neither of them can make a claim; and if there is no claim, the testimony is not accepted, unlike if the emancipation is specified, then the claimant exists, who is that slave. [4] His saying: Due to the absence of a claimant; because the one with the right is unknown, and a claim from the unknown is not realized. [From page 656] Except if this is in a will, i.e., they testify that he emancipated one of them during his death illness, or they testify about his tadbir in health or illness, and the performance of the testimony during his death illness or after death. If you say: It should be accepted here if the slave claims that, because there is a claim and a claimant. I say: The right-holder, i.e., the emancipation of one of them not specifically, so their claim is a claim from other than the right-holder, so it is not considered, and moreover the testimony then does not correspond to the claim; because the testimony is about one of the two slaves, not about both. This is in al-Inaya. [1] His saying: in his death illness; for emancipation during death illness is in the ruling of a will; therefore it is not valid beyond one-third, unlike emancipation in health, for it is not in the ruling of a will. [2] His saying: in health or illness; for tadbir, since it is emancipation after the master's death, becomes in the ruling of a will absolutely, whether it is issued by the master in health or in his death illness, unlike immediate emancipation; it is only in the ruling of a will if it occurs during his death illness. Thus the commentator's generalization in tadbir and particularization in emancipation becomes clear. [3] His saying: And the performance of the testimony... etc.; this explicitly states that testimony on ambiguous emancipation in the context of emancipation during death illness, and likewise on ambiguous tadbir in his health or illness, is accepted absolutely, whether its performance is during the master's death illness or after his death, and this is stated in al-Hidaya and many of its commentaries and others. And it contradicts what is in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi by al-Isbijabi from his saying: If someone testifies against a man that he said to his two slaves, 'One of you is free,' and the two slaves both claim that, or one of them claims it, then according to his (Abu Hanifa's) saying, if this is during his life, it is not accepted; but if they testify after death, then if they say it was in health, it is also subject to this difference. And if they say it was during illness, it is accepted by istihsan, and half of each is freed, based on consideration of the one-third. And if they testify that he said to his two slaves, 'One of you is mudabbar,' then if they testify during his life...
Source pages p. 655

Commentary
This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya discusses two distinct but related rulings under the chapter of ambiguous emancipation (al-'itq al-mubham). The first ruling concerns the case of a slave woman (umm walad) who gives birth to twins: a boy and a girl. The key point is that the son is always a slave regardless of the order of birth. The mother and daughter are freed only if the boy is born first; if the girl is born first, neither is freed. Since the order is often uncertain, the ruling here is that half of each (mother and daughter) is freed, and they must work (sa'y) to earn the remaining half. The son remains a full slave because he was born while the mother was a slave, and the condition for her freedom (birth of the boy first) does not affect him. The commentary explains that the condition for the mother's freedom is the birth of the boy first; if she gives birth to the girl first, she remains a slave and thus the girl, being born in slavery, remains a slave. The daughter's potential freedom is derivative of her mother's—if the mother is freed at the time of the girl's birth (i.e., after the boy first), the girl is born free and thus follows her. The second ruling is on the validity of testimony regarding an ambiguous emancipation—two witnesses testify that a master emancipated one of his two slaves without specifying which. According to Abu Hanifa, such testimony is invalid because there is no specific claimant; the right is ambiguous, and testimony in civil rights requires a prior claim (da'wa). However, the testimony is accepted if it occurs in the context of a will (wasiyya) or tadbir (postponed emancipation), because in those cases the emancipation is treated like a bequest and the testimony can be accepted after the master's death even without a specific claimant. The commentary further elaborates on the distinction between immediate emancipation during health (which is not in the ruling of a will) and during death illness (which is in the ruling of a will), and that tadbir is always in the ruling of a will. There is also a discussion contrasting the view in al-Nihaya with that in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi regarding the acceptance of testimony after death, where the latter allows acceptance by istihsan if the emancipation was during illness.

Key Terms
عتق مبهم ('itq mubham): Emancipation that is ambiguous because the master does not specify which slave is freed.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has given birth to her master's child.
سعي (sa'y): The act of working to earn money to pay for the remaining portion of freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if the order of birth is unknown in an ambiguous emancipation, what is the status of the son?
A) He is free.
B) He is half-free.
C) He is a slave.
D) He is a mudabbar.

Key Takeaway
The son is always a slave; the mother and daughter are half-free when the birth order is uncertain because the condition for full freedom is the boy being born first.

Testimony on Ambiguous Emancipation: Validity and Exceptions
Ruling on testimony validity in ambiguous emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why testimony on ambiguous emancipation is invalid in Hanafi law and identify the exceptions for wills (wasiyya) and postponed emancipation (tadbir).

Core Idea
Testimony on ambiguous emancipation is invalid because no specific claimant exists, except in wills and tadbir where the right-holder is identifiable after death.

Ambiguous emancipation creates legal uncertainty not only for the slaves but also for the validity of testimony in court. This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya explains that two witnesses testifying that a master freed 'one of his two slaves' cannot establish freedom because there is no specific claimant to assert the right. However, the testimony is accepted if it relates to a will (wasiyya) or postponed emancipation (tadbir), as the beneficiary becomes identifiable after the master's death. Let's examine the reasoning, including an intra-madhab difference on this point.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Two witnesses testify that a master emancipated one of his two slaves ambiguously. The testimony is invalid according to Abu Hanifa.
Invalid means the testimony is not accepted in court.
2
Identify the reason
Testimony in civil rights requires a prior claim (da'wa) from a specific claimant. Here, since the emancipated slave is not specified, no individual slave can claim the right.
Claimant must be known and specific.
3
Note the exception
The testimony is accepted if it is about emancipation in a will (wasiyya) or about tadbir, because these are considered future rights that vest after death, making the beneficiary identifiable.
Also accepted if the emancipation was during death illness.
4
Analyze the intra-madhab difference
Al-Isbijabi in his commentary allows acceptance after death by istihsan if the emancipation was during illness, while al-Nihaya affirms Abu Hanifa's position of rejection.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the rejection as in al-Hidayah.

Source pages p. 655

Commentary
This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya discusses two distinct but related rulings under the chapter of ambiguous emancipation (al-'itq al-mubham). The first ruling concerns the case of a slave woman (umm walad) who gives birth to twins: a boy and a girl. The key point is that the son is always a slave regardless of the order of birth. The mother and daughter are freed only if the boy is born first; if the girl is born first, neither is freed. Since the order is often uncertain, the ruling here is that half of each (mother and daughter) is freed, and they must work (sa'y) to earn the remaining half. The son remains a full slave because he was born while the mother was a slave, and the condition for her freedom (birth of the boy first) does not affect him. The commentary explains that the condition for the mother's freedom is the birth of the boy first; if she gives birth to the girl first, she remains a slave and thus the girl, being born in slavery, remains a slave. The daughter's potential freedom is derivative of her mother's—if the mother is freed at the time of the girl's birth (i.e., after the boy first), the girl is born free and thus follows her. The second ruling is on the validity of testimony regarding an ambiguous emancipation—two witnesses testify that a master emancipated one of his two slaves without specifying which. According to Abu Hanifa, such testimony is invalid because there is no specific claimant; the right is ambiguous, and testimony in civil rights requires a prior claim (da'wa). However, the testimony is accepted if it occurs in the context of a will (wasiyya) or tadbir (postponed emancipation), because in those cases the emancipation is treated like a bequest and the testimony can be accepted after the master's death even without a specific claimant. The commentary further elaborates on the distinction between immediate emancipation during health (which is not in the ruling of a will) and during death illness (which is in the ruling of a will), and that tadbir is always in the ruling of a will. There is also a discussion contrasting the view in al-Nihaya with that in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi regarding the acceptance of testimony after death, where the latter allows acceptance by istihsan if the emancipation was during illness.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Testimony in court; here it refers to witness testimony regarding an act of emancipation.
دعوى (da'wa): A legal claim made by a plaintiff seeking a right.
وصية (wasiyya): A will or bequest; emancipation during death illness is treated as a wasiyya, limited to one-third of the estate.
تدبير (tadbir): Postponed emancipation, where the master declares that a slave will be free after his death; treated like a wasiyya in all cases.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference, a method of reasoning that allows departure from strict analogy for the sake of public interest or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is testimony on ambiguous emancipation accepted?
A) Always, if two witnesses testify.
B) Never, because the emancipation is ambiguous.
C) Only if it relates to a will (wasiyya) or tadbir.
D) Only if both slaves agree on who was freed.

Key Takeaway
Testimony on ambiguous emancipation is invalid due to the lack of a specific claimant, except in wills and tadbir where the right-holder is identifiable after death.

Acceptance of Testimony for Ambiguous Emancipation (The Intra-Hanafi Dispute)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on acceptance of testimony for ambiguous emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when testimony for ambiguous emancipation is accepted and explain the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Testimony for ambiguous emancipation is accepted only after the master's death, as per Imam Abu Hanifa.

In this lesson, we examine the intra-Hanafi dispute concerning testimony for ambiguous emancipation—when a master says 'one of my two slaves is free' without specifying. The central question is whether witnesses can testify to this statement during the master's lifetime, especially during terminal illness. Imam Abu Hanifa rejects acceptance during life, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani accept it under certain conditions based on istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and context
The act is ambiguous emancipation (al-itq al-mubham). The context is testimony regarding the master's statement. Understand that the rule differs based on timing.
2
State the agreed ruling
After the master's death, testimony is accepted unanimously because it is considered a will. Half of each slave is freed (according to Muhammad).
Ignorance of the beneficiary does not invalidate a will.
3
Identify the dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that testimony during life (including terminal illness) is not accepted. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept it during terminal illness by istihsan.
4
Follow the Hanafi response
During life, the slave claimant is unknown, and the master is a denier; thus no valid lawsuit exists. The successor (heir/executor) has no standing while the master is alive.
Al-Shurunbulali and Ibn al-Humam critique the opposing view.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If testimony accepted during life, the slave would be freed immediately. If not, the slave is freed only after death, and half of each is freed (according to Muhammad).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب العتاق العتق المبهم
فهو على الاختلاف، وإن كان بعد الوفاة تقبل، سواء كان القولُ في المرض والصحة ; لأنّ هذه وصيته، والجهالة لا تبطل الوصية. انتهى.
ومثله في «شرح الكنز»، المسمّى بـ«كشف الحقائق»، وقال حسن الشرنبلالي في رسالته: «إصابة الغرض الأهم في العتق المبهم بعد نقله، وقد قصر قبول الشهادة على حصولها بعد موت الموصي عند الإمام له ; لمنع الإمام قبول الشهادة على عتق أحدهما حال الحياة ; لعدم تصوّر الدعوى من مجهول في العبدين، ولعدم المشهود له عيناً في الأمتين.
فلا يتجه ما أريد من تصحيح قبول الشهادة الحاصلة في مرض الموت بقول الشراح تبعاً للهداية» بأنّ العتق المذكور وصية، والخصم ; أي المدعي في إثبات الوصية إنما هو الموصى ; لأنَّ نفعه يعود إليه، وهو معلوم، وله خلف، وهو الوصي أو الوارث. ووجه عدم الاستقامة : أنَّ الخلف لا حكم له مع وجود الأصل، فلا يتصوّر له حكم لما أنه في حال حياة المولى إنما يكون الدعوى من العبد لا من المولى ; لأنه منكر، والعبد هاهنا مجهول، ولهذا قال المحقق ابن الهمام: قوله في «الهداية»: «يفيد أنها تقبل في حياته ، يعني عند الإمام الله ، وأنت قد علمت عدم قبولها قبل موته ; لأنَّ المدعي العبدان، وهما غير من أثبت فيه العتق.
فالحاصل أنّ إنزاله ; أي المولى مُدّعياً إنّما يكون بعد موته، وأما قبله فهو منكر ; ولهذا احتيج إلى الشهادة وردّت لعدم المدّعي ، ولا مخلّص إلا بتقييده بما إذا كان المريض قد صمت حال أداء الشهادة واستمرّ كذلك إلى أن مات، وعلى هذا يجب أن يؤخر القضاء بهذه الشهادة إلى أن يموت، فيقضى بها أو يعيش فيطلق لسانه فــرد لـعــدم الخصم». انتهى كلام ابن الهمام). أقول : وفيما جعله مخلصاً نظر ; لقوله : إنّه قبل موته منكر، فاحتيج إلى الشهادة، وردّت لعدم المدعي ، فلا وجود للشهادة ، ليتأخّر القضاء بها بعد الموت لفقد الدعوى ; إذ لا شهادة بدونها ; لأنه ليس الخصم إلا العبد حال حياة المولى، وهو مجهول ، فانتفى قبول الشهادة بفقد الدعوى الحقيقية والتقديرية. انتهـى كــلام الشرنبلالي، وهو كلام حسن، صادر من متكلم حسن، فاحفظه.
[ ١ ] قوله : استحساناً ; يعني أن مقتضى القياس الجلي هاهنا أيضاً هو عدم القبول لما مرّ أنّه لا اعتبار للشهادة عند عدم الدعوى، ولا وجود للدعوى إلا عند تعيين صاحب الحق، وهو هاهنا أحدهما مبهماً ، لكنّ القياس الخفي والنظر الدقيق وهو الذي يعبرون عنه بالاستحسان هاهنا هو القبول، وإليه أشار محمد له في «كتاب العتق» من «مبسوطه» حيث : قال لو قال الشاهدان كان ذلك عند الموت استحسن أن يعتق من كلّ واحد نصفه.
[٢] قوله : لأن التدبير ... الخ ; حاصله : إن التدبير حيثما وقع; أي في الصحة أو في المرض، والعتق في مرض كلاهما في حكم الوصيّة، والمدعي في إثبات الوصية هـو الموصي ; لأنه يحتاج إلى تنفيذ وصاياه وإثباتها ; لكون نفع الوصية عائداً إليه في الدنيا أو في الآخرة، فيكون المدعي هاهنا معلوماً، وبعد موته خلفه يقوم مقامه، وهو الوارث أو الوصي إلى الذي فَوَّضَ إليه الميت انتظام أموره، وجعله مدبر بيته، إذا كان الوارث صغيراً مثلاً ، فتقبلُ الشهادة لوجودها بعد الدعوى المعتبرة.
(۳) قوله : ولأن ... الخ ; هذا وجه آخر استحساني، ومحصله أن العتق المبهم بعد موت المولى يصير شائعاً بين العبدين، فيكون كلاً منهما مدعياً ; لكون كل منهما صاحب الحق، فيؤخذ المدعي بخلافِ الصورة السابقة، فإنّ الشهادة وردت في حياة المولى على عتق أحدهما، وليس هو بشائع فيهما ، حتى يكون كل منهما مدعيا، بل المدعي هو أحد العبدين، وهو مجهول، ولا يمكن أيضاً جعل المولى مدعياً ; لأنَّ المحتاج إلى إثباتِ العتق هو من له الحق، وهو العبد لا المولى، بل هو يكون منكراً ، فلا تقبل الشهادة لعدم الدعوى.
Book of Emancipation: Ambiguous Emancipation. So it is according to the difference, and if it was after death, it is accepted, whether the statement was during illness or health; because this is his will, and ignorance does not invalidate a will. End. Similar is in Sharh al-Kanz called Kashf al-Haqa'iq, and Hasan al-Shurunbulali said in his treatise: 'Isabah al-Gharad al-Ahm fi al-Itq al-Mubham after its transmission, and he restricted acceptance of testimony to after the death of the testator according to Imam Abu Hanifa; because the Imam prohibits acceptance of testimony for the emancipation of one of them during life due to the impossibility of a lawsuit from an unknown one among the two slaves, and due to the lack of a designated beneficiary among the two female slaves. So what is intended from correcting the acceptance of testimony occurring during terminal illness by the statement of the commentators following al-Hidayah is not sound' that the mentioned emancipation is a will, and the opponent—i.e., the claimant in proving the will—is the testator; because its benefit returns to him, and he is known, and he has a successor, who is the executor or heir. And the aspect of unsoundness: that the successor has no ruling in the presence of the original, so no ruling can be imagined for him because during the master's life the lawsuit is from the slave, not from the master; because he is a denier, and the slave here is unknown. For this reason, the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam said: His statement in al-Hidayah: 'It indicates that it is accepted during his life, meaning according to Imam Abu Hanifa'—and you already know its non-acceptance before his death; because the claimants are the two slaves, and they are not those for whom emancipation is established. So the conclusion is that his being considered a claimant—i.e., the master—is only after his death, but before it he is a denier; for this reason testimony was needed and rejected due to lack of a claimant, and there is no escape except by restricting it to when the patient was mute at the time of testimony and remained so until death, and on this the judgment with this testimony must be postponed until he dies, then judgment is given by it, or he lives and his tongue is released, so it is rejected due to lack of opponent. End of Ibn al-Humam's speech. I say: In what he made an escape there is consideration; because of his statement that before his death he is a denier, so testimony was needed and rejected due to lack of claimant, so there is no existence of testimony to postpone judgment with it after death due to loss of lawsuit; since there is no testimony without it; because the opponent is only the slave during the master's life, and he is unknown, so acceptance of testimony is negated by loss of actual and constructive lawsuit. End of al-Shurunbulali's speech, and it is good speech from a good speaker, so memorize it. [1] His statement: 'by istihsan' means that the requirement of clear analogy (qiyas jali) here is also non-acceptance, as previously mentioned that testimony is not considered in the absence of a lawsuit, and a lawsuit only exists when the right-holder is specified, but here he is one of them ambiguously. However, the hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) and precise consideration—which they call istihsan—here is acceptance. And Imam Muhammad referred to this in his "Mabsut" in the "Book of Emancipation" where he said: If the two witnesses say 'that was at the time of death', it is deemed good (istihsan) that half of each slave is freed. [2] His statement: 'because tadbir...' etc.; its summary: Tadbir wherever it occurs—i.e., in health or illness—and emancipation during illness, both are in the ruling of a will. The claimant in proving the will is the testator; because he needs to execute his bequests and prove them, since the benefit of the will returns to him in this world or the hereafter. So the claimant here is known, and after his death his successor stands in his place, which is the heir or the executor to whom the deceased entrusted the management of his affairs and made him administrator of his household, if the heir is a minor, for example. So testimony is accepted because it exists after a valid lawsuit. (3) His statement: 'and because...' etc.; this is another istihsan-based aspect, and its summary: Ambiguous emancipation after the master's death becomes shared between the two slaves, so each of them becomes a claimant, since each is the right-holder. So the claimant is identified, unlike the previous scenario, where testimony was given during the master's life for the emancipation of one of them, and it is not shared between them so that each becomes a claimant; rather the claimant is one of the two slaves, and he is unknown. It is also not possible to make the master a claimant because the one who needs to prove emancipation is the right-holder, i.e., the slave, not the master; rather he is a denier. So testimony is not accepted due to lack of a lawsuit.
Source pages p. 657

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the acceptance of testimony for ambiguous emancipation (al-Itq al-Mubham). The discussion arises when a master, during his life or terminal illness, says 'one of my two slaves is free' without specifying which one. Witnesses testify to this statement. The ruling differs based on whether the testimony is given during the master's lifetime or after his death. The passage begins by establishing that if the testimony occurs after death, it is accepted unanimously, because it is considered a will (wasiyyah), and ignorance of the beneficiary does not invalidate a will. The dispute centers on acceptance during the master's life, especially during terminal illness. Imam Abu Hanifa (referred to as 'Imam') holds that testimony during life is not accepted, because there is no identifiable claimant: the slave who would benefit is unknown, and the master is a denier (denying the claim). The commentators following al-Hidayah attempted to accept testimony during terminal illness by analogizing it to a will, arguing that the testator (master) is the claimant and is known, and after death his successor (heir or executor) takes over. However, al-Shurunbulali refutes this, stating that during the master's life, the successor has no standing while the original (master) exists. The lawsuit must come from the slave, but the slave is unknown. Ibn al-Humam suggests a possible escape: if the master was mute at the time of testimony and remained so until death, then the testimony could be accepted after death. But this is criticized because the testimony itself is considered non-existent during life due to lack of claimant. The passage then explains the reasoning behind the Hanafi position using the concept of istihsan (juristic preference). Clear analogy (qiyas jali) would dictate non-acceptance in all cases, but hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) or istihsan leads to acceptance after death. Imam Muhammad reported in his Mabsut that if witnesses say the statement was made at the time of death, it is deemed good that each slave gets half freedom. Two istihsan-based reasons are given: First, tadbir (granting freedom after death) and emancipation during illness are like wills, and the testator is the claimant, so testimony is accepted. Second, after death, the ambiguous emancipation becomes shared between the two slaves, making each a claimant. During life, it is not shared, so one slave is the unknown claimant. Thus, testimony is only accepted after death. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that testimony is accepted only after the master's death, as per Imam Abu Hanifa's view, and this is supported by the later scholars.

Key Terms
العتق المبهم (al-'itq al-mubham): Emancipation of a slave without specifying which one, e.g., 'one of my two slaves is free'.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference overriding clear analogy (qiyas jali) due to a stronger evidence or need.
خصم (khasm): The adversary or claimant in a lawsuit; the one who brings the case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon position), when is testimony for ambiguous emancipation accepted?
A) During the master's life, even in health.
B) During terminal illness only.
C) Only after the master's death.
D) Never, because the slave is unknown.

Key Takeaway
Testimony for ambiguous emancipation is accepted only after the master's death, because only then is there a known claimant (the slaves become co-claimants) and it is considered a will.

The Istihsan Reasoning in Ambiguous Emancipation
Expansion on istihsan reasoning in ambiguous emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the istihsan-based reasoning for accepting testimony after death and critique the attempt to extend it to life.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides clear analogy: after death, emancipation becomes shared, making each slave a claimant.

This lesson explores the istihsan (juristic preference) that underlies the acceptance of testimony for ambiguous emancipation after death. While clear analogy (qiyas jali) would dictate rejection always, hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) through istihsan leads to acceptance after death by treating the emancipation like a will. We also examine why this reasoning does not apply during the master's lifetime.

Guided Path
1
Recall the ruling of clear analogy (qiyas jali)
Clear analogy dictates that testimony requires a known claimant. In ambiguous emancipation, the slave is unknown, so testimony should never be accepted.
2
Identify the istihsan (hidden analogy)
After death, the emancipation is like a will (wasiyyah). The testator (master) becomes the claimant, and after death his successor (heir/executor) takes over. Thus testimony is accepted.
This is the first istihsan reason mentioned in the passage.
3
Examine the second istihsan reason
After death, the ambiguous emancipation becomes shared (shai') between the two slaves. Each becomes a claimant because each is a right-holder (sahib al-haqq).
4
Understand why istihsan does not apply during life
During life, the master is a denier, not a claimant. The successor has no standing while the original exists. The slave is unknown, so there is no lawsuit.
Al-Shurunbulali and Ibn al-Humam affirm this.
5
Critique of the escape attempt
Ibn al-Humam suggested that if the master is mute at the time of testimony and remains mute until death, judgment could be postponed. Al-Shurunbulali rejects this because the testimony itself is invalid without a lawsuit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب العتاق العتق المبهم
فهو على الاختلاف، وإن كان بعد الوفاة تقبل، سواء كان القولُ في المرض والصحة ; لأنّ هذه وصيته، والجهالة لا تبطل الوصية. انتهى.

فالحاصل أنّ إنزاله ; أي المولى مُدّعياً إنّما يكون بعد موته، وأما قبله فهو منكر ; ولهذا احتيج إلى الشهادة وردّت لعدم المدّعي ، ولا مخلّص إلا بتقييده بما إذا كان المريض قد صمت حال أداء الشهادة واستمرّ كذلك إلى أن مات، وعلى هذا يجب أن يؤخر القضاء بهذه الشهادة إلى أن يموت، فيقضى بها أو يعيش فيطلق لسانه فــرد لـعــدم الخصم». انتهى كلام ابن الهمام). أقول : وفيما جعله مخلصاً نظر ; لقوله : إنّه قبل موته منكر، فاحتيج إلى الشهادة، وردّت لعدم المدعي ، فلا وجود للشهادة ، ليتأخّر القضاء بها بعد الموت لفقد الدعوى ; إذ لا شهادة بدونها ; لأنه ليس الخصم إلا العبد حال حياة المولى، وهو مجهول ، فانتفى قبول الشهادة بفقد الدعوى الحقيقية والتقديرية. انتهـى كــلام الشرنبلالي، وهو كلام حسن، صادر من متكلم حسن، فاحفظه.
[ ١ ] قوله : استحساناً ; يعني أن مقتضى القياس الجلي هاهنا أيضاً هو عدم القبول لما مرّ أنّه لا اعتبار للشهادة عند عدم الدعوى، ولا وجود للدعوى إلا عند تعيين صاحب الحق، وهو هاهنا أحدهما مبهماً ، لكنّ القياس الخفي والنظر الدقيق وهو الذي يعبرون عنه بالاستحسان هاهنا هو القبول، وإليه أشار محمد له في «كتاب العتق» من «مبسوطه» حيث : قال لو قال الشاهدان كان ذلك عند الموت استحسن أن يعتق من كلّ واحد نصفه.
[٢] قوله : لأن التدبير ... الخ ; حاصله : إن التدبير حيثما وقع; أي في الصحة أو في المرض، والعتق في مرض كلاهما في حكم الوصيّة، والمدعي في إثبات الوصية هـو الموصي ; لأنه يحتاج إلى تنفيذ وصاياه وإثباتها ; لكون نفع الوصية عائداً إليه في الدنيا أو في الآخرة، فيكون المدعي هاهنا معلوماً، وبعد موته خلفه يقوم مقامه، وهو الوارث أو الوصي إلى الذي فَوَّضَ إليه الميت انتظام أموره، وجعله مدبر بيته، إذا كان الوارث صغيراً مثلاً ، فتقبلُ الشهادة لوجودها بعد الدعوى المعتبرة.
(۳) قوله : ولأن ... الخ ; هذا وجه آخر استحساني، ومحصله أن العتق المبهم بعد موت المولى يصير شائعاً بين العبدين، فيكون كلاً منهما مدعياً ; لكون كل منهما صاحب الحق، فيؤخذ المدعي بخلافِ الصورة السابقة، فإنّ الشهادة وردت في حياة المولى على عتق أحدهما، وليس هو بشائع فيهما ، حتى يكون كل منهما مدعيا، بل المدعي هو أحد العبدين، وهو مجهول، ولا يمكن أيضاً جعل المولى مدعياً ; لأنَّ المحتاج إلى إثباتِ العتق هو من له الحق، وهو العبد لا المولى، بل هو يكون منكراً ، فلا تقبل الشهادة لعدم الدعوى.
Book of Emancipation: Ambiguous Emancipation. So it is according to the difference, and if it was after death, it is accepted, whether the statement was during illness or health; because this is his will, and ignorance does not invalidate a will. End. Similar is in Sharh al-Kanz called Kashf al-Haqa'iq, and Hasan al-Shurunbulali said in his treatise: 'Isabah al-Gharad al-Ahm fi al-Itq al-Mubham after its transmission, and he restricted acceptance of testimony to after the death of the testator according to Imam Abu Hanifa; because the Imam prohibits acceptance of testimony for the emancipation of one of them during life due to the impossibility of a lawsuit from an unknown one among the two slaves, and due to the lack of a designated beneficiary among the two female slaves. So what is intended from correcting the acceptance of testimony occurring during terminal illness by the statement of the commentators following al-Hidayah is not sound' that the mentioned emancipation is a will, and the opponent—i.e., the claimant in proving the will—is the testator; because its benefit returns to him, and he is known, and he has a successor, who is the executor or heir. And the aspect of unsoundness: that the successor has no ruling in the presence of the original, so no ruling can be imagined for him because during the master's life the lawsuit is from the slave, not from the master; because he is a denier, and the slave here is unknown. For this reason, the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam said: His statement in al-Hidayah: 'It indicates that it is accepted during his life, meaning according to Imam Abu Hanifa'—and you already know its non-acceptance before his death; because the claimants are the two slaves, and they are not those for whom emancipation is established. So the conclusion is that his being considered a claimant—i.e., the master—is only after his death, but before it he is a denier; for this reason testimony was needed and rejected due to lack of a claimant, and there is no escape except by restricting it to when the patient was mute at the time of testimony and remained so until death, and on this the judgment with this testimony must be postponed until he dies, then judgment is given by it, or he lives and his tongue is released, so it is rejected due to lack of opponent. End of Ibn al-Humam's speech. I say: In what he made an escape there is consideration; because of his statement that before his death he is a denier, so testimony was needed and rejected due to lack of claimant, so there is no existence of testimony to postpone judgment with it after death due to loss of lawsuit; since there is no testimony without it; because the opponent is only the slave during the master's life, and he is unknown, so acceptance of testimony is negated by loss of actual and constructive lawsuit. End of al-Shurunbulali's speech, and it is good speech from a good speaker, so memorize it. [1] His statement: 'by istihsan' means that the requirement of clear analogy (qiyas jali) here is also non-acceptance, as previously mentioned that testimony is not considered in the absence of a lawsuit, and a lawsuit only exists when the right-holder is specified, but here he is one of them ambiguously. However, the hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) and precise consideration—which they call istihsan—here is acceptance. And Imam Muhammad referred to this in his "Mabsut" in the "Book of Emancipation" where he said: If the two witnesses say 'that was at the time of death', it is deemed good (istihsan) that half of each slave is freed. [2] His statement: 'because tadbir...' etc.; its summary: Tadbir wherever it occurs—i.e., in health or illness—and emancipation during illness, both are in the ruling of a will. The claimant in proving the will is the testator; because he needs to execute his bequests and prove them, since the benefit of the will returns to him in this world or the hereafter. So the claimant here is known, and after his death his successor stands in his place, which is the heir or the executor to whom the deceased entrusted the management of his affairs and made him administrator of his household, if the heir is a minor, for example. So testimony is accepted because it exists after a valid lawsuit. (3) His statement: 'and because...' etc.; this is another istihsan-based aspect, and its summary: Ambiguous emancipation after the master's death becomes shared between the two slaves, so each of them becomes a claimant, since each is the right-holder. So the claimant is identified, unlike the previous scenario, where testimony was given during the master's life for the emancipation of one of them, and it is not shared between them so that each becomes a claimant; rather the claimant is one of the two slaves, and he is unknown. It is also not possible to make the master a claimant because the one who needs to prove emancipation is the right-holder, i.e., the slave, not the master; rather he is a denier. So testimony is not accepted due to lack of a lawsuit.
Source pages p. 657

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the acceptance of testimony for ambiguous emancipation (al-Itq al-Mubham). The discussion arises when a master, during his life or terminal illness, says 'one of my two slaves is free' without specifying which one. Witnesses testify to this statement. The ruling differs based on whether the testimony is given during the master's lifetime or after his death. The passage begins by establishing that if the testimony occurs after death, it is accepted unanimously, because it is considered a will (wasiyyah), and ignorance of the beneficiary does not invalidate a will. The dispute centers on acceptance during the master's life, especially during terminal illness. Imam Abu Hanifa (referred to as 'Imam') holds that testimony during life is not accepted, because there is no identifiable claimant: the slave who would benefit is unknown, and the master is a denier (denying the claim). The commentators following al-Hidayah attempted to accept testimony during terminal illness by analogizing it to a will, arguing that the testator (master) is the claimant and is known, and after death his successor (heir or executor) takes over. However, al-Shurunbulali refutes this, stating that during the master's life, the successor has no standing while the original (master) exists. The lawsuit must come from the slave, but the slave is unknown. Ibn al-Humam suggests a possible escape: if the master was mute at the time of testimony and remained so until death, then the testimony could be accepted after death. But this is criticized because the testimony itself is considered non-existent during life due to lack of claimant. The passage then explains the reasoning behind the Hanafi position using the concept of istihsan (juristic preference). Clear analogy (qiyas jali) would dictate non-acceptance in all cases, but hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) or istihsan leads to acceptance after death. Imam Muhammad reported in his Mabsut that if witnesses say the statement was made at the time of death, it is deemed good that each slave gets half freedom. Two istihsan-based reasons are given: First, tadbir (granting freedom after death) and emancipation during illness are like wills, and the testator is the claimant, so testimony is accepted. Second, after death, the ambiguous emancipation becomes shared between the two slaves, making each a claimant. During life, it is not shared, so one slave is the unknown claimant. Thus, testimony is only accepted after death. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that testimony is accepted only after the master's death, as per Imam Abu Hanifa's view, and this is supported by the later scholars.

Key Terms
العتق المبهم (al-'itq al-mubham): Emancipation of a slave without specifying which one, e.g., 'one of my two slaves is free'.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference overriding clear analogy (qiyas jali) due to a stronger evidence or need.
خصم (khasm): The adversary or claimant in a lawsuit; the one who brings the case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does clear analogy (qiyas jali) reject testimony for ambiguous emancipation?
A) Because the master might change his mind.
B) Because the claimant (the slave) is unknown.
C) Because emancipation is not valid orally.
D) Because witnesses are not reliable.

Key Takeaway
Istihsan (hidden analogy) allows testimony for ambiguous emancipation after death because the claimants become known, but this reasoning does not extend to the master's lifetime.
