لا إن أدى بعضه بأن وضع المال في موضع يتمكنُ المولى من أخذه، وقوله : وإن خَلّي، يتصل بقوله : وعتق أي يعتق وإن كان الأداء بطريق التخلية": أي الأداء يحمل
بالتخلية.
[٤]
(لا إن أدى بعضه) : أي لا يعتق إن أدى بعضه [1] قوله : بأن وضع؛ أي العبد، حاصله : إن المولى ينزل قابضاً بالتخلية برفع الموانع، سواء قبض أو لم يقبض. (٢) قوله : بطريق التخلية ؛ هي بأن يرفع موانع القبض، ويضع المال بين يدي المولى، بحيث لو مدّ يده إليه أخذه، فحينئذ يحكم الحاكم بأنه قبضه، وكذا في ثمن المبيع وبدل الإجارة وسائر الحقوق.
وهذا يـفـيـد أنـه يـعـتـق بحقيقة القبض بالطريق الأولى، وهذا إذا كان العوض صحيحا، أما إن كان فاسداً كأن كان العوض خمراً أو مجهولاً جهالة فاحشة، كما لو قال : إن أديت إلي خمراً أو ثوباً فأنت حر ، فأدى ذلك لا ينزل المولى قابضاً إلا إن أخذه
مختاراً. كذا في «البحر» و«الفتح». [٣] قوله : يحصل بالتخلية ؛ وكذلك يحصلُ الأداء والعتق بعده بالتخلية في الكتابة أيضاً . عند العامة ، وعند زفـر الله لا يحصل العتق في الكتابة في التخلية بـل بالقبض حقيقة، فعلى هذا يكون هذا أيضاً من وجوه الفرق بين المكاتب والمعلّق عتقه بالأداء ، حيث لا يعتقُ عنده بالتخلية المكاتب، ويعتق المعلّق عتقه بالأداء.
[٤] قوله : لا إن أدى بعضه ؛ وذلك لأنَّ الشرط أداء الكل، وعند فواتِ الشرط يفوت المشروط ؛ ولهذا لا يعتقُ إن قيَّد المولى بدراهم فأدّى العبد دنانير، أو قيد بكيس أبيض مثلاً فدفعه في كيس أسود، أو قيده بالأداء في هذا الشهر فأدى إليه في الشهر
الآخر.
ولو حط المولى البعض بطلب العبد فأدّى الباقي لا يعتق لفقد الشرط الذي عَلَّقَ عليه العتق ، بخلاف المكاتب ؛ فإنه لو حط عنه المولى شيئاً من مال الكتابة فأدى الباقي عُتِق ؛ لأنَّ الكتابة عقد معاوضة، والمالُ هناك واجب شرعاً، فيتصور فيه الحط، وهاهنا
The Book of Manumission: Oath by Manumission and Manumission for a Payment. [The slave is] permitted to trade; if he pays, he is freed; not a mukatib. His payment is restricted to the assembly if he conditioned it with 'in'; but not with 'idha'. The master can take back from him if he pays from what he earned before the condition, not from after. He is freed in both cases. And if he vacates between him and it. [Commentary:] He becomes permitted to trade (ma'dhun) because of the master's desire for him to earn. Payment is restricted to the assembly if conditioned with 'in', not with 'idha'. The master recovers from him if he pays from earnings before the condition, not after. He is freed in both cases: whether he pays from pre-condition or post-condition earnings. 'And if he vacates between him and it' means between the master and the money. [1] 'Permitted to trade' because the master's demand for payment implies permission to trade by indication, but it is restricted to the assembly in the case of conditioning with 'in'. [2] 'It is restricted' means if he conditioned his freedom on payment with the word 'in', it is required that the payment occurs in that same assembly; he is freed by payment therein, not by payment after. If he conditioned it with 'idha' or 'mata', it is not restricted to the assembly because these words indicate generality of time. [3] 'And he can recover' means that if the slave pays from money he earned before the condition, the master can take it back because all that money belongs to the master, not from his earnings after the condition. [4] 'And he is freed in both cases' means the slave becomes free upon paying the money he conditioned, whether he pays from his previous earnings or his subsequent earnings, because the condition (payment of the specified money) is fulfilled. [0] 'And if he vacates...' The waw is conjunctive; this is brought to indicate that payment occurs by actual delivery (qabd) a fortiori, and the specification of vacating (takhliya) is to remove the misconception that the one whose freedom is conditioned on payment is not freed until actual payment occurs, which is not achieved by takhliya. (1) Because it is explicit in conditioning freedom on payment. He becomes permitted to trade because the master encourages him to earn by demanding payment from him, and his intent is trade not begging, so it becomes permission by indication; thus his selling is valid, and the slave is not entitled to his earnings, so the master can take from him without his consent, unlike the mukatib. Its completion is in Durar al-Hukkam (2:15). (2) Because it is not used for time like 'mata'. However, if he pays part of it, [he is not freed] by placing the money where the master can take it. And his statement 'and if he vacates' connects to his statement 'he is freed' meaning he is freed even if the payment is by way of takhliya: i.e., payment is achieved by takhliya. (He is not freed if he pays part of it) i.e., he is not freed if he pays part. [1] 'By placing' means the slave; summary: the master is considered a recipient by takhliya through removing obstacles, whether he takes it or not. (2) 'By way of takhliya': it is that he removes obstacles to reception and places the money before the master such that if he extended his hand he would take it; then the judge rules that he has taken possession. Similarly for the price of a sale, rental payment, and all rights. This implies that he is freed by actual possession a fortiori. This applies if the consideration is valid. But if it is invalid, such as wine or something grossly unknown, like if he said 'If you pay me wine or a garment, you are free,' then if he pays that, the master is not considered a recipient unless he takes it willingly. As in al-Bahr and al-Fath. [3] 'Is achieved by takhliya': Similarly, payment and subsequent freedom are achieved by takhliya in kitaba also according to the general [scholars]; but according to Zufar (may Allah have mercy on him), freedom in kitaba is not achieved by takhliya, but rather by actual possession. So this is another point of difference between the mukatib and one whose freedom is conditioned on payment: the mukatib is not freed by takhliya in his view, while the one whose freedom is conditioned on payment is freed. [4] 'He is not freed if he pays part of it': because the condition is payment of the whole, and when the condition is lost, the conditioned thing is lost. For this reason he is not freed if the master specified dirhams and the slave paid dinars, or specified a white bag and he paid a black one, or specified payment in this month and he paid in the next. And if the master reduces part at the slave's request and he pays the remainder, he is not freed because the condition on which freedom was conditioned is lost. Unlike the mukatib: if the master reduces some of the kitaba money and he pays the remainder, he is freed, because kitaba is a commutative contract and the money there is legally obligatory, so reduction is conceivable; here it is not.
Source pages p. 671

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya expounds the rulings of a slave whose freedom is conditioned on payment (العتق على جعل). The author explains that the slave becomes a 'madhun' (permitted to trade) by implication, because the master's demand for payment motivates him to earn through trade, not begging. A key distinction is made based on the particle used: if the condition is expressed with 'in' (إن), the payment must occur in the same assembly (majlis); if with 'idha' (إذا) or 'mata' (متى), the payment is not restricted to the session because these words indicate generality of time. The master can reclaim money earned by the slave before the condition, as that belongs to the master; but earnings after the condition are the slave's own. The slave is freed whether he pays from pre-condition or post-condition earnings, as long as the condition is fulfilled. A subtle point is that 'takhliya' (vacating obstacles and placing the money within the master's reach) constitutes constructive delivery (qabd hukmi), so the slave is freed even if the master has not physically taken the money. This is stated to preempt the misunderstanding that only actual physical payment counts. The passage also addresses partial payment: if only part is paid, the slave is not freed because the condition requires full payment. Similarly, if the master specifies a particular type of payment (dirhams, a specific bag, a specific month) and the slave pays something else, the condition is not met. Significantly, if the master reduces the amount at the slave's request and the slave pays the remainder, he is not freed—unlike a mukatib (slave under a kitaba contract), because kitaba is a commutative contract where reduction (hatt) is possible. Finally, a difference within the Hanafi school is noted: according to the general view (Abu Hanifa and others), a mukatib is also freed by takhliya; but according to Zufar, the mukatib is not freed by takhliya, only by actual possession. This is a point of intra-Hanafi dispute.

Key Terms
مأذون (mādhūn): A slave permitted by the master to engage in trade; here it arises by implication when the master demands payment as a condition for freedom.
تخلية (takhliya): The act of removing obstacles to possession and placing the money within the master's reach such that he can take it; constitutes constructive delivery (qabd hukmi).
مكاتب (mukatib): A slave who has entered into a kitaba contract (contract of manumission upon payment of a sum in installments).
إن (in): A conditional particle that, when used in conditioning freedom on payment, restricts the payment to the same assembly (majlis).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master says to his slave, 'If you pay me 100 dirhams in this session, you are free,' and the slave pays 100 dirhams in the next session, what is the ruling?
A) The slave is freed because the payment was made.
B) The slave is not freed because the payment was not made in the same session.
C) The slave is freed only if the master accepts it.
D) The slave becomes a mukatib.

Key Takeaway
Conditional manumission is valid upon full payment as per the precise terms; constructive delivery (takhliya) is legally sufficient.

Master Treated as Receiver in Conditional Manumission
Intra-Hanafi dispute on master's compulsion in conditional manumission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi majority position on conditional manumission with payment and distinguish it from Zufar's view, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
In conditional manumission, the master is compelled to accept full payment because the transaction combines a vow and an exchange.

This passage from al-Hidayah, as commented on in 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: can a master be forced to accept payment from a slave whose manumission is conditional on payment? The majority view, supported by Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, holds that the master is legally deemed a receiver (qābiḍ) upon full payment, ensuring the slave can achieve freedom. Zufar disagrees, arguing that it is a mere vow with no compulsion.

Guided Path
1
State the factual scenarios
Identify the two scenarios: full payment and partial payment. Note the ruling in each: freedom upon full payment, no freedom upon partial payment.
The master is legally treated as a receiver in both scenarios, but the condition for freedom is full payment.
2
Identify the majority Hanafi ruling
The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) holds that the master is compelled to accept full payment; if the slave brings the amount, the judge enforces acceptance and the slave is freed.
Compulsion is legal (tanzīl) not physical.
3
Identify Zufar's opposing view
Zufar argues the master cannot be compelled because the transaction is a pure vow (yamin) like an oath; no entitlement exists before the condition is fulfilled.
Zufar compares it to oaths where conditions are not binding before occurrence.
4
Analyse the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi response combines ta'liq (wording) and mu'awada (purpose). Initially it is treated as a suspension to protect the master; at fulfillment it becomes an exchange, obliging the master to accept.
This dual nature prevents deception of the slave and is analogous to kitabah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: under Zufar, the slave may never achieve freedom; under majority, the master must accept full payment, giving the slave a path to freedom.
The majority position is mufta bihi.

And Zufar said: 'He is not compelled to accept, and that is the analogy, because it is an act of a vow, since it is a suspension of manumission upon a condition verbally, and therefore it does not depend on the slave's acceptance, nor does it bear rescission, nor is there compulsion to fulfill the conditions of vows, because there is no entitlement before the existence of the condition, unlike kitabah because it is an exchange and the substitute therein is wajib.' And our argument: it is a suspension in view of the wording, and an exchange in view of the purpose, because he only suspended his manumission upon payment to motivate him to pay the money, so the slave attains the honor of freedom and the master attains the money in return, resembling kitabah; and therefore it was a substitute in divorce in such wording, such that it was bain. So we made it a suspension initially, acting on the wording, and to prevent harm to the master, so that his sale is not prevented, nor is the slave more entitled to his earnings, nor does it extend to the child born before payment. And we made it an exchange at the conclusion upon payment, to prevent deception of the slave, so that the master is compelled to accept. Upon this revolves fiqh and issues are derived.' [3] His saying: 'He only said this' meaning: the author only stated this, that the master is treated as a receiver in both situations, even if not freed in one of them. [4] His saying: 'he is not compelled' i.e. the master, and the meaning of not being compelled here is that he is not treated as a receiver merely by khaliyah, just as the meaning of compulsion to accept is that he is treated as a receiver, and it does not mean that the master is physically forced or the like. Thus in al-Binayah. End from al-Hidayah (5:6).
Source pages p. 673

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal status of the master in conditional manumission involving payment. The core issue is whether the master can be compelled to accept partial payment and whether he is considered a receiver (qabid) of the payment. The text opens by explaining that in the first scenario (full payment), the slave is freed, while in the second (partial payment), he is not, even though the master is treated as a receiver in both. This ruling is based on the principle that the money is a condition (shart) for freedom, not an obligatory payment. The author then quotes from al-Hidayah, stating that if the slave brings the full payment, the judge compels the master to accept and the slave is freed by virtue of the master being treated as a receiver through khaliyah (constructive possession). Zufar challenges this, arguing that it is purely a vow (yamin): the manumission is suspended on a condition like an oath, and in oaths, there is no compulsion to fulfill conditions before they occur. Furthermore, unlike kitabah (contract of manumission), this is not an exchange (mu'awada) requiring a substitute. The Hanafi response (Lana) synthesizes both views: the transaction is a suspension (ta'liq) in terms of wording but an exchange (mu'awada) in terms of purpose. Initially, it is treated as a suspension to protect the master's rights (e.g., he can sell the slave, the slave's earnings belong to the master, and it does not extend to children). However, upon eventual full payment, it is treated as an exchange, obliging the master to accept, otherwise the slave would be deceived. The passage concludes by clarifying that 'compulsion' does not mean physical force but legal treatment as a receiver. This ruling is foundational for many derived issues in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
تنزيل (tanzīl): Legally treating a person as if they have performed an act (here, receiving payment) even if not physically done, as a legal construct.
قابض (qābiḍ): One who takes possession (qabḍ) of an asset; here, the master is legally deemed to have received the payment through tanzīl.
تعليق (ta‘līq): Suspending a legal effect (like manumission) on a future condition; here, the manumission is suspended on payment.
معاوضة (mu‘āwaḍah): An exchange transaction where both parties give and receive countervalues; here, freedom for payment is analogous to a sale.
فصل (faṣl): A section or scenario; here, the two possible outcomes (full payment vs. partial payment) of the conditional manumission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The master must accept and the slave is freed proportionally.
B) The master is not compelled to accept, and the slave remains a slave.
C) The master is legally deemed a receiver, but the slave is not freed until full payment.
D) The slave is freed immediately upon any payment.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority treats conditional manumission as a hybrid of suspension and exchange, compelling the master to accept full payment and freeing the slave only upon full payment, with the master legally deemed a receiver in both scenarios.

Conditions for Valid Conditional Manumission After Death
Clarifying the conditions of acceptance after death and emancipation by the heir for validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions required for the validity of a conditional manumission that is suspended on the master's death with payment, and apply the analogy to distinguish it from tadbīr.

Core Idea
A slave's acceptance after death and the heir's emancipation are both required for conditional manumission by payment.

When a master declares 'You are free after my death for 1000 dirhams', the manumission is not automatic. The Hanafi school specifies that the slave must accept the offer after the master's death, and the heir must actually emancipate the slave. This lesson examines why these conditions exist and how they derive from legal principles, including an analogy to a future sale and a comparison with the contract of tadbīr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional statement
Recognize the master's declaration as a suspended manumission for payment. The structure is 'You are free' (ta'liq) + 'after my death' (future event) + 'for a thousand' (payment).
This is not a simple tadbīr, because it includes a payment.
2
Determine the timing of acceptance
Analyze why acceptance must occur after the master's death. Compare to 'You are free tomorrow for a thousand' – acceptance must be at the time when the contract takes effect, which is after death.
The idhāfa (addition) postpones the existence of the obligation to the future time.
3
Determine the necessity of heir's emancipation
Explain that at the moment of death, the slave enters the ownership of the heir. The condition for freedom cannot be fulfilled while the slave is in someone else's ownership; thus the heir must actively emancipate.
The executor or judge may step in if the heir refuses.
4
Distinguish from tadbīr
Note that in tadbīr, acceptance is immediate because the declaration creates a legal status (mudabbar) without payment. The payment in the conditional manumission makes it resemble a sale, requiring acceptance at the future time.
This distinction shows why acceptance timing differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And in 'You are free after my death for a thousand', if he accepts after his death and the heir emancipates him, he is freed; otherwise not. [1] His saying: 'if he accepts' i.e. the slave after the master's death. As for if he accepts before death, he is not freed, because it is like 'You are free tomorrow for a thousand', for the place of acceptance is tomorrow, since acceptance is only considered in its council, and its council is the time of its existence, and the idhafa postpones its existence to the existence of the thing added to. And here it is after death, unlike 'You are mudabbar for a thousand', for acceptance is required immediately, because the ijab of tadbir is immediate, because the money is not obligatory immediately due to the existence of slavery, and the master has no claim of debt against his slave nor after. The reason: here the emancipator is after death, and the slave at that time leaves the ownership of the master to the ownership of the heir, so the condition is not found except while he is in the ownership of another, so it is required that he also emancipate him. Source pages p. 674

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling for a specific type of conditional manumission: the master says 'You are free after my death for 1000 dirhams.' The validity of the manumission depends on two conditions: first, the slave must accept after the master's death (acceptance before death is ineffective, analogous to future sales where acceptance must be at the time the contract takes effect); second, the heir must perform the actual manumission, because at the moment of the master's death, the slave becomes part of the heir's property, and the heir's action is needed to effect the freedom. The text clarifies that acceptance after death is required, comparing it to a contract for future delivery. If the slave accepts before death, it is invalid because the contract's time has not arrived. This differs from tadbir (declaring a slave mudabbar, free after the master's death) where acceptance is immediate because the declaration is an immediate legal act. The commentary also discusses the role of the heir: if the heir refuses, the judge or executor can step in. Finally, the passage addresses the phrasing of the condition, noting that the addition 'bi al-mal al-madhkur' (by the mentioned money) is meaningful to indicate that the slave is not freed by that specific payment if the conditions of acceptance and heir's emancipation are not met. The footnotes add that wala (patronage) goes to the heir and is inherited by agnatic males, and the heir may even emancipate the slave gratuitously.

Key Terms
قبول (qabūl): Acceptance; here, the slave's expression of willingness to be freed in exchange for payment, which must occur after the master's death.
إعتاق الوارث (i‘tāq al-wārith): The act of the heir (or his substitute) emancipating the slave, which is a necessary condition for the manumission to take effect.
تدبير (tadbīr): A declaration that a slave will be free after the master's death; here distinguished from the conditional manumission for payment because acceptance is immediate in tadbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) At any time before the master's death.
C) After the master's death.
D) Acceptance is not required at all.

Key Takeaway
For a conditional manumission for payment after death, the slave must accept after death and the heir must emancipate; otherwise the manumission is invalid.

Conditions for Freedom in Conditional Manumission After Death
Ruling on conditional manumission with payment after death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for a slave's freedom in a conditional manumission after death and explain the effect of partial payment and the intra-Hanafi difference on the master's status as receiver.

Core Idea
Freedom requires both post-death acceptance and heir's manumission; partial payment never frees the slave.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya examines a specific case of conditional manumission (itq 'ala ja'l) where the master says 'You are free after my death for a thousand.' The text clarifies that the slave's freedom hinges on two conditions that must occur after the master's death: the slave's acceptance of the offer and the heir's actual manumission. It also addresses partial payment (takhliyah), introducing an intra-Hanafi difference on whether the master is considered a receiver of the paid portion. Understanding these rules is essential for correctly applying the school's position on suspended contracts of manumission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions for freedom
Locate in the text that freedom requires (1) the slave's acceptance after the master's death and (2) the heir's manumission. Note that acceptance before death is invalid, as the offer is tied to a future time.
The text compares this to "You are free tomorrow for a thousand" – acceptance must be in the future council.
2
Analyze the timing of acceptance
Understand why acceptance must be after death: the offer is suspended (mu'allaq) and only becomes effective when the condition (death) occurs. The slave's acceptance before death is like accepting a future promise, which is not a valid contract formation.
Contrast with tadbir (suspensive manumission) where acceptance is immediate because the offer is immediate.
3
Consider partial payment (takhliyah)
Examine the scenario where the slave pays only part of the promised amount. The text states that the preferred view (al-mukhtar) is that the master is considered a receiver (qabid) of that part, but the slave is not freed because full payment is a condition for freedom.
An alternative narration holds the master is not a receiver; the chosen view affirms receiver status but denies freedom.
4
Examine the three scenarios of missing conditions
The commentary lists three possibilities: (a) slave accepts but heir does not manumit, (b) slave does not accept but heir manumits, (c) neither accepts nor manumits. In all cases, the slave is not freed by the conditional contract; in scenario (b), the heir's manumission frees the slave independently (without the promised wealth).
The phrase 'he does not become free' always refers to freedom via the conditional offer, not by other means.
5
Apply the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify the difference in narrations: one says the master is not considered a receiver; the chosen view says he is. Both agree that partial payment does not effect freedom because full payment is a condition. The practical difference lies in whether the master can claim the paid portion – under the chosen view, he keeps it as partial payment.
The tarjih authority is not named in the text, but 'al-mukhtar' indicates the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي أنت حر بعد موتي بألف إن قبل بعد موته وأعتقه الوارث عتق وإلا فلا فعلى هذه الرواية إن أدَّى البعض بطريق التَّخلية لا يُنَزِّلُ المولى مَنْزلَةَ القابض، لكن المختار أنه يكون قابضاً ، لكنه لا يعتق؛ لأن شرط العتق أداء الكلّ ؛ فلا يعتق لهذا المعنى، لا لأنه لم يصر قابضاً، بل صار قابضاً للبعض.
( وفي أنت حر بعد موتي بألف ، إن قبل) بعد موته وأعتقهُ الوارث (٣) عُتِق (۱) وإلا فلا) أي لا يعتق بالمال المذكور (۳) ، وإنما قيدَتُ بهذا القيد ; لأنه قال : وإلا فلا ; أي إن لم يوجد المجموع، وهو القبول بعد الموت ، وإعتاق الوارث لا يعتق التخلية، كما أنه معنى الجبر على القبول، هو أنه ينزل قابضاً، وليس معناه أنه يجبر المولى عليه بالضرب أو نحوه. كذا في «البناية».
[١] قوله : إن قبل ; أي العبد بعد موت المولى، أما لو قبل قبل الموت لا يعتق ; لأنه مثل : أنت حرّ غداً لألف، فإنّ القبول محله الغد ; إذ القبول إنما يعتبر في مجلسه، ومجلسه وقت وجوده ، والإضافة تؤخّر وجوده إلى وجودِ المضاف إليه.
وهو هاهنا بعد الموت، بخلاف أنت مدبّر بألف، فإنّ القبول يشترط فيه في الحال ; لأنّ إيجاب التدبير في الحال ; لأنه لا يجب المال في الحال ; لقيام الرق، والمولى لا يستحق على عبده ديناً ولا بعده. كذا في «فتح القدير»(۳).
[٢] قوله : وأعتقه الوارث ; وكذا الوصي أو القاضي عند امتناع الوارث.
والوجه فيه : إن المعتق هاهنا بعد الموت، والعبد يخرج عند ذلك من ملك المولى إلى ملك الوارث ، فلم يوجد الشرط إلا وهو في ملك غيره، فيشترط أن يعتق هو أيضاً.
[٣] قوله : وإنما قيدت على صيغة المتكلّم يرد به بیان وجه زيادة قوله : بالمال المذكور.
(٤) قوله : لأنه قال ... الخ حاصله : إن المصنف قال : وإلا فلا ; أي وإن لم يوجد ما ذكر قبله وهو القبول بعد الموت وعنق الوارث لا ، فإن أريد به أنه لا يعتق عند
(۱) والولاء للوارث، فيرثه عصبته المتعصبون بأنفسهم دون الإناث، ولو كان الولاء للورثة ابتداءً لدخل فيه الإناث. ينظر : حاشية الطحطاوي (۲ : ۳۰۹).
(۲) وإن جاز أن يعتقه الوارث مجاناً. ينظر : (الدر المنتقى»(١ : ٥٣٠).
(۳) «فتح القدير (٥ : ١٢).
فقد مجموع الأمرين مطلقاً لم يصدق الكلام في إحدى الصورتين، فإن لعدم وجودِ المجموع صورتين، بل ثلاث صور :
إحداهما : أن يقبل بعد الموت ولا يعتقه الوارث، وحينئذ يصدق نفي العتق مطلقاً.
وثانيتها : أن لا يقبل بعد الموت ولا يعتق الوارث أيضاً، وحينئذ يصدق أيضاً نفي العتق.
وثالثتها : أن لا يقبل العبد بعد الموت ، لكن يعتقه الوارث، فحينئذ لا يصدق عليه أنه لا يعتق , نعـم يـصدق أن يقال : إنّه لا يعتق بالمال المذكور، بل يعتق بعتقِ الوارث بلا مال ، فلذا قيد الشارح عدم العتق بكونه بالمال المذكور، فإنه صادق في كلتا الصورتين، بل في الصور الثلاث.
[١] قوله : فحينئذ لا يعتق ; لما مرّ من أنّه انتقل عند موت المورث إلى ملك الوارث، فيشترط عتقه.
[٢) قوله : فيصدق ; لأنَّ نفي المطلق يستلزم نفي المقيد، فإذا صدق أنه لا يعتق مطلقاً صدق أنه لا يعتق بالمال المذكور أيضاً.
[٣] قوله : ما إذا لم يقبل بعد الموت ; سواء قبله قبل الموت، أو لم يقبل مطلقاً.
! 1 أي بلا بدل ،
[٤]قوله : ضرورة أنه يعتق مجاناً ; - بفتح الميم وتشديد الجيم . وفيه ما فيه، فإنّه يجوز أن يعتقه الوارث بأقل من ذلك المال أو بأكثر . منه ، فحينئذ لا يصدق أنه يعتق مجاناً.
And in 'You are free after my death for a thousand, if he accepts after his death and the heir manumits him, he becomes free, and if not, then not.' So according to this narration, if he pays part by way of freeing, the master does not place him in the position of the receiver, but the chosen view is that he is a receiver, but he does not become free because the condition for freedom is payment of the whole; so he does not become free for this reason, not because he did not become a receiver, but he became a receiver of part. (And in 'You are free after my death for a thousand, if he accepts) after his death and the heir manumits him (3) he becomes free (1) and if not, then not' meaning he does not become free with the mentioned wealth (3), and I restricted it with this restriction because he said: 'and if not, then not' meaning if the entirety is not found, which is acceptance after death and the heir's manumission, he does not become free by freeing, just as the meaning of compulsion to accept is that he is placed as a receiver, and it does not mean that he compels the master by beating or the like. Thus in 'al-Binaya'. [1] His saying: 'if he accepts' i.e., the slave after the master's death; as for if he accepted before death, he does not become free because it is like 'you are free tomorrow for a thousand'; indeed, the place of acceptance is tomorrow, since acceptance is only considered in its council, and its council is the time of its existence, and the addition delays its existence to the existence of the added-to. And it here is after death, unlike 'you are mudabbar for a thousand', because acceptance is required immediately because the offer of tadbir is immediate; since the wealth is not obligatory immediately due to the persistence of slavery, and the master does not deserve a debt from his slave nor after it. Thus in 'Fath al-Qadir'(3). [2] His saying: 'and the heir manumits him'; likewise the executor or the judge when the heir refuses. And the reason is that the manumitter here is after death, and the slave at that time leaves the master's ownership to the heir's ownership, so the condition was not found except while he is in the ownership of another, so it is required that he also manumits. [3] His saying: 'And I restricted' in the first person to express the reason for adding his saying 'with the mentioned wealth'. (4) His saying: 'because he said' ... the summary: that the author said: 'and if not, then not' meaning if what was mentioned before it is not found, which is acceptance after death and the heir's manumission no, so if it is meant that he does not become free at (1) and the wala is for the heir, his 'asaba who are agnates by themselves inherit him, not the females; and if the wala were initially for the heirs, the females would be included. See: Hashiyat al-Tahtawi (2:309). (2) Even if it is permissible for the heir to free him for free. See: al-Durr al-Muntaqa (1:530). (3) Fath al-Qadir (5:12). So the entirety of the two matters absolutely is lost; the statement is not true in one of the two pictures, because for the non-existence of the entirety there are two, rather three pictures: One: that he accepts after death and the heir does not free him, then the negation of freedom is true absolutely. Second: that he does not accept after death and the heir does not free him either, then the negation of freedom is also true. Third: that the slave does not accept after death, but the heir frees him, then it is not true that he does not become free; rather it is true to say that he does not become free with the mentioned wealth, but he becomes free by the heir's freeing without wealth, therefore the commentator restricted the negation of freedom to being with the mentioned wealth, for it is true in both pictures, rather in the three pictures. [1] His saying: 'then he does not become free' because of what passed that he transferred upon the death of the testator to the heir's ownership, so his manumission is required. [2] His saying: 'it is true' because the negation of the absolute necessitates the negation of the restricted; if it is true that he does not become free absolutely, it is true that he does not become free with the mentioned wealth also. [3] His saying: 'the case when he does not accept after death' whether he accepted before death or did not accept at all. '! 1' meaning without compensation. [4] His saying: 'necessarily he becomes free for free' - with fatha on the mim and shadda on the jim. And there is something in it, because it is permissible for the heir to free him for less than that wealth or more, then it is not true that he becomes free for free.
Source pages p. 674

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on conditional manumission (العِتْق على جعل) where the master says 'You are free after my death for a thousand'. The ruling is that the slave becomes free only if two conditions are met: (1) the slave accepts the offer after the master's death, and (2) the heir (or executor/judge) actually manumits him. If these are not both present, the slave is not freed with the mentioned wealth. The commentary clarifies that acceptance before death is ineffective because the offer is tied to a future time, like 'You are free tomorrow'. This differs from tadbir (suspensive manumission) where acceptance is immediate because the offer is immediate. The text also discusses the case where the slave pays only part of the amount: the preferred view (المختار) is that the master is considered a receiver of that part, but the slave is not freed because full payment is a condition for freedom. The commentary further explores scenarios regarding the lack of the two conditions, listing three possibilities and concluding that the statement 'he does not become free' is always true except when the heir frees him for free (without the wealth), in which case he is freed by the heir's act, not by the condition. The text emphasizes that the negation of freedom is specifically with respect to the mentioned wealth.

Key Terms
عتق على جعل (itq ‘ala ja’l): Manumission in exchange for a consideration (wealth or service) payable by the slave.
تخلية (takhliyah): Paying part of the consideration to free the slave, treating the master as if he accepted partial payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the conditional manumission 'You are free after my death for a thousand', when must the slave accept the offer?
A) Before the master's death
B) After the master's death
C) Either before or after death
D) Only at the moment of the master's death

Key Takeaway
Conditional manumission after death requires the slave's post-death acceptance and the heir's manumission; partial payment does not effect freedom.

Manumission in Exchange for Service: The Hanafi Contract
Definition and clarification of the manumission-for-service contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the Hanafi contract of manumission in exchange for service, identify the party obligated to serve, and differentiate it from other forms of manumission.

Core Idea
Freedom can be earned through a specified term of service—the slave serves, the master frees.

In this lesson, we examine a unique Hanafi contract: the master says, 'I free you on condition that you serve me (or so-and-so) for a year.' This creates a binding agreement where the slave earns manumission by performing the stipulated service. The commentary clarifies that the pronoun in 'on his service' refers to the slave himself—meaning the slave's service, not the master's. Understanding this contract highlights Hanafi flexibility in facilitating freedom through labor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract formulation
The master declares manumission conditional on service for a period (e.g., 'I free you on condition that you serve me for a year') or directs service to a third party ('on condition that you serve so-and-so for a year'). The contract is valid and binding.
The service term must be specified; otherwise it may be invalid due to uncertainty.
2
Determine who performs the service
The pronoun 'his' in 'on his service' refers to the slave—the slave is the agent (fā‘il) of the service. Thus, the obligation is on the slave to serve.
Some might mistakenly think 'his service' means the master's service, but the commentary corrects this: the slave serves.
3
Recognize the practical effect
Upon completion of the agreed service, the slave becomes free automatically. No additional manumission is needed. The contract is a form of 'itq 'ala khidma (manumission for service).
If the slave fails to serve without excuse, the contract may be voided, and the slave remains a slave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Source pages p. 675

Commentary
This passage introduces the ruling on manumission in exchange for service (العِتْق على خدمة). The main text states 'If he frees him on his service for a year'. The commentary then initially continues the previous discussion about the three scenarios of acceptance and heir manumission (likely a copyist or editor error, as it belongs to the previous lesson). The relevant commentary for this lesson begins at note [01], where the author explains that this refers to the master saying 'I freed you on condition that you serve me for a year', or 'on condition that you serve so-and-so for a year'. The pronoun in 'his service' (خدمته) refers back to the slave, so the service is performed by the slave (fā‘il). This clarifies that the service obligation is on the slave.

Key Terms
عتق على خدمة (itq ‘ala khidma): Manumission of a slave in exchange for a specified term of service to the master or a third party.
خدمته (khidmatuhu): Refers to the slave's service; the pronoun 'his' indicates the slave is the doer of the service.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The master
B) The slave
C) The heir
D) A third party

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi master may free a slave in return for a fixed term of service, which can be rendered to the master or a named third party; the slave becomes free upon completion.

Conditional Emancipation with Service: Immediate Freedom and Death of Master
Commentary on conditional emancipation with service and death of master; analysis of three post-death scenarios and intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional emancipation (al-‘itq ‘ala ja‘l), explain why the slave is freed immediately, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the master's death before service completion.

Core Idea
In conditional emancipation, acceptance frees immediately; service is a non-inheritable benefit, so heirs cannot demand service after master's death.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in the Book of Emancipation: a master frees his slave on condition of serving for a year. The Hanafi school holds that the slave is freed immediately upon acceptance, and the service becomes a binding obligation. The central legal question arises when the master dies before the service period is complete: does the slave owe the remaining service to the heirs, or must he pay his value? We will explore the Zahir al-Riwayah position and an intra-Hanafi difference with ‘Isa ibn Aban.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type and its effect
This is a contract (mu‘awada) requiring immediate exchange. The emancipation takes effect upon acceptance, not upon service completion. Note the distinction from a suspended condition (ta‘liq).
The acceptance must occur in the same session.
2
Understand the obligation of service
The service becomes wajib on the slave, but is it inheritable? This is the key point of dispute.
Service is a benefit (manfa‘a), not a monetary debt.
3
Note the master's death scenario
If the master dies before the service period ends, what is the slave's duty? The commentator discusses three possible post-death scenarios.
The slave may or may not have accepted after death; the heir may or may not have freed him.
4
Compare the two opinions
Zahir al-Riwayah (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): the slave pays his value (qima). ‘Isa ibn Aban: the heirs may demand the remaining service.
The dispute centers on whether service is inheritable like a debt.
5
Analyze the reasoning
Service is a manfa‘a, which is not inheritable. Also, people's capacity for service differs, making it impractical to inherit. Hence, value is due.
The Hanafi response to 'Isa ibn Aban's analogy with debt.
6
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is the Zahir al-Riwayah: the slave pays the value and is free.
This is confirmed in al-Bahr al-Raiq and other authoritative texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب العتاق الحلف بالعتق والعتق على جعل
ولو حرره على خدمته سنة
فيشمل ما إذا قبل بعد الموت، لكن الوارث لم يعتقه، فحينئذ لا يعتق، فيصدق أن يقال: لا يعتق بالمال المذكور، ويشمل ما إذا لم يقبل بعد الموت، ولكن الوارث أعتقه فحينئذ يصدق أيضاً: أنه لا يعتق بالمال المذكور، ولا يصدق أن يقال: إنه لا يعتق ضرورة أنه يعتق مجاناً.
ولو حرره على خدمته سنة
فقد مجموع الأمرين مطلقاً لم يصدق الكلام في إحدى الصورتين، فإن لعدم وجود المجموع صورتين، بل ثلاث صور: إحداهما: أن يقبل بعد الموت ولا يعتقه الوارث، وحينئذ يصدق نفي العتق. وثانيتها: أن لا يقبل بعد الموت ولا يعتق الوارث أيضاً، وحينئذ يصدق أيضاً نفي العتق. وثالثتها: أن لا يقبل العبد بعد الموت، لكن يعتقه الوارث، فحينئذ لا يصدق عليه أنه لا يعتق، نعم يصدق أن يقال: إنّه لا يعتق بالمال المذكور، بل يعتق بعتق الوارث بلا مال، فلذا قيد الشارح عدم العتق بكونه بالمال المذكور، فإنه صادق في كلتا الصورتين، بل في الصور الثلاث.
[١] قوله: فحينئذ لا يعتق؛ لما مرّ من أنّه انتقل عند موت المورث إلى ملك الوارث، فيشترط عتقه.
[٢] قوله: فيصدق؛ لأنَّ نفي المطلق يستلزم نفي المقيد، فإذا صدق أنه لا يعتق مطلقاً صدق أنه لا يعتق بالمال المذكور أيضاً.
[٣] قوله: ما إذا لم يقبل بعد الموت؛ سواء قبله قبل الموت، أو لم يقبل مطلقاً.
[٤] قوله: ضرورة أنه يعتق مجاناً؛ أي بلا بدل، بفتح الميم وتشديد الجيم. وفيه ما فيه، فإنّه يجوز أن يعتقه الوارث بأقل من ذلك المال أو بأكثر منه، فحينئذ لا يصدق أنه يعتق مجاناً.
[٠١] قوله: لو حرّره؛ أي حرَّر المولى العبد على خدمة العبد سنة مثلاً، كقوله: أعتقتك على أن تخدمني سنة، وكذا لو قال: على أن تخدم فلاناً سنة، وبهذا ظهر أنّ الضمير في خدمته راجع إلى العبد، فإضافة الخدمة إليه إضافة إلى الفاعل، ولو أرجع الضمير إلى المولى وجعلت الإضافة إلى المفعول لم يشتمل الكلام ما إذا حرره على خدمة غيره.
فقبل عتق، وخدَمَهُ مدته، فإن مات مولاه قبلها تجب قيمته فقبل عتق، وخدَمَهُ مدته: أي وجب عليه الخدمة عليه في المدة المذكورة، والضمير في مدته يرجع إلى العبد، أضاف المدة إليه بأدنى ملابسة: أي مدة ضربت له، ومدتها في نسخة بخط المصنف الله يعني مدة الخدمة، أي مدة ضربت للخدمة.
[٢] فإن مات مولاه قبلها: أي قبل المدة، تجب قيمته: أي قيمة العبد.
[١] قوله: عتق؛ أي في الحال؛ لأنَّ الإعتاق على الشيء يشترط فيه وجود القبول في المجلس، لا وجود المقبول كسائر العقود، بخلاف ما لو قال: لإن خدمتني سنة فأنت حر، فإنّه لا يعتق إلا بعد خدمة سنة؛ لوجود التعليق. كذا في «البحر».
[٢] قوله: والضمير...الخ؛ لما كان يرد هاهنا أن ضمير مدته راجع إلى الخدمة؛ لأنَّ المدة لا تضاف حقيقة إلا إلى المظروفات، فيقال: مدة الخدمة، ومدة العتق، ومدة الصلاة إلى غير ذلك مما وجه تذكير الضمير، أشار الشارح له إلى دفعِهِ بأَنَّ الضمير راجع إلى العبد والإضافة إليه لأدنى اتصال مناسبة، وقد يدفع الإيراد بعد تسليم أنَّ الضمير إلى الخدمة، بأن تأنيث المصدر، وما تاؤه ليست زائدة عليه لا يعتد به، فيذكر الضمير الراجع إليه كثيراً.
[٣] قوله: يعني مدة الخدمة؛ ويحتمل أن يرجع الضمير على تقدير تأنيثها إلى السنة.
[٤] قوله: فإن مات مولاه قبلها؛ وكذا الحكم إذا مات العبد قبل تمام الخدمة، أو كانت الخدمة التي جعلت عوضاً عن العتق مجهولة. كذا في «البحر» وغيره.
[٥] قوله: تجب قيمته؛ وعند عيسى بن أبان له يخدم ورثته ما بقي؛ لأنها دين فيخلفه وارثه فيه كما لو أعتقه على ألف فاستوفى بعضهما ومات. وفي ظاهر الرواية لا يخدمهم؛ لأنَّ الخدمة منفعة، وهي لا تورث، ولأنّ الناس يتفاوتون فيها. كذا في «البحر»
Book of Emancipation: Oath by emancipation and emancipation for a consideration. And if he frees him on condition of his service for a year... It includes the case where he accepts after death but the heir does not free him, then he is not freed, so it is true to say: he is not freed by the mentioned wealth. And it includes the case where he does not accept after death, but the heir frees him, then it is also true: that he is not freed by the mentioned wealth, but it is not true to say that he is not freed at all, because he is freed for free. And if he frees him on condition of his service for a year, the combination of both matters absolutely did not apply to the speech in one of the two forms, because the non-existence of the combination has two forms, rather three forms: One: that he accepts after death and the heir does not free him, and then the negation of emancipation is true. Second: that he does not accept after death and the heir also does not free him, and then the negation of emancipation is also true. Third: that the slave does not accept after death, but the heir frees him, then it is not true that he is not freed, yes it is true to say that he is not freed by the mentioned wealth, but he is freed by the emancipation of the heir without wealth, so the commentator restricted the negation of emancipation to being by the mentioned wealth, for it is true in both forms, rather in the three forms. [1] His saying: then he is not freed; because of what has passed that he transferred upon the death of the testator to the ownership of the heir, so his emancipation is conditional. [2] His saying: it is true; because the negation of the absolute necessitates the negation of the restricted, so if it is true that he is not freed absolutely, it is true that he is not freed by the mentioned wealth also. [3] His saying: the case where he does not accept after death; whether he accepted before death or did not accept at all. [4] His saying: necessarily that he is freed for free; i.e., without compensation, with fatha on the mim and tashdid on the jim. And there is something in it, for it is possible that the heir frees him for less than that wealth or more than it, then it is not true that he is freed for free. [01] His saying: if he frees him; i.e., the master freed the slave on condition of the slave's service for a year, for example, like his saying: I freed you on condition that you serve me for a year, and likewise if he said: on condition that you serve so-and-so for a year, and by this it is clear that the pronoun in 'his service' refers to the slave, so the addition of service to him is an addition to the agent, and if he referred the pronoun to the master and made the addition to the object, the speech would not include the case where he freed him on condition of the service of someone else. So he accepted, he is freed, and he served him for his period. Then if his master dies before it, his value becomes obligatory. So he accepted, he is freed, and he served him for his period: i.e., service became obligatory upon him in the mentioned period, and the pronoun in 'his period' refers to the slave, he added the period to him with the slightest connection: i.e., a period set for him, and 'her period' in a copy in the handwriting of the author may mean the period of service, i.e., a period set for the service. [2] Then if his master dies before it: i.e., before the period, his value becomes obligatory: i.e., the value of the slave. [1] His saying: he is freed; i.e., immediately; because freeing upon a thing requires the existence of acceptance in the session, not the existence of the accepted thing, like other contracts, contrary to if he said: if you serve me for a year then you are free, then he is not freed except after serving a year; because of the presence of a condition. Thus in 'al-Bahr'. [2] His saying: and the pronoun... etc.; because there occurs here that the pronoun of 'his period' refers to the service; because the period is not added in reality except to containers, so it is said: the period of service, and the period of freedom, and the period of prayer, etc., and the reason for the masculine pronoun, the commentator pointed to its rebuttal by that the pronoun refers to the slave and the addition to him is due to the slightest connection of appropriateness, and the objection may be rebutted after admitting that the pronoun refers to the service, by that the masdar is feminine, and its ta is not extra upon it so it is not considered, so the pronoun referring to it is often masculine. [3] His saying: meaning the period of service; and it is possible that the pronoun on the assumption of its femininity refers to the year. [4] His saying: then if his master dies before it; and likewise the ruling if the slave dies before the completion of the service, or if the service which was made as a countervalue for emancipation was unknown. Thus in 'al-Bahr' and others. [5] His saying: his value becomes obligatory; and according to 'Isa ibn Aban, he serves his heirs for what remains; because it is a debt, so his heir succeeds him in it, as if he freed him for a thousand and collected some of it and died. And in the apparent narration, he does not serve them; because service is a benefit, and it is not inherited, and because people differ in it. Thus in 'al-Bahr'.
Source pages p. 675

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya deals with a specific form of conditional emancipation (al-'itq 'ala ja'l). The scenario is: a master says to his slave 'I free you on condition that you serve me for one year' (or serve another). The slave accepts in the same session. The ruling is that the slave is freed immediately upon acceptance, not after completing the service. This is because this is a contract (mu'awada) that requires immediate exchange of offer and acceptance. The service then becomes a binding obligation (wajib) on the slave. The commentary discusses three possible scenarios after the master's death: (1) the slave accepts after death but the heir does not free him – the slave is not freed; (2) the slave does not accept after death and the heir does not free him – again not freed; (3) the slave does not accept but the heir frees him – the slave is freed but not by the original contract, but by the heir's own act. The author then clarifies that the negation of freedom 'by the mentioned wealth' applies in all three cases. The commentary then addresses linguistic points: the pronoun in 'his service' and 'his period' refers to the slave. Finally, a dispute is reported: According to the Zahir al-Riwayah (the relied-upon position of Abu Hanifa and his students), if the master dies before the service period ends, the slave's value becomes due (i.e., he must pay the market value to the heirs) and he does not serve the heirs. 'Isa ibn Aban differs, holding that the service is a debt, so the heirs can demand the remaining service. The Hanafi authorities argue that service (manfa'a) is not inheritable because it is a personal benefit and people's abilities differ. Therefore, the correct position is the Zahir al-Riwayah: the slave pays the value, not serve.

Key Terms
عتق ('itq): Emancipation of a slave, freeing from the state of slavery.
خدمة (khidma): Service; in this context, a condition attached to emancipation.
قيمة (qima): Market value; the amount to be paid if the service period is not completed.
عيسى بن أبان ('Isa ibn Aban): A Hanafi scholar known for some differing opinions within the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah, if a master frees his slave on condition of service for a year and dies before the year is complete, what is the ruling?
A) The slave must complete the service for the heirs.
B) The slave is free and no payment is due.
C) The slave's value must be paid.
D) The emancipation is void.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, emancipation for a consideration frees immediately; service is a non-inheritable benefit, so upon the master's death the slave pays his value, not serve the heirs.

10 min
Master Dies Before Slave Completes Service: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on compensation after voided service condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on compensation when a master dies before a slave completes service as a condition for freedom, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf based on the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
When the service condition voids due to master's death, the slave must pay compensation – either his own value or the service value.

In a contract of manumission for a consideration (‘itq ‘alā ja‘l), the slave is freed immediately but owes the agreed service. If the master dies before the service is completed, the service becomes impossible because benefits are not inheritable in the Hanafi school. This leads to an important intra-Hanafi dispute: what should the slave compensate – his own market value (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) or merely the value of the remaining service (Muhammad al-Shaybani)? The practical difference can be huge, and the later preferred view (mufta bihi) is Muhammad’s. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the methodological debate on whether this issue is built (binā’) on another similar case or merely analogous (tashbīh).

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type
Recognize that ‘itq ‘alā ja‘l is a contract of exchange: the slave becomes free immediately in exchange for a specified service. The service is like a debt, but it is a benefit (manfa‘ah) not a physical asset.
Contrast with suspended manumission (ta‘līq) where freedom depends on completion of service.
2
State the event and the problem
The master dies before the service is finished. The service was for the master personally; after his death, it cannot be performed for him. What does the slave owe?
Also note that if the slave dies, a similar issue arises with his estate.
3
Lay out the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the slave owes his full market value (qīmat nafsihi). Muhammad: the slave owes only the value of the remaining service (qīmat al-khidmah). Excerpt from the passage: 'وعند محمد له قيمة خدمته'.
If partial service was done, the amounts are prorated.
4
Analyze the reasoning (talīl)
The two imams argue that the service was a benefit tied to the master's person, not inheritable; upon death the obligation is void, so compensation is based on the value of freedom. Muhammad analogizes to the case where a slave buys himself for a specific slave girl: if the girl is lost, the slave owes her value, not his own. Here the service is like the slave girl.
This analogy is the basis of the building (binā’) claim in al-Hidayah.
5
Evaluate the methodological critique
The commentator of al-Fath rejects the building (binā’) as arbitrary; al-Wiqayah used 'tashbīh' (similarity) instead. Understand that the two issues may be independently derived, and the tarjīh (preference) for Muhammad’s view is not based on that analogy alone but on later authority.
The mufta bihi is Muhammad’s view, as recorded in al-Jami‘ al-Qudsi.

Book of Manumission: Swearing by Manumission and Manumission for a Consideration
And according to Muhammad, he owes the value of his service, like the sale of a slave from himself.
[And according to Muhammad, he owes the value of his service, like the sale of a slave from himself. 677
In 'Al-Binayah': 'Explanation of the issue as stated in 'Sharh al-Tahawi': If he said to his slave: "You are free on condition that you serve me for four years", then if the master dies before the service, the service is void because the condition of service is for the master and the master has died. So according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, he owes the value of himself, and according to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, he owes the value of service for four years.
If he had served for one year and then died, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): three-quarters of his own value, and according to Muhammad: he owes the value of service for three years. Similarly, if the slave dies and leaves wealth, it is taken from his wealth to pay the value of himself according to the two, and according to Muhammad, to pay the value of the service." [1] His saying: 'like the sale...' etc.; It is mentioned in 'Al-Hidayah': 'Indeed, the difference is based on another difference, which is that if a person sold himself (the slave) for a specific slave girl, then the slave girl is reclaimed or perishes, the master claims from the slave the value of himself according to the two, and the value of the slave girl according to him, and this is well known. The basis for the building is: just as delivery of the slave girl becomes impossible due to destruction or claim, so delivery of the service becomes impossible due to the death of the slave, and similarly due to the death of the master, so it became parallel to it.' End. This statement, as you see, indicates that the difference in our issue is built upon the difference in that issue, and no sound basis for it is apparent. Therefore, it was said in 'Al-Fath': 'It is not hidden that building this on that is not more appropriate than the opposite; rather, the difference in both is originally independent.' End. Hence, the author (of 'Al-Wiqayah') omitted the mention of building and sufficed with analogy and similarity, indicating that the difference in our issue resembles the difference in the issue of a slave selling himself for a slave girl. And the commentator (of 'Al-Hidayah') did not contemplate the author's change of his wording from the building mentioned in 'Al-Hidayah' to mere similarity, so he interpreted his words by mentioning the building. This is not the first time his glass has been broken; rather, he often does not...
Source pages p. 676

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, a commentary on Sharh al-Wiqayah, discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling when a master dies before a slave completes a service that was a condition for his freedom. The case is: a master says to his slave, 'You are free on condition that you serve me for four years.' The slave is freed immediately upon acceptance in the session (since it is a conditional contract, not a suspended condition), but he owes the service. If the master dies before the service is completed, what does the slave owe? Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the slave owes the full value of himself (qimat nafsihi), because the service was a benefit for the master personally, and upon his death, the service becomes impossible since benefits are not inheritable. Thus, the slave must compensate by paying his own market value. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the slave owes only the value of the remaining service (qimat al-khidmah), analogizing this to the case where a slave buys himself from his master in exchange for a specific slave girl: if that slave girl is lost or reclaimed, the slave owes the value of the slave girl (not his own value). Similarly, here the service is like the consideration, so its value is owed. The commentator notes that this difference is built on another disagreement: in the case of a slave buying himself for a slave girl, the two imams say the master claims the slave's own value upon loss of the girl, while Muhammad says the value of the girl applies. The author of al-Hidayah presented this as a building of one issue on another, but the commentator of al-Fath criticizes that view, stating the differences are independent. The author of al-Wiqayah (the matn) wisely omitted the building and just gave an analogy. The commentator of al-Hidayah, however, missed this subtlety and continued to mention the building. The passage also notes that if the slave had already served part of the term (e.g., one year) before the master's death, then according to the two, he owes three-quarters of his own value (since one year is done), and according to Muhammad, he owes three-quarters of the service value. Similarly, if the slave dies, his estate pays accordingly. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in later Hanafi works is Muhammad's view, as stated in al-Jami' al-Qudsi and affirmed by later authorities.

Key Terms
عتق على جعل (‘itq ‘alā ja‘l): Manumission in exchange for a consideration (money or service) to be paid by the slave.
قيمة نفسه (qīmat nafsihi): The market value of the slave himself, i.e., the price he would fetch if sold.
قيمة الخدمة (qīmat al-khidmah): The monetary value of the service that was agreed upon as the consideration for freedom.
بناء (binā’): Building one legal ruling on another, i.e., deriving the ruling here from a similar ruling in another case.
تشبيه (tashbīh): Analogy or similarity, less than strict qiyas; suggesting resemblance without claiming direct derivation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, if a master says to his slave 'You are free on condition that you serve me for four years' and the master dies after one year, what does the slave owe?
A) The value of himself (qimat nafsihi) in full
B) Three-quarters of the value of himself
C) The value of three years of service
D) Nothing, because the condition is void

Key Takeaway
In 'itq 'ala ja'l, if the master dies before service completion, the mufta bihi Hanafi position is that the slave owes only the value of the remaining service, not his own market value.

intermediate

Compensation for Unfulfilled Service Upon Master's Death
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation for impossible service

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding compensation when a conditional emancipation's service becomes impossible due to the master's death, and explain the underlying legal reasoning based on the nature of the substitute.

Core Idea
When service for freedom becomes impossible, do you pay the slave's value or the service's value? The answer hinges on whether service is a substitute for the slave or for manumission.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute that arises when a master frees his slave on condition of service for a fixed term, but the master dies before the service is rendered. The condition becomes void, but the slave has already received his freedom. What must he pay? The two leading positions within the school differ, and their reasoning reveals a fundamental question about the legal nature of the service condition. We will also examine how this dispute is connected (or not) to a similar case involving a slave buying himself with a specific commodity.

Guided Path
1
State the Case
Master says 'You are free on condition that you serve me for four years.' Master dies before any service. The service condition is void because it was personal to the master. Now, the slave is free but must compensate the master's estate.
The compensation is not a penalty but a substitute for the unfulfilled condition.
2
Identify the Two Positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two imams): the slave pays the full value of himself (qimat nafsihi). Muhammad al-Shaybani: the slave pays the value of the service (qimat al-khidma).
The amount differs: the slave's value is usually higher than the service value for a few years.
3
Trace the Reasoning: The Substitute Framework
According to the two imams, the service is a substitute (badal) for the slave himself. When service becomes impossible, the original subject (the slave) should be returned, but since manumission is irrevocable, his value is paid. According to Muhammad, the service is a substitute for manumission, which is not property; so when service is impossible, its value is paid.
This difference stems from whether the service is seen as compensation for the slave's person or for the act of freeing.
4
Identify the Parallel Case and the Building Claim
A parallel case: a slave buys himself from his master for a specific commodity (e.g., a jariyah). If that commodity perishes, the two imams say the slave pays his own value; Muhammad says he pays the commodity's value. Al-Hidayah states that the service dispute is built on this commodity dispute. However, al-Fath criticizes this, arguing the disputes are independent.
The author of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah (our text) deliberately avoids claiming a building and instead uses analogy, indicating he sides with al-Fath.
5
Evaluate the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the late Hanafi school is the view of Muhammad al-Shaybani, i.e., the slave pays the value of the service. This is consistent with the principle of charity to the slave and ease of calculation.
This is confirmed in later fatwa collections.

وأما في المبني عليه فوجه قول محمد الله : إنّ هذا بدل ما ليس بمال وهو العتق ؛ لأن بيع العبد من نفسه إعتاق، وقد عجز عن إيفاء البدل، وليس للمبدل وهو العتقِ قيمة، فتجب قيمة البدل.

So remember this, for it is from the incidents of the time. [2] His statement: 'building... etc.'; he said in al-Inaya: 'The aspect of Muhammad's statement: the service is a substitute for what is not property, which is manumission, and there is no value for manumission, and inability to deliver the service has occurred, so it is necessary to deliver its value. And the aspect of their statement: the service is a substitute for property because it is a substitute for the slave himself, but when the substitute could not be delivered, it is necessary to deliver the substituted thing which is the slave, but it cannot be delivered because manumission does not accept rescission, so it is necessary to deliver his value due to the possibility of that. This is in the building upon. As for the building upon it, the aspect of Muhammad's statement: this is a substitute for what is not property, which is manumission, because selling the slave from himself is manumission, and he was unable to fulfill the substitute, and the substituted thing, i.e., manumission, has no value, so the value of the substitute becomes due. And the aspect of their statement: the slave girl is a substitute for the slave himself by manumission, so it is necessary to deliver his value, just as if they exchanged a slave for a slave girl, then the slave died, and they rescinded the sale of the slave for the slave girl, the value of the slave is incumbent upon him.' End. [3] His statement: 'I sold yourself from you'; he indicated by it the addition of the sale to the slave in the author's statement 'like the sale of a slave from himself', addition to the object, and its subject is the master, and the pronoun 'him' refers to the slave. [4] His statement: 'so the commodity perished'; real perishing or legal perishing, as if that commodity is claimed, i.e., another claims that it is his property, so he takes it from the hand of the slave buyer. [1] His statement: 'it becomes due'; i.e., it becomes due upon the slave who bought himself from his master when he is unable to deliver

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the case of a conditional emancipation where the master says to his slave: 'You are free on condition that you serve me for four years.' If the master dies before the service period begins, the condition is void because it was personal to the master. The disagreement among the Hanafi imams is about what the slave must pay as compensation. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two), the slave must pay the full value of himself (qimat nafsihi). According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, the slave pays the value of the service for the remaining years (here four years). The passage then extends the same logic to cases where the slave dies after serving some years, or where the slave dies leaving property: the two imams require payment of the slave's value, while Muhammad requires payment of the service value. The author of this commentary (from al-Binaya) notes that this dispute is built upon another well-known dispute: if a slave buys himself from his master by means of a specific commodity (e.g., a jariyah), and that commodity perishes or is claimed by a third party, then according to the two imams, the slave owes the value of himself, but according to Muhammad, he owes the value of that specific commodity. The author reports that al-Marghinani (in al-Hidayah) explicitly states that the one case is built upon the other, but the author of al-Fath criticizes this as arbitrary, stating that the dispute in both is independent. Consequently, the author of this commentary (the one who wrote 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah) notes that the original author (as-Suyuti?) merely presented an analogy (tashbih) without claiming a direct building. The commentator (sharh) here tried to explain the author's words by mentioning the building from al-Hidayah, but he missed the author's subtle change. The passage then gives the detailed reasoning from al-'Inayah for both positions: Muhammad views the service as a substitute for manumission itself (which is not a financial value), so when the service is impossible, you pay the value of the service. The two imams view the service as a substitute for the slave himself, so when service is impossible, you revert to the original subject (the slave) and since the slave cannot be returned (manumission is irrevocable), you pay his value. Similarly for the base case: the two imams see the commodity as substitute for the slave himself; Muhammad sees it as substitute for manumission. The passage ends with clarifications: 'bel-ayn' means a specific commodity, not cash; 'perishing' includes legal perishing (e.g., third-party claim).

Key Terms
قيمة نفسه (qīmat nafsihi): The monetary value of the slave himself as a human commodity.
قيمة الخدمة (qīmat al-khidma): The estimated monetary value of the service that was conditionally required.
عتق على جعل (itq 'ala ja'l): Emancipation for a consideration or fee (e.g., the slave pays or renders service to gain freedom).
بنا (bina): Building (one ruling upon another); the claim that the dispute in the service case is built on the dispute in the commodity case.
تشبيه (tashbih): Analogy; the author of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah uses this term instead of 'building' to indicate resemblance without necessary dependency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a master says to his slave 'You are free on condition that you serve me for four years' and then the master dies before any service is rendered, what compensation does Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani require from the slave?
A) The full value of the slave (qimat nafsihi)
B) A third of the slave's value
C) The value of the service for four years (qimat khidmat arba' sinin)
D) Nothing, because the service becomes void

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's internal disagreement on compensation for impossible service reveals a deeper question: is the service a substitute for the slave's person or for manumission?
