Dispute over Compensation When Slave-Girl Refuses Marriage After Manumission
Presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation amount

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the compensation owed by a freed slave-girl who refuses marriage, and explain the qiyas used by each side.

Core Idea
When a slave-girl freed on condition of marriage refuses, the Sahibayn say she pays her own value; Muhammad says she pays the value of the promised item.

This passage delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a manumission contract conditioned on marriage. According to the majority of the school (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the freed slave-girl is liable for her own value if she declines the marriage. Imam Muhammad, however, argues that she must compensate the value of the specific item promised as the substitute. Understanding this disagreement requires careful analysis of the nature of manumission and its analogy to barter exchanges.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
A man says to the owner of a slave-girl: 'Free her for a thousand on condition that you marry her to me.' The owner frees her, but she refuses marriage. The commander owes nothing.
The commander is the one who made the offer.
2
Isolate the point of divergence
Although both sides agree that the slave-girl must compensate, they disagree on the measure: Muhammad says she pays the value of the specific item (qimat al-'ayn); the Sahibayn say she pays her own value (qimat nafsiha).
The 'ayn is the specific property promised as replacement.
3
Analyze Muhammad's dalil
Muhammad argues that the 'ayn is a substitute for manumission, which is not property (mal). Since manumission has no monetary value, the 'ayn itself must be returned or its value paid.
Manumission is seen as a non-proprietary act.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's dalil
The Sahibayn analogize to a barter sale (muqayada): if a slave is sold for a slave-girl and the slave dies, then rescission requires paying the value of the slave. Here, the 'ayn was a substitute for the slave herself, so she pays her own value.
The qiyas is based on treating the manumission condition as a counter-exchange.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference is the amount owed. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position according to Al-Hidayah is the view of the Sahibayn: she pays her own value.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي : أعتقها بألف على أن تزوجنيها ، إن فعل وأبت عتقت ولا شيء على آمره محمد له قيمة العين ؛ لتعذر الوصول إلى البدل هاهنا، كما في تلكِ الصورة، وإنما تجب قيمة العين عنده ؛ لأن العين بدلُ شيءٍ ليس بمال وهو العتق ، والعتق لا قيمة له فتجب قيمة العين.
ولهما : إن العين بدلُ نفس العبد، فصار كما إذا باع عبداً بجارية، فمات العبد ، ثُمَّ فسخا العقد في الجارية، تُحِبُّ قيمة العبد. ( وفي : أعتقها بألف على أن تزوجنيها ، إن فعل وأبت عُتِقَتْ ولا شيء علی آمره) العين التي جعلها عوضاً أن يؤدّي إليه قيمة نفسه عندهما، وعند محمد له يؤدّي إليه قيمة تلك العين التي جعلها عوضاً، وعجز عن تسليمها.
وهو
قوله : لتعذر؛ بيان لوجه البناء، ومتعلّق به، يعني: تعذر الوصول إلى البدل، الخدمة فيما نحن فيه بموتِ المولى، كما تعذر الوصول إلى البدل هو العين في تلك المسألة بهلاكها، وأنت تعلم أنَّ هذا القدر لا يكفي لإثبات البنائية، كما ذكرنا سابقاً. قوله : كما إذا باع عبداً بجارية ؛ هذا البيعُ يُسمى بيع المقايضة، وهو الذي يكون الثمن والمثمن كلاهما فيه غير النقود، وفي مثله يكون كل منهما بيعاً من وجه ، وثمناً من وجه. قوله : بألف على أن...الخ ؛ ذكر في بعض الكتب لفظ : علي، قبل : على الجارة، وهو الأظهر ؛ ليفيد وجوب الألف على الألف صراحة. قوله : وأبت ؛ أي أنكرت الأمة التزوج بذلك الأمر ولا تجبر عليه ؛ لأنها صارت مالكة نفسها، فلها الاختيار.
قوله : ولا شيء على آمره ؛ قال في «الهداية»: «لأن من قال لغيره : اعتق عبدك بألف علي ففعل، لا يلزمه شيء، ويقع العتق عن المأمور، بخلاف ما إذا قال لغيره : طلق امرأتك على ألف درهم علي ففعل، حيث يجب الألف على الآمر ؛ لأنَّ اشتراط البدل على الأجنبي في الطلاق جائز ، وفي العتاق لا يجوز». انتهى من الهداية (٥ : ١٦).
And [the ruling]: If he frees her for a thousand on condition that she marry him, and he does so and she refuses, she is freed and there is nothing upon the commander. According to Muhammad, she owes the value of the specific thing because it is impossible to reach the substitute here, as in that scenario. And the value of the specific thing is obligatory according to him because the specific thing is a substitute for something that is not property, and that is manumission, and manumission has no value, so the value of the specific thing is obligatory. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): The specific thing is a substitute for the slave himself, so it becomes like if he sold a slave for a slave-girl, then the slave died, then they rescinded the contract regarding the slave-girl, he is required to pay the value of the slave. And [the ruling]: If he frees her for a thousand on condition that she marry him, then he does so and she refuses, she is freed and there is nothing upon the commander. The specific thing that he made as compensation, he should pay to him the value of himself according to them (the two), and according to Muhammad he should pay to him the value of that specific thing which he made as compensation, and he is unable to deliver them.
His saying: 'Due to impossibility' is an explanation of the basis, and is related to it, meaning: the impossibility of reaching the substitute, the service in our case by the death of the master, just as the impossibility of reaching the substitute is the specific thing in that case by its destruction. And you know that this amount is not sufficient to prove the baseness, as we mentioned previously.
His saying: 'Just as if he sold a slave for a slave-girl' – this sale is called barter sale, in which both the price and the commodity are non-monetary, and in such each is a sale from one aspect and a price from one aspect.
His saying: 'For a thousand on condition that...' etc. – Some books mention the word 'علي' before 'على' as a preposition, and that is more apparent because it indicates the obligation of the thousand upon the commander explicitly.
His saying: 'And she refuses' – meaning the slave-girl refuses marriage to that commander and she is not compelled because she has become the owner of herself, so she has the choice.
His saying: 'And there is nothing upon the commander' – He said in Al-Hidayah: 'Because whoever says to another: Free your slave for a thousand upon me, and he does so, nothing is obligatory upon him, and the manumission takes place on behalf of the commanded. Unlike if he says to another: Divorce your wife for a thousand dirhams upon me, and he does so, then the thousand is obligatory upon the commander because stipulating a substitute upon a third party in divorce is permissible, while in manumission it is not permissible.' End from Al-Hidayah (5:16).
Source pages p. 679

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani on one hand, and Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf (the Sahibayn) on the other, regarding a man who says to the owner of a slave-girl: 'Free her for a thousand on condition that you marry her to me.' The owner frees her, but the slave-girl refuses marriage. According to Imam Muhammad, the slave-girl must pay the value of the specific thing (qimat al-'ayn) that was promised, because the substitute (the thousand) cannot be reached from the commander since it was not validly stipulated on him. According to the Sahibayn, the slave-girl must pay the value of herself (qimat nafsiha), because the specific thing is a substitute for the slave herself. They draw an analogy (qiyas) with a barter sale where if a slave is sold for a slave-girl and the slave dies, then the contract is rescinded, the buyer must pay the value of the slave. The commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the reasoning behind the impossibility clause and includes a quotation from Al-Hidayah distinguishing between manumission and divorce: in divorce, stipulating a substitute on a third party is valid so the commander pays; in manumission, it is invalid so the commander owes nothing. This highlights that manumission involves strengthening the slave, akin to a counter-exchange, whereas divorce is a pure release.

Key Terms
العين (al-'ayn): The specific physical object or property stipulated as compensation in the manumission contract.
القيمة (al-qima): Monetary value or compensation assessed as equivalent to something.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, if a slave-girl refuses marriage after being freed on condition, what must she pay?
A) The value of herself
B) The value of the specific item
C) Nothing
D) The entire thousand

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a slave-girl freed on condition of marriage refuses, she must compensate; the Sahibayn hold she pays her own value, while Muhammad holds she pays the value of the promised replacement.

Adding 'On My Behalf' in Conditional Manumission
Ruling when 'on my behalf' is added to conditional manumission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when the commander adds 'on my behalf' and distinguish it from the case without that addition.

Core Idea
Adding 'on my behalf' turns the command into an implied purchase, splitting the promised sum.

Previously, we learned that if a commander says 'Free your slave-girl for a thousand on condition you marry her to me' and she refuses marriage, the commander owes nothing. But what if he adds 'on my behalf'? The ruling changes dramatically. This lesson explores that variation and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scenarios
Distinguish the case without 'on my behalf' (commander owes nothing) from the case with it (commander must pay the value share).
The key difference is the addition of the word عنّي.
2
Understand the Implication of Purchase
Adding 'on my behalf' implies the commander is first purchasing the slave-girl and then ordering her manumission as his agent.
The commander's speech is interpreted as: 'Sell your slave-girl to me for a thousand, then free her on my behalf.'
3
Explain the Division of the Thousand
The thousand is split between the value of the slave-girl (purchase price) and her dower (marriage consideration). Since marriage did not occur, the dower share is not due; only the value share must be paid.
The division is based on the two counter-values: the price of the slave and the right to marry her.
4
Appreciate the Distinction from Khul'
The passage contrasts with khul' (divorce by payment) where a condition on a third party is valid, but in manumission it is not because manumission involves granting legal capacity akin to a sale.
Al-'Ayni's commentary clarifies the conceptual difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ضم: عنِّي ؛ قسم الألفُ على قيمتها ومهرها، وتجب حصة القيمة أي قال رجل لآخر: أعتق أمتك بألف علي بشرط أن تُزوجنيها، فأعتقها المولى، وأبت الجارية التزوج ، فلا شيء على الأمر ؛ لأنَّ اشتراط البدل على الغير لا يجوز في العتق.
(ولو ضم : عنِّي ؛ قسم الألفُ على قيمتها ومهرها، وتجب حصة القيمة) وقال العيني في «البناية»: «لأنَّ اشتراط البدل على المرأة في الخلع مشروع من غير أنَّ يُسلّم لها شيء ؛ لأنَّ الخُلعَ إسقاط محض ، فلما جاز على المرأة من دون سلامة شيء لها جاز على الأجنبي كذلك. بخلاف الإعتاق ؛ فإنّ فيه معنى الإثبات، وإن كان هو إزالة الملك ؛ لأنَّ به تحصل للعبد قوة حكميّة لم تكن ثابتة قبل الإعتاق، فكان في معنى المعاوضة، واشتراط العوض لا يجوز على غير من يسلم المعوض فلا يجب على الأجنبي شيء؛ لأنه لم يسلّم له شيء بهذا الضمان»(۱).
قوله : لآخر ؛ المراد به مولى أمة.
قوله : بشرط ؛ أشار به إلى أنَّ «على» في قوله : «على أن تزوجنيها» للشرط لا للعوض، فإنّ العوض إنما هو الألف.
قوله : فلا شيء ؛ أي لا يجب على الأمر أداء الألفُ الذي شرطه على نفسه في جملة أمره. 
قوله : ولــوضـم عـني ...الخ ؛ أي لو زادَ الآمر في جملة أمره كلمة : عني، فقال : أعتق أمتك عني بألف على أن تزوّجنيها فأعتقها المولى وأبت الأمة التزوج به ، فحينئذ يقسم الألف على قيمة الجارية ومهر مثلها، ويجب على الأمر أداء حصة القيمة إلى المولى ؛ وذلك لأنه لَمَّا قال عنّي تضمّن الشراء اقتضاء ، فكأنه قال : بع أمتك مني بألف ثم كن وكيلي في إعتاقها عنّي ، وذلك لظهور عدمِ تصوّر عتق أمة رجل عن آخر، فكلامه يقتضي اعتبار البيع والشراء وترتب الإعتاق عليه. ومن المعلوم أن الأمر قد قابل الألف بعوض الرقبة شراء، وبالبضع نكاحاً، ذكر أمرين، فينقسم الألف عليهما بالضرورة ، ولما لم يحصل له البضع لإباء الجارية حيث (۱) انتهى من البناية (٥ : ١٢٠ - ١٢١).
And if he adds: 'on my behalf' – the thousand is divided between its value and its dower, and the share of the value is obligatory. That is, a man said to another: Free your slave-girl for a thousand upon me, on condition that you marry her to me, so the master freed her, and the slave-girl refused marriage, then there is nothing upon the commander because stipulating a substitute upon a third party is not permissible in manumission. (And if he adds: 'on my behalf' – the thousand is divided between its value and its dower, and the share of the value is obligatory). And Al-'Ayni said in Al-Binayah: 'Because stipulating a substitute upon the woman in khul' is legislated without anything being surrendered to her; because khul' is pure relinquishment, so when it is permissible upon the woman without anything being surrendered to her, it is permissible upon a third party likewise. Unlike manumission, for it contains the meaning of affirmation, even though it is removal of ownership, because by it the slave acquires a legal strength that was not present before manumission, so it is in the meaning of a counter-exchange, and stipulating a substitute is not permissible upon one who does not surrender the object of exchange, so nothing is obligatory upon the third party because nothing has been surrendered to him by this guarantee.' His saying: 'To another' – meaning the owner of the slave-girl. His saying: 'On condition' – he indicated by it that 'upon' in his statement 'on condition that you marry her to me' is for condition, not for consideration, for the consideration is only the thousand. His saying: 'Then nothing' – meaning that it is not obligatory upon the commander to pay the thousand that he stipulated upon himself in his order. His saying: 'And if he adds: on my behalf... etc.' – meaning if the commander adds in his order the word 'on my behalf', and says: Free your slave-girl on my behalf for a thousand on condition that you marry her to me, so the master frees her and the slave-girl refuses to marry him, then at that moment the thousand is divided between the value of the slave-girl and her like dower, and it is obligatory upon the commander to pay the share of the value to the master; because when he said 'on my behalf', it implied a purchase by necessity, so it is as if he said: Sell your slave-girl to me for a thousand, then be my agent in freeing her on my behalf, because of the apparent impossibility of a slave-girl of one man being freed on behalf of another, so his speech necessitates considering the sale and purchase and the ordering of manumission upon it. And it is known that the commander has exchanged the thousand for the price of the slave (as purchase) and for the vulva (as marriage), so he mentioned two things, so the thousand is divided between them necessarily, and since he did not obtain the vulva due to the slave-girl's refusal – where (1) End from Al-Binayah (5:120-121).
Source pages p. 680

Commentary
This passage discusses a variation of the earlier case where the commander adds the word 'عنّي (on my behalf)' to his statement. The ruling changes: the thousand is now divided between the value of the slave-girl (as the price for purchase) and her dower (as the consideration for marriage). The commander is obligated to pay the portion corresponding to the value to the owner. The commentary explains that adding 'on my behalf' implies that the commander is first purchasing the slave-girl and then requesting her manumission on his behalf. Since she refuses marriage, the dower portion is not due, but the price for her value must be paid. The passage also quotes Al-Binayah, which contrasts manumission with khul' (divorce initiated by the wife with payment): in khul', stipulating a substitute on a third party is permissible, but in manumission it is not, because manumission involves granting legal capacity to the slave, which is akin to a counter-exchange requiring compensation from the recipient.

Key Terms
ضم (dam): Adding an additional word or phrase to the original statement.
عنّي ('anni): Meaning 'on my behalf' or 'for me', indicating that the commander takes responsibility.
مهر (mahr): Dower or bridal gift in marriage, often monetary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man says to a slave-owner: 'Free your slave-girl on my behalf for a thousand on condition that you marry her to me', and the owner frees her but she refuses marriage, what must the commander pay?
A) The entire thousand
B) The value of the slave-girl only
C) The share of the value
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
Adding 'on my behalf' transforms the conditional manumission into an implied purchase, obligating the commander to pay the value portion of the promised sum.

Conditional Manumission with 'عني': Division of Payment
Explains division of payment when 'عني' is added.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on conditional manumission with 'عني' to calculate the division of payment between the slave's value and dower.

Core Idea
Adding 'عني' transforms the command into an implied purchase, splitting the payment proportionally.

This passage examines a nuanced case in manumission: a man commands another to free his slave-girl for a thousand dirhams on condition that she be married to him. The ruling depends critically on whether the commander adds the word 'عني' (on my behalf). Without it, no payment is due if the slave-girl refuses; with it, the payment is split between her value and her dower. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning—including a qiyas to khul'—and shows how to calculate the shares.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two commands
Identify the base case (without 'عني') where no payment is due because stipulating a condition on a third party is invalid in manumission. Then note the exceptional case with 'عني' where payment is divided.
The addition of a single word changes the entire legal outcome.
2
Analyze the implied purchase
When 'عني' is added, the command is interpreted as a sale followed by agency in manumission. This is because a third party cannot simply free another's slave without a transaction.
The implication is necessary (qarīna) that the commander intends to purchase and then free.
3
Calculate the proportional division
The thousand is divided based on the slave's value (qīma) and her mahr mithl (customary dower). For example, if value=1000, mahr=500, total=1500; the thousand is split 2/3 (667) for value and 1/3 (333) for dower.
The division is by the fraction: (value)/(value + mahr) for the value portion.
4
Apply when marriage does not occur
Since the slave-girl refuses, the commander does not get the marital benefit, so the mahr portion drops. He only pays the value portion to the owner.
If she refuses, the commander pays only the value portion.
5
Apply when marriage occurs
If she agrees to marry, the mahr portion becomes her dower. The commander pays the full thousand: value portion to the owner and mahr portion to the slave-girl as dower.
The mahr portion is always the slave-girl's dower in either scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ضم: عني؛ قسم الألف على قيمتها ومهرها، وتجب حصة القيمة. أي قال رجل لآخر: أعتق أمتك بألف على أن تزوجنيها، فأعتقها المولى، وأبت الجارية التزوج، فلا شيء على الأمر؛ لأن اشتراط البدل على الغير لا يجوز في العتق. (ولو ضم: عني؛ قسم الألف على قيمتها ومهرها، وتجب حصة القيمة) وقال العيني في «البناية»: «لأن اشتراط البدل على المرأة في الخلع مشروع من غير أن يسلم لها شيء؛ لأن الخلع إسقاط محض، فلما جاز على المرأة من دون سلامة شيء لها جاز على الأجنبي كذلك. بخلاف الإعتاق؛ فإن فيه معنى الإثبات، وإن كان هو إزالة الملك؛ لأن به تحصل للعبد قوة حكمية لم تكن ثابتة قبل الإعتاق، فكان في معنى المعاوضة، واشتراط العوض لا يجوز على غير من يسلم المعوض فلا يجب على الأجنبي شيء؛ لأنه لم يسلم له شيء بهذا الضمان». قوله: لآخر؛ المراد به مولى أمة. قوله: بشرط؛ أشار به إلى أن «على» في قوله: «على أن تزوجنيها» للشرط لا للعوض، فإن العوض إنما هو الألف. قوله: فلا شيء؛ أي لا يجب على الأمر أداء الألف الذي شرطه على نفسه في جملة أمره. قوله: ولو ضم عني...الخ؛ أي لو زاد الآمر في جملة أمره كلمة: عني، فقال: أعتق أمتك عني بألف على أن تزوجنيها فأعتقها المولى وأبت الأمة التزوج به، فحينئذ يقسم الألف على قيمة الجارية ومهر مثلها، ويجب على الأمر أداء حصة القيمة إلى المولى؛ وذلك لأنه لما قال عني تضمن الشراء اقتضاء، فكأنه قال: بع أمتك مني بألف ثم كن وكيلي في إعتاقها عني، وذلك لظهور عدم تصور عتق أمة رجل عن آخر، فكلامه يقتضي اعتبار البيع والشراء وترتب الإعتاق عليه. ومن المعلوم أن الأمر قد قابل الألف بعوض الرقبة شراء، وبالبضع نكاحاً، ذكر أمرين، فينقسم الألف عليهما بالضرورة، ولما لم يحصل له البضع لإباء الجارية حيث عين التزوج، سقط عنه ما حاذى مهر المثل. أي لو قال: أعتق أمتك عني بألف، وباقي المسألة بحالها، فإنه يقع الإعتاق عن الأمر بطريق الاقتضاء، كما عرفت فيقسم الألف على قيمتها ومهر مثلها، ففرضنا أن قيمتها ألف ومهر مثلها خمسمئة، فيقسم الألف على ألف وخمسمئة، فثلثا الألف حصة القيمة، وثلثه حصة مهر المثل، فوجب عليه أداء ثلثي الألف إلى المولى، وسقط عنه ثلث الألف؛ لأنه قابل الألف بالرقبة شراء، وبالبضع نكاحا، فسلم له الرقبة دون البضع، فوجب حصة ما سلم له، ولم يجب حصة ما لم يسلم له. (فلو نكحت فحصة مهرها مهرها في وجهيه) أي إذا لم تأب ونكحته، فمهرها حصة مهر المثل من الألف، وهو ثلث الألف فيما فرضنا. قال في «التبيين»: «لو زوجت نفسها منه في الوجهين لم يذكره في «الجامع الصغير»، وجوابه: ما أصاب قيمتها سقط في الوجه الأول، وهو للمولى في الوجه الثاني، وما أصاب مهر مثلها كان مهراً لها في الوجهين، ولو أعتق أمةً على أن تزوجه نفسها فزوجته نفسها كان لها مهر مثلها عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد؛ لأن العتق ليس بمال فلا يصلح مهراً.
And if he adds: 'from me', the thousand is divided upon her value and her dower, and the portion of the value is obligatory. That is, a man said to another: 'Free your slave-girl for a thousand on condition that you marry her to me,' so the master freed her, and the slave-girl refused marriage, so nothing is due from the commander; because stipulating a consideration upon a third party is not permissible in manumission. (And if he adds: 'from me', the thousand is divided upon her value and her dower, and the portion of the value is obligatory) and al-'Ayni said in al-Binaya: 'Because stipulating a consideration upon the woman in khul' is legislated without anything being given to her; because khul' is pure relinquishment. Since it is permissible upon the woman without anything being given to her, it is likewise permissible upon a third party. Unlike manumission; for in it there is a meaning of affirmation, even though it is removal of ownership; because the slave acquires a legal power that was not established before manumission, so it is in the meaning of exchange. Stipulating compensation is not permissible upon someone who does not give the countervalue, so nothing is due from the third party; because nothing was given to him by this guarantee.' His statement: 'to another' means the master of the slave-girl. His statement: 'on condition' indicates that 'on' in his saying 'on condition that you marry her to me' is for condition, not for compensation; for the compensation is only the thousand. His statement: 'so nothing' means that it is not obligatory upon the commander to pay the thousand that he stipulated upon himself in his command. His statement: 'And if he adds: from me...etc.' means if the commander adds in his command the word 'from me', saying: 'Free your slave-girl from me for a thousand on condition that you marry her to me,' so the master freed her and the slave-girl refused to marry him, then the thousand is divided upon the value of the slave-girl and her dower of the like, and it is obligatory upon the commander to pay the portion of the value to the master; because when he said 'from me', it implied purchase by necessity. It is as if he said: 'Sell your slave-girl to me for a thousand, then be my agent in freeing her from me.' This is because it is evidently inconceivable that a man's slave-girl be freed by another without this. So his speech necessitates consideration of sale and purchase and the ordering of manumission upon it. It is known that the commander has matched the thousand with the compensation of the slave's body by purchase, and with the vulva by marriage, mentioning two things. So the thousand is divided upon them necessarily. Since he did not obtain the vulva due to the slave-girl's refusal where the marriage was specified, what corresponds to the dower of the like drops from him. That is, if he said: 'Free your slave-girl from me for a thousand,' and the rest of the case remains as it is, then the manumission occurs on behalf of the commander by way of implication, as you have learned. So the thousand is divided upon her value and her dower of the like. Suppose her value is a thousand and her dower of the like is five hundred. Then the thousand is divided upon one thousand five hundred. So two-thirds of the thousand is the portion of the value, and one-third is the portion of the dower of the like. So he is obliged to pay two-thirds of the thousand to the master, and one-third of the thousand drops from him; because he matched the thousand with the slave's body by purchase and with the vulva by marriage. The body was delivered to him without the vulva, so the portion of what was delivered to him is obligatory, and the portion of what was not delivered is not obligatory. (If she marries, then the portion of her dower is her dower in both aspects) i.e., if she does not refuse and marries him, then her dower is the portion of the dower of the like from the thousand, which is one-third of the thousand in our assumed case. He said in al-Tabyin: 'If she marries herself to him in the two aspects, he did not mention it in al-Jami' al-Saghir. Its answer: what corresponds to her value drops in the first aspect, and it is for the master in the second aspect. And what corresponds to her dower of the like is her dower in both aspects. And if he freed a slave-girl on condition that she marry herself to him, and she married herself to him, she has her dower of the like according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; because manumission is not property, so it is not valid as a dower.'
Source pages p. 680

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) from the Hanafi school on the division of payment when a man commands another to free his slave-girl 'from him' (عني) for a thousand dirhams, on condition that the commander marries her. The commentary explains the difference between the case without 'عني' and with it. The passage is structured as a commentary on the matn (base text). It begins by clarifying the base ruling: if a man says to the master, 'Free your slave-girl for a thousand on condition that you marry her to me,' and the master frees her but she refuses to marry, then nothing is due from the commander. This is because stipulating a consideration (بدل) upon a third party (the commander) is invalid in manumission. The reason is that manumission has a meaning of affirmation (إثبات) — the slave acquires a legal power — so it is like an exchange; compensation cannot be imposed on someone who does not receive the countervalue. Then the text introduces the exceptional case: if the commander adds the word 'عني' (from me), the ruling changes. This word implies a purchase: it is as if he said, 'Sell her to me for a thousand, then be my agent in freeing her on my behalf.' Since the manumission of another's slave by a third party is inconceivable without this implication, his statement is interpreted as a sale followed by manumission. Consequently, the thousand is divided into two portions: one for the slave's value (purchase) and one for her dower (marriage). The division is proportional to the value and her mithl mahr (dower of a woman of similar standing). For example, if her value is 1000 and her mahr is 500, the total is 1500; the thousand is divided as two-thirds (667) for the value and one-third (333) for the mahr. Since the slave-girl refused marriage, the commander does not get the marital benefit, so the portion corresponding to the mahr drops, and he only pays the value portion (two-thirds) to the master. If she does marry him, then the mahr portion becomes her dower. The passage ends with a note from al-Tabyin that if she marries him in both aspects (i.e., with or without 'عني'), the value portion drops in the first case (without 'عني') and goes to the master in the second, but the mahr portion is always her dower. Finally, it cites a ruling from Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: if a man frees a slave-girl on condition that she marries him, and she does, she receives her mithl mahr because manumission is not property and cannot serve as dower. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that manumission is not a valid exchange in marriage.

Key Terms
ضمان (damān): A guarantee or undertaking by the commander to pay the thousand in the case of conditional manumission.
عني (ʿannī): A phrase meaning 'on my behalf' that changes the legal nature of the command to imply a purchase.
مهر مثل (mahr mithl): The customary dower for a woman of similar standing to the slave-girl, used to determine the portion of payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man says, 'Free your slave-girl from me for a thousand on condition that you marry her to me,' and she refuses to marry, how much is the commander obligated to pay?
A) The full thousand
B) Nothing
C) The portion of her value only
D) The portion of her dower only

Key Takeaway
Adding 'عني' to a conditional manumission command turns it into an implied purchase, requiring division of payment proportional to value and dower.

Definitions and Forms of Tadbir and Istilad
Introduction to definitions and forms of post-mortem emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal definitions of Tadbir and Istilad, and identify valid expressions for Tadbir according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Tadbir and Istilad both secure freedom after the master's death, but Tadbir is explicit while Istilad is implied through paternity.

This lesson opens the chapter on Tadbir (post-mortem emancipation) and Istilad (making a slave-woman an umm walad). Both result in freedom after the master's death, but Tadbir uses direct expressions, whereas Istilad arises indirectly from claiming paternity of a child. Understanding their definitions and the specific Tadbir formulations is essential for drafting valid declarations and avoiding confusion with mere ta'liq (suspension).

Guided Path
1
Identify the shared feature of post-mortem emancipation
Notice that both Tadbir and Istilad are presented together because they both cause freedom after the master's death. This is the key commonality that groups them in one chapter.
2
Differentiate Tadbir and Istilad linguistically and legally
Tadbir literally means 'looking at outcomes' and legally means effecting emancipation after death by explicit words. Istilad literally means 'seeking a child' and legally means claiming paternity of a child born to one's slave-woman, which makes her an umm walad and frees her upon the master's death.
Tadbir is explicit (sarih), Istilad is implicit (not sarih).
3
Categorize the valid expressions for Tadbir
The text from al-Bada'i' lists four categories: (1) explicit words like 'mudabbar' or 'dabbar', (2) words of emancipation like 'free after my death', (3) oath-like conditionals like 'if I die, you are free', (4) will-like expressions bequeathing the slave himself or his person.
Be careful: conditioning emancipation on someone else's death is not Tadbir but mere ta'liq.

باب التدبير والاستيلاد من أعتق عن دُبُرِ مطلقاً بإذا مت فانت حر، أو أنت حر عن دبر مني، أو دُبُرِ أنت مدبر، أو دبرتك، أو إن مت إلى مئة سنة. قوله: باب التدبير... الخ؛ لَمَّا فرغ عن أنواع العتق الحاصل قبل الموتِ منجزاً أو معلقاً شرع في أنواع إيجاب العنق الحاصل بعد الموت، ولما كان التدبير والاستيلاد مشتركين في حصول العتق بهما بعد موتِ المولى جمعهما في باب واحد، وقدّم التدبير؛ لأنه إيجاب عتق صريحاً، ولا كذلك الاستيلاد. ثم الاستيلاد لغة: طلب الولد وشرعاً: عبارة عن ادّعاء نسب ولد أمة موطوءة من نفسه، ويطلق بذلك على الأمة أم الولد، وهو من الأسماء الغالبة. والتدبير لغة: النظر في عواقب الأمور، وشرعاً: إيجاب العتق الحاصل بعد الموت بألفاظ تدلّ عليه، فكأنّ المولى ينظرُ إلى عاقبة أمره، فيخرج عبده من الرقية إلى الحرية. كذا في «النهاية» وغيرها. قوله: عن دبر؛ الدبر بضمتين وقد يخفّف الباء خلافَ القُبل من كلِّ شيء، ومنه يقال لآخر الأمر: دبر، والمراد به دبر المولى؛ أي أعتقه بعده، وأما تعليقه بموتِ غيره فليس بتدبير بل تعليق. كذا في «البحر» نقلا عن «المبسوط». قوله: بإذا مت...الخ؛ قال في «البدائع»: «له ألفاظ: فقد يكون بصريح اللفظ، مثل أن يقول: أنت مدبّر أو دبرتك. وقد يكون بلفظ التحرير والإعتاق مثل: أنت حرّ بعد موتي، أو حرّرتك بعد موتي، أو أنت عتيق أو معتق بعد موتي. وقد يكون بلفظ اليمين بأن يقول: إن مت فأنت حرّ، أو إذا مت أو متى مت، أو متى مامت، أو إن حدث بي حدث، أو متى حدث بي حدث، وكذا إذا ذكر في هذه الألفاظ مكان الموت الوفاة أو الهلاك. وقد يكون بلفظ الوصية: وهو أن يوصي لعبده بنفسه أو برقبته أو بعتقه أو بوصيّة يستحق من جملتها رقبته أو بعضها، نحو أن يقول: أوصيتك بنفسك أو رقبتك أو
Chapter of Tadbir and Istilad. Whoever emancipates 'an dubur' absolutely, by saying 'If I die, you are free', or 'You are free after my death', or 'You are mudabbar', or 'I have made you mudabbar', or 'If I die up to a hundred years...' His saying: 'Chapter of Tadbir etc.': When he finished from the types of emancipation occurring before death, immediate or suspended, he began the types of effecting emancipation occurring after death. And since Tadbir and Istilad share in obtaining emancipation by them after the master's death, he combined them in one chapter, and gave precedence to Tadbir because it is an explicit effecting of emancipation, unlike Istilad. Then Istilad linguistically: seeking a child, and legally: it is an expression for claiming the lineage of a child of a slave-woman who is cohabited, from himself, and it is applied by that to the slave-woman as 'umm walad', and it is from the dominant names. And Tadbir linguistically: looking at the outcomes of matters, and legally: effecting emancipation occurring after death by expressions that indicate it, as if the master looks at the outcome of his affair, so he brings his slave out from slavery to freedom. Thus in al-Nihayah and others. His saying: 'an dubur'; al-dubur with two dammas and it may be lightened, contrary to qubul of everything, and from it it is said for the end of a matter: dubur, and the intended meaning is the dubur of the master; i.e., he emancipates him after him. And as for suspending it on the death of someone else, it is not Tadbir but ta'liq. Thus in al-Bahr quoting from al-Mabsut. His saying: 'If I die etc.'; He said in al-Bada'i': 'It has expressions: sometimes it is with explicit wording, such as saying: you are mudabbar or I have made you mudabbar. And sometimes it is with the wording of tahrir and i'taq, such as: you are free after my death, or I have freed you after my death, or you are atiq or mu'taq after my death. And sometimes it is with the wording of an oath, such as: if I die, you are free, or when I die, or whenever I die, or whenever you die, or if an event happens to me, or whenever an event happens to me, and similarly if he mentions in these expressions instead of death, demise or destruction. And sometimes it is with the wording of a will: that he bequeaths to his slave his own self or his slave-person or his emancipation or a bequest by which the slave-person or part of it is owed, such as saying: I have bequeathed to you yourself or your slave-person or...
Source pages p. 683

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter on Tadbir and Istilad in the commentary on Al-Hidayah. The author (the commentator, likely Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani's work or a later commentary) explains that after completing the types of emancipation that take effect before death (either immediate or conditional), he now turns to types that take effect after the master's death. Tadbir (post-mortem emancipation) and Istilad (declaring a slave-woman as mother of a child, thus securing her freedom upon the master's death) are combined because both result in freedom after death. Tadbir is presented first because it is a straightforward declaration of emancipation, whereas Istilad is not. The definitions are given: Tadbir literally means 'looking at outcomes' (tadbir al-umur) and legally means effecting emancipation after death through specific expressions. Istilad literally means 'seeking a child' and legally means claiming paternity of the child born to one's slave-woman, thereby making her an umm walad (mother of a child), who becomes free upon the master's death. The commentator then clarifies the phrase 'an dubur' in the matn: 'dubur' (with two dammas or lightened) is the opposite of 'qubul' and refers to the end; here it means 'after the master' (i.e., after his death). If the emancipation is conditioned on someone else's death, it is not Tadbir but pure ta'liq (suspension). Finally, the passage lists various forms of Tadbir expressions according to al-Bada'i': explicit words like 'mudabbar' or 'dabbar', words of emancipation like 'free after my death', oath-like conditionals like 'if I die', and will-like expressions such as bequeathing the slave himself or his person. The text is cut off mid-sentence discussing the will form.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): Legally: effecting emancipation of a slave that occurs after the master's death through specific expressions.
استيلاد (istilad): Legally: the master's claim of paternity of a child born to his slave-woman, making her an umm walad.
دبر (dubur): Literally the back or end; here used to mean 'after' or 'posterior', i.e., emancipation after the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a valid category of Tadbir expressions according to al-Bada'i'?
A) Explicit words like 'mudabbar'.
B) Words of emancipation like 'free after my death'.
C) Words of sale like 'I sell you to yourself after my death'.
D) Words of oath like 'if I die, you are free'.

Key Takeaway
Tadbir is a binding post-mortem emancipation declared by specific expressions, distinct from Istilad, and requires that the condition be the master's own death.

Definition and Wording of Tadbir
Defining tadbir and listing its valid wordings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Tadbir, list its valid wordings, and distinguish absolute from restricted Tadbir.

Core Idea
Tadbir is a valid postponement of emancipation until after the master's death, effected by specific wordings.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi definition of Tadbir (postponed manumission) and the precise wordings that make it valid. The passage opens the chapter on Tadbir and Istilad, explaining why these two topics are combined and why Tadbir is given precedence. We will dissect the linguistic and legal meanings, examine the range of valid expressions, and understand the critical distinction between absolute and restricted Tadbir—a distinction that determines which legal rulings apply to the mudabbar slave.

Guided Path
1
Understand the legal definition of Tadbir
Identify the linguistic and technical definitions of Tadbir as given in the passage. Note that Tadbir linguistically means ‘considering consequences’ and legally means ‘necessitating emancipation after death by words that indicate it.’
The term ‘dubur’ (back/after) is central; Tadbir is derived from it.
2
Recognize the relationship between Tadbir and Istilad
Both Tadbir and Istilad result in freedom after the master's death, but Tadbir is explicit while Istilad involves claiming paternity. Understand why they are combined in one chapter.
Istilad is discussed separately in this chapter but given secondary treatment.
3
List the valid wordings for Tadbir
From the passage (quoting al-Bada'i'), enumerate the four categories: (1) explicit wording like ‘anta mudabbar’, (2) wording of emancipation like ‘anta hurr ba'd mawti’, (3) oath-like conditions like ‘in muta fa-anta hurr’, (4) will-based phrasing like ‘awsaytu laka bi-nafsika’.
All wordings must clearly tie emancipation to the master's death.
4
Distinguish absolute vs restricted Tadbir
The passage emphasizes ‘mutlaqan’ (absolutely). Absolute Tadbir is unconditional regarding time; restricted Tadbir limits emancipation to a period (e.g., 'if I die within 100 years'). Only absolute Tadbir carries the full rulings of a mudabbar (e.g., cannot be sold).
If the master is old and death is expected before the limit, the slave is still mudabbar.
5
Apply the definition to identify what is NOT Tadbir
Suspending emancipation on the death of someone else, or on an event other than the master's death, is not Tadbir but general ta'liq (suspension).
This distinction prevents confusion with other forms of conditional manumission.

Chapter of Tadbir and Istilad. (Whoever emancipates after death absolutely with 'if I die then you are free', or 'you are free after my death', or 'you are mudabbar', or 'I have made you mudabbar', or 'if I die within a hundred years') [1] Chapter of Tadbir and Istilad. (Whoever emancipates after death absolutely with 'if I die' then you are free...) 1] His saying: Chapter of Tadbir... etc.; When he finished from the types of emancipation occurring before death, whether immediate or suspended, he began in the types of necessitating emancipation occurring after death. Since Tadbir and Istilad share in the occurrence of emancipation after the death of the master, he combined them in one chapter, and he gave precedence to Tadbir because it is an explicit necessitation of emancipation, and not so Istilad. Then Istilad linguistically: seeking a child; and legally: a statement of claiming lineage of a child of a slave woman who is cohabited from himself, and it is applied thereby to the slave woman as Umm Walad, and it is one of the predominant nouns. And Tadbir linguistically: looking into the consequences of matters; and legally: necessitating emancipation occurring after death with words that indicate it, as if the master looks to the consequence of his affair, so he takes his slave out from slavery to freedom. Thus in 'al-Nihayah' and others. [2] His saying: 'an dubur (after death); al-dubur with two dammas and it may be lightened in the ba, opposite of qubul (front) of everything, and from it is said for the end of the matter: dubur, and what is intended by it is the back of the master; i.e., he emancipated him after him. As for suspending it upon the death of someone else, it is not tadbir but suspension. Thus in 'al-Bahr' quoting from 'al-Mabsut'. [3] His saying: 'idha mut... etc.; He said in 'al-Bada'i': 'It has wordings: sometimes it is with explicit wording, like his saying: you are mudabbar or I have made you mudabbar. And sometimes it is with the wording of tahrir and i'taq, like: you are free after my death, or I have freed you after my death, or you are atiq or mu'taq after my death. And sometimes it is with the wording of an oath, like his saying: if I die then you are free, or when I die, or whenever I die, or if something happens to me, or whenever something happens to me, and similarly if he mentions in these words instead of death: demise or destruction. And sometimes it is with the wording of a will: and it is that he makes a will for his slave of himself, or his person, or his emancipation, or a will from whose total his person or part of it is deserved, like his saying: I have bequeathed to you yourself or your person or your emancipation, or everything that expresses the entire body, and similarly if he said: I have bequeathed to you a third of my wealth.' End. (2) [1] His saying: 'and it dominates'; it is attached to the last example, and the waw is for the state, and the result is that if he restricted death to a period and the dominant expectation was that death would occur before it, such as if the master was old and said, while his age was eighty years: 'if I die within a hundred years', he is also mudabbar. [2] His saying: 'indeed he said in al-Hidayah... etc.; The expression of al-Hidayah at the beginning of 'Chapter of Tadbir': 'When the master says to his slave: if I die then you are free, and you are free after my death, or you are mudabbar, or I have made you mudabbar, then he becomes mudabbar; because these wordings are explicit in tadbir, for it is the establishment of emancipation after death.' End (3). So the author of al-Hidayah defined tadbir by his saying: establishment of emancipation after death, in observance of the derivation of tadbir, for it is taken from al-dubur. So the author (may Allah have mercy on him) pointed to it by his saying: whoever emancipates after death... etc. [3] His saying: 'as a precaution against the restricted'; the apparent meaning of the speech of many jurists is that the mudabbar legally is only the absolute mudabbar, and as for the restricted, it is excluded from mudabbar legally. And among them are those who said: the mudabbar is a shared meaning between the absolute and the restricted. In any case, the rulings specific to the mudabbar which the author will mention, such as the impermissibility of selling him and the like, are only for the absolute, not the restricted. So it is necessary to take precaution against the restricted, therefore the author added his saying: 'absolutely'. [4] His saying: 'that he suspends'; passive present from ta'liq, and what follows is its deputy subject, and it is likely...
Source pages p. 683

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Tadbir (postponed manumission) and Istilad (umm walad). The commentator explains that after covering types of emancipation occurring before death (whether immediate or suspended), the text now turns to types that occur after the master's death. Tadbir and Istilad are combined because both result in freedom after the master's death, but Tadbir is given precedence because it is an explicit declaration of emancipation, whereas Istilad involves claiming paternity. The linguistic and legal definitions are given: Tadbir linguistically means considering consequences, legally it means necessitating emancipation after death through specific words. The word 'dubur' (back/after) is explained: it refers to after the master's death, and suspending emancipation on someone else's death is not Tadbir but a general suspension. The text then details the types of wordings for Tadbir, quoting from al-Bada'i': (1) explicit words like 'anta mudabbar' or 'dabbartuka'; (2) words of emancipation like 'anta hurr ba'd mawti'; (3) oath-like conditions such as 'in muta fa-anta hurr'; (4) will-based phrasing like 'awsaytu laka bi-nafsika'. The commentary then discusses the phrase 'wa ghalaba mawtuhu qablaha fa-mudabbar' regarding cases where death is expected within a stated period; even if the death is conditional upon a time, if the dominant expectation is death before that time, the slave becomes mudabbar. The Hidayah definition is cited: Tadbir is 'ithbat al-'itq 'an dubur' (establishment of emancipation after death), emphasizing the derivation from dubur. Finally, the term 'mutlaqan' (absolutely) is explained as a precaution: only absolute (unrestricted) Tadbir carries the rulings of Tadbir; restricted formulations do not. So the author adds 'mutlaqan' to limit the ruling to absolute Tadbir.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): لغة: النظر في عواقب الأمور. شرعاً: إيجاب العتق الحاصل بعد الموت بألفاظ تدلّ عليه.
دبر (dubur): بضمتين وقد يخفف الباء، خلاف القبل من كل شيء، والمراد به دبر المولى أي بعد موته.
مدبر (mudabbar): العبد الذي علق عتقه بموت مولاه بألفاظ التدبير.
استيلاد (istilad): لغة: طلب الولد. شرعاً: ادعاء نسب ولد أمة موطوءة من نفسه.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a valid wording for Tadbir according to the passage?
A) 'You are free after my death'
B) 'If I die then you are free'
C) 'You are free if the sun rises'
D) 'I have bequeathed to you yourself'

Key Takeaway
Tadbir is valid emancipation after death using specific wordings; only absolute Tadbir carries full legal effects.

Definition and Types of Tadbir (Manumission Upon Death)
Defining tadbir and its absolute/restricted types with the predominant death criterion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tadbir, distinguish between absolute (mutlaq) and restricted (muqayyad) tadbir, and apply the Hanafi rule that predominant death makes a time-bound declaration functionally absolute.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, a mudabbar is freed upon the master's death; absolute tadbir includes cases where death is predominant, even if time-bound.

This lesson explains the definition of tadbir (manumission upon death) and the two types: absolute and restricted. The commentary on al-Hidayah clarifies that the distinguishing criterion is not the wording alone, but the likelihood of death. An apparent contradiction with temporary marriage rulings is also resolved, reinforcing the context-sensitive nature of legal classification.

Guided Path
1
Define Tadbir
Read the source passage's definition: tadbir is 'the establishment of freeing from the back (dubur),' i.e., freedom tied to the master's death. Identify the subject and predicate in the base text's phrase.
The term 'mudabbar' is the predicate describing a slave freed upon the master's death.
2
Distinguish Absolute vs. Restricted
Note the two categories: mutlaq (absolute) is either unconditional or conditioned on a death that is predominant; muqayyad (restricted) is conditioned on a death that is not predominant (e.g., within a year for a young master).
The absolute includes both pure 'when I die' and time-bound statements where death is the likely outcome.
3
Apply the Predominant Death Criterion
Examine the example: an eighty-year-old saying 'if I die within a hundred years' is functionally absolute because death is inevitable before that period. Contrast with 'within a year' for a healthy young person, which is restricted.
The ruling is based on ghalabah al-zann (predominant probability), not the literal wording.
4
Resolve the Apparent Contradiction with Temporary Marriage
The commentary notes that in tadbir, a hundred-year limit with predominant death is absolute, but in nikah mut'ah, the same wording makes the marriage temporary. Understand that the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) differs because the 'illa (cause) for each ruling is different: tadbir looks to the likelihood of death; temporary marriage looks to any temporal specification.
This shows how context and legal purpose can change the classification of the same wording.

Source Text

And if his death before it predominates, then he is a mudabbar. So his statement: 'Who is freed' is the subject, and its predicate is 'mudabbar'. Know that he said in al-Hidayah: 'Indeed tadbir is the establishment of freeing from the back (dubur).' He only explained it this way observing the derivation of tadbir; for this the text said: 'Who is freed from the back.' And he only said 'absolutely' to be cautious about the restricted. So the absolute is that free is suspended on death absolutely or restricted by a condition whose occurrence is predominant. The restricted is that he suspends it on death restricted by a condition that is not like that customarily, like: 'If you die in this', so it is free. So his statement: 'If I die within a hundred years' while he is eighty, for example, even if in form restricted, it is in meaning absolute, because death before this period is predominant. So his statement 'If I die within a hundred years' is like his statement 'If I die', so it is in the ruling of absolute. So the absolute mudabbar is of two types: one is that freeing is attached to death absolutely without being restricted by time or condition. The second is that it is attached to death restricted by a condition whose occurrence is predominant. The restricted mudabbar is what is contrary to these two forms. He said in al-Hidayah: 'From the restricted is that he says: If I die within a year or ten years for what we mentioned, unlike if he says: within a hundred years, and the like of him does not live to it in the predominant, because it is inevitably like happening.' And it was objected against him that this statement of his contradicts his statement in the discussion of temporary marriage in the book of marriage: 'There is no difference between whether the period of temporary marriage is long or short, because the timing is what determines the temporary enjoyment, and it has occurred.' For his statement here necessitates that restriction by a condition whose occurrence is predominant is in the ruling of absolute, and his statement there indicates that it is restricted, so the marriage with his statement 'I married you for a hundred years' is temporary.
Source pages p. 684

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary (sharh) on al-Hidayah defining tadbir and its types. The author explains that the base text's phrase 'who is freed from the back' refers to a mudabbar (a slave granted freedom upon the master's death). The term 'mutlaqan' (absolutely) is added to exclude restricted tadbir. Absolute tadbir is of two kinds: 1) unconditionally attached to death with no time or condition, and 2) attached to a time frame where death is the predominant expectation (e.g., an eighty-year-old saying 'if I die within a hundred years'). Restricted tadbir is where death is not predominant (e.g., within a year for a young person). The passage then notes an apparent contradiction in al-Hidayah: regarding tadbir, a hundred-year limit with predominant death is treated as absolute, but regarding temporary marriage (nikah mut'ah), the same time frame is treated as restricted (since any temporal limit makes it temporary). This highlights that context changes the ruling: tadbir looks to the likelihood of death, while temporary marriage looks to the existence of any specified time.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): The legal act of establishing a slave's freedom upon the master's death, derived from 'dubur' (back/after).
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been granted freedom upon the master's death, with restrictions on sale.
مطلق (mutlaq): Absolute tadbir where freedom is not tied to a condition or tied to a condition where death is predominant.
مقيد (muqayyad): Restricted tadbir where freedom is tied to a condition where death is not the predominant occurrence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, when is a time-bound tadbir (e.g., 'if I die within 100 years') considered absolute (mutlaq)?
A) When the time period is very long.
B) When the master is so old that death before expiry is predominant.
C) When the slave is young and healthy.
D) When the master explicitly says 'mutlaq'.

Key Takeaway
Whether a tadbir is absolute or restricted depends on the predominant likelihood of death, not the literal wording.

Definition of Mudabbar: Absolute vs Conditional
Defining mudabbar mutlaq and muqayyad with conditions likely to occur

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mudabbar mutlaq and mudabbar muqayyad, and apply the Hanafi rule that a condition whose occurrence is prevalent (ghalib) is treated as absolute.

Core Idea
A condition that is virtually certain to occur does not make a tadbir conditional—it remains absolute.

Tadbir is a form of manumission deferred until the owner's death. The Hanafi school distinguishes between absolute (mutlaq) and conditional (muqayyad) tadbir. However, this lesson examines a key subtlety: when the owner attaches a condition that is almost certain to occur—like 'if I die within 100 years' when he is 80—the tadbir is treated as absolute in meaning. This ruling arises from the principle that what is inevitable is like what has already occurred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of tadbir
State the definitions of mudabbar mutlaq (no condition or condition virtually certain) and mudabbar muqayyad (condition not generally expected to occur).
2
Recognize the borderline case
Examine the example: 'If I die within 100 years' from an 80-year-old owner. Note that in form it is conditional, but in meaning it is absolute due to the prevalence of death before that time.
This is the key nuance in the passage.
3
Analyze the Hanafi reasoning
Understand why the condition is treated as absolute: the prevalent (ghalib) is that death will occur before the specified time, so the condition is effectively meaningless. The principle 'what is inevitable is like what has already occurred' (al-ghalib ka al-muhaqqaq) underpins this.
4
Compare the opposing view
Learn that some Hanafi scholars (e.g., Qadi Khan) hold that any explicit condition remains conditional, analogizing to fixed-term marriage. Identify their proof and the Hanafi response.
The distinction lies in the caution (ihtiyat) required in marriage to prevent prohibited temporary marriage, which is not applicable to tadbir.
5
Resolve the dispute
Determine the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position: the tadbir is absolute when the condition is prevalent. Understand why this view is preferred and how it differs from the ruling on nikah mu'aqqat.
This resolution shows the importance of context in applying legal maxims.

Source Text

Or conditional with a condition whose occurrence is prevalent. And the conditional: that he attaches it to a death conditioned by a condition that is not usually like that, such as: 'If I die of this disease, then he is free.' So his saying: 'If I die within a hundred years' – while he is, for example, eighty years old – although in form it is conditional, in meaning it is absolute, because the prevalent is that he will die before this period. So his saying: 'If I die within a hundred years' is equivalent to his saying: 'If I die', so it is in the ruling of the absolute... The absolute mudabbar is of two types: one: that manumission is attached to death absolutely without being restricted by time or condition. Second: that it is attached to death conditioned by a condition whose occurrence is prevalent. And the conditional mudabbar is what is contrary to these two forms. He said: 'And he' – i.e., the situation is that the master saying that speech, his age at that time is eighty years, for example, for it is apparent that one whose age is eighty will not live to a hundred years from that time. He said: 'So in meaning it is absolute'; Al-Hidayah says: 'And from the conditional is that he says: If I die within a year or ten years, according to what we mentioned, contrary to if he says: within a hundred years, and someone like him generally does not live to it; because it is as if it will necessarily occur.' He finished. And it was objected that this statement contradicts his saying in the discussion of 'Fixed-term Marriage' in the Book of Marriage: 'There is no difference whether the fixed term is long or short; because the fixing is what specifies the aspect of mut'ah, and it exists.' So his statement here implies that restriction with a condition whose occurrence is prevalent is in the ruling of absolute, and his statement there indicates that it is conditional, so the marriage with his saying: 'I married you for a hundred years' is a fixed-term marriage. Then afterwards it was mentioned: Qadi Khan and the author of 'Jami' al-Fiqh' and 'Yanabi' stated that the conditional with a condition, absolutely, even if its occurrence is prevalent, is mudabbar and conditional, and this agrees with what they mentioned in the discussion of marriage. And a group among them mentioned that the chosen view is that it is absolute, and restriction with a condition whose occurrence is prevalent is in the ruling of perpetuity. As for what was mentioned in Al-Hidayah in the discussion of fixed-term marriage, it is based on caution in prohibiting fixed-term marriage, giving priority to the prohibited. Thus in 'Al-Bahr' and others.
Source pages p. 685

Commentary
This is a definition and ruling passage from a commentary on Al-Hidayah. It defines two categories of tadbir: absolute (mutlaq) and conditional (muqayyad). The absolute is when the owner attaches manumission to his death without any condition. The conditional is when there is a condition. However, a key point is that if the condition is almost certain to occur—like saying 'if I die within 100 years' when the owner is 80—it is treated as absolute in meaning, because the condition is virtually inevitable. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author of Al-Hidayah had ruled that such a condition makes the tadbir absolute, but others, including Qadi Khan, argue it remains conditional. The majority (jam' minhum) choose the view that it is absolute, and the ruling in Al-Hidayah on fixed-term marriage is distinguished as being based on caution (ihtiyat) to prevent temporary marriage, which is prohibited. The lesson thus clarifies the nuanced definition of mudabbar based on the probability of the condition's occurrence.

Key Terms
مدبر مطلق (mudabbar muṭlaq): A slave whose manumission is attached to the owner's death without any condition or with a condition that is almost certain to occur, treated as absolute.
مدبر مقيد (mudabbar muqayyad): A slave whose manumission is attached to death with a condition that is not generally expected to occur, e.g., 'if I die within a year' when one is healthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if a man says to his slave, 'If I die within 100 years, you are free,' and the man is 80 years old, what is the status of the tadbir?
A) It is a conditional tadbir (muqayyad) because a condition was stated.
B) It is an absolute tadbir (mutlaq) because death is virtually certain within that time.
C) It is invalid because the condition is impossible.
D) It is considered a contract of kitabah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a tadbir condition that is overwhelmingly likely to occur is treated as absolute (mutlaq), not conditional (muqayyad).

Rulings on the Mudabbar: Prohibited and Permitted Dispositions
Stating the legal rulings on selling, gifting, using, renting, and marrying a mudabbar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which dispositions are prohibited and which are permitted regarding a mudabbar, and explain the rationale based on the owner's retained ownership (mulk al-raqaba).

Core Idea
A mudabbar cannot be sold or gifted, but can be used, hired, and married—because the owner retains ownership of the person.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya outlines the legal limits on what an owner may do with a mudabbar (a slave promised freedom upon the owner's death). The core principle is that while full ownership (mulk al-raqaba) remains, any disposition that would transfer ownership away is prohibited because it nullifies the slave's right to future freedom. Understanding this balance is essential for correctly applying the tadbir contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
List the prohibited acts (sale, gift, etc.) and permitted acts (use, hire, marry, intercourse). Note that the list of prohibited acts is exemplary.
All dispositions that would remove the slave from ownership are prohibited.
2
Locate the dalil
The rationale given is that ownership of the slave's person (mulk al-raqaba) remains with the owner. This justifies permissible acts as with any other slave. Sale etc. are prohibited because they would invalidate the slave's right to manumission after the owner's death.
The proof is aqli (rational) based on the nature of ownership and the tadbir contract.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The connection: Since mulk al-raqaba remains, normal owner prerogatives (use, hire, marry) are allowed. However, sale and gift transfer ownership, which would cancel the tadbir's effect, so they are excluded.
The prohibition is not because of any defect in the owner's right, but because of the supervening right of the slave.
4
Note the exemplary nature
The author says 'he mentioned them as examples' – meaning any transaction that transfers ownership (e.g., pledge, bequest) is likewise prohibited. The list is not exhaustive.
Also, the child of a female mudabbar is also mudabbar.
5
Note cross-madhhab divergence
This Hanafi ruling relies on the binding nature of tadbir. Shafi'is do not consider tadbir binding; for them, the slave can still be sold. This is a key practical difference.
Always be aware of the madhhab context when applying rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يباع ولا يوهب، ويستخدم، ويستأجر، والأمة توطأ وتنكح. قوله : لا يباع ولا يوهب ; ذكرهما على سبيل التمثيل، وإلا فكل تصرف لا يقع في الحرّ نحو الأمهار والرهن والوصيّة والبيع والشراء والهبة والصدقة يمتنع في المدبّر وبالجملة لا يخرجُ المدبّر من الملك بوجه من الوجوه إلا بالإعتاق والكتابة. كذا في «الذخيرة» و«البحر». قوله : ويستخدم ; عطف على قوله : لا يباع، لا على قوله : «يباع»، وبالجملة : هو ليس بداخل تحت النفي، والحاصل : إنّه يجوز استخدام المدبر واستئجاره وإيجاره وإنكاحه ووطء المدبّر. والوجه فيه : إنَّ ملك الرقبة باق للمولى، فتجوزُ هذه الأشياء كما تجوز بسائر المماليك، وإنّما امتنع البيع ونحوه مما يخرجه عن ملكه ؛ لأنّ فيه إبطالاً لما استحقه العبد من العتق بعد موت مولاه (1) لأن ملك المولى ثابت له و به تستفاد هذه التصرفات من غير إبطال حق العبد، وولد المدبّرة مدبّر. ينظر : فتح باب العناية»(۲ : ۲۲۹).
He is not sold nor given as a gift, and he is used, and hired out, and the female slave is cohabited and married. He said: 'He is not sold nor given as a gift' – he mentioned them as examples, otherwise every disposition that does not apply to a free person, such as dower, pledge, bequest, sale, purchase, gift, charity, is prohibited for the mudabbar. In short, the mudabbar does not leave ownership in any way except through manumission and kitabah. Thus in 'Al-Dhakhira' and 'Al-Bahr'. He said: 'And he is used' – it is a conjunction to 'he is not sold', not to 'he is sold', and in short it is not included under the negation. The summary: it is permissible to use the mudabbar, hire him out, rent him, marry him off, and cohabit the female mudabbar. The rationale for it is that ownership of the slave's person (mulk al-raqaba) remains with the owner, so these things are permissible as they are permissible with other slaves. The prohibition of sale and similar things that remove him from ownership is only because it would nullify the right that the slave has acquired to manumission after the owner's death, because the owner's ownership is established for him and through it these dispositions are utilized without nullifying the slave's right. And the child of a female mudabbar is a mudabbar. See: 'Fath Bab al-Inayah' (2:229).
Source pages p. 686

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on a mudabbar (a slave promised freedom upon the owner's death). The primary ruling is that the owner cannot sell or give away the mudabbar, because that would defeat the slave's right to freedom after the owner's death. However, the owner may still use the mudabbar for service, hire him out to others, and in the case of a female mudabbar, the owner may have intercourse with her or marry her off. The reasoning is that the owner retains full ownership of the slave's person (mulk al-raqaba), so all normal benefits of ownership are permitted, except those that would transfer ownership away from the owner. The commentary clarifies that the list of prohibited acts (sale, gift) is exemplary; any transfer of ownership is prohibited. Permitted acts include any usage or benefit that does not remove the slave from ownership. The passage also notes that the child of a female mudabbar automatically becomes a mudabbar as well.

Key Terms
ملك الرقبة (mulk al-raqaba): Ownership of the slave's person, as opposed to the right of usufruct. This ownership remains with the owner during the slave's life and justifies permissible dispositions.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the owner's death via a tadbir declaration. This creates a right for the slave that cannot be revoked by sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following actions is permissible for an owner regarding his mudabbar slave?
A) Selling the mudabbar to pay a debt.
B) Giving the mudabbar as a gift to his son.
C) Hiring out the mudabbar for work.
D) Freeing the mudabbar immediately.

Key Takeaway
The mudabbar's right to freedom upon the owner's death prevents the owner from selling or giving him away, but other uses of ownership remain permissible.

Rulings of Umm Walad (Mother of the Master's Child)
Explains who becomes umm walad and her legal status similar to mudabbarah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a female slave becomes an umm walad in the Hanafi school and explain her legal status.

Core Idea
A female slave becomes umm walad by bearing her master's child, and is freed upon his death — she cannot be sold.

This passage explains the key rulings regarding the umm walad (mother of the master's child). You will learn the two situations that give her this status: directly from the master or indirectly via a husband. The commentary clarifies that even a stillborn child counts if limbs have formed, and it provides the proof from the hadith of Mariya al-Qibtiyya. Understanding these rules is essential for correctly handling the legal status of a female slave who bears her master's child.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two ways a slave becomes umm walad
Read the first part of the passage: "A female slave who gives birth to a child from her master, or from a husband and then the master owns her, becomes umm walad." Note the two distinct scenarios.
2
Analyze the definition of 'child' for umm walad
The commentary explains that 'child' includes both live and stillborn, but only if some limbs have formed. A mere miscarriage without formed limbs does not trigger the status.
This shows the Hanafi reliance on the existence of a recognizable child.
3
Understand the husband scenario
Consider the example: a free man marries a slave woman of another; she bears his child; then he later comes to own her. She becomes his umm walad. If he co-owns her, he must pay the partner's share.
The ruling applies even if ownership is partial.
4
Examine the legal effect (hukm) of being umm walad
Her status is like a mudabbarah: she cannot be sold or transferred, and she becomes free automatically upon the master's death.
This is the core legal consequence.
5
Confirm the proof (dalil)
The passage cites the hadith: "Her child set her free" (referring to Mariya al-Qibtiyya). This indicates that bearing the master's child causes emancipation, but delayed until death.
The hadith is ahad but clear in meaning (qati al-dalala).

[0] قوله : أو من زوج ; صورته : أن يتزوج حرّ بأمةٍ لغيره ، فيولد له منها ولد، ثمّ يملك الزوج زوجته باشتراء أو هبة أو إرث أو نحو ذلك، سواء كان ملكه ملك الكل أو ملك البعض، بأن يشتريها هو وآخر فتصير أم ولد للزوج ، وتلزمه قيمة نصيب شريكه في صورة الشركة. كذا في «البحر». [٦] قوله : وحكمها كالمدبرة ; أي في عتقها بعد موت سيدها، وعدم جواز إخراجها من ملك إلى ملك بالبيع ونحوه. والأصل فيه قول النبي [؟] المارية القبطية، وهي أمته وأمّ ولده إبراهيم : «أعتقها ولدها».
And a female slave who gives birth to a child from her master, or from a husband and then the master owns her, becomes umm walad, and her ruling is like that of a mudabbarah. [1] His saying: 'gives birth' – he said in al-Bahr: He gave the word 'child' generally encompassing a live child and a stillborn, because the stillborn is a child by evidence that rulings of childbirth apply to it, such as the completion of the waiting period ('iddah) by it, and the woman becomes... and it includes one whose some limbs have formed; but if nothing has formed, she is not considered the mother of a miscarried child... and it is considered a child even if claimed. [0] His saying: 'or from a husband' – its picture is that a free man marries a female slave belonging to another, then she gives birth to a child from him, then the husband owns his wife through purchase, gift, inheritance, or similar, whether his ownership is complete or partial, such that he buys her together with another, then she becomes umm walad for the husband, and he owes the value of his partner's share in the case of partnership. Thus in al-Bahr. [6] His saying: 'and her ruling is like that of a mudabbarah' – i.e., in her emancipation after the master's death, and the impermissibility of removing her from ownership to another through sale and similar. The basis for this is the saying of the Prophet [؟] to Mariya the Copt, who was his female slave and the mother of his son Ibrahim: 'Her child set her free.'
Source pages p. 689

Commentary
This passage explains the rulings of the umm walad (mother of the master's child). It first states the general rule: a female slave becomes umm walad either by giving birth to a child from her master directly, or by first having a child from a husband and then being owned by the master later. Her status is then similar to that of a mudabbarah: she cannot be sold or gifted, and she becomes automatically free upon the master's death. The commentary elaborates on each part. Regarding 'gives birth' (ولدت), it clarifies that 'child' includes both live and stillborn children, because even a stillborn triggers rulings of childbirth such as completing the 'iddah. If the fetus has not formed limbs, it is not considered a child for this purpose. For the scenario of a husband, the example is a free man marrying a slave girl belonging to another; he fathers a child with her; then if he later comes to own her (by purchase, gift, inheritance), she becomes his umm walad, and if she was co-owned, he must pay the partner's share. The legal effect is that she becomes free upon the master's death and cannot be sold. The proof is the hadith about the Prophet's slave Mariya al-Qibtiyya: 'Her child set her free.'

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who bears a child from her master, thereby acquiring the status of Umm Walad.
استيلاد (istilad): The act of a female slave becoming Umm Walad by bearing her master's child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following conditions makes a female slave an Umm Walad?
A) She gives birth to a live child from her master.
B) She gives birth to a stillborn child from her master with limbs formed.
C) She gives birth to a child from a husband, then the master later owns her.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
A female slave becomes umm walad by bearing her master's child (live or stillborn with formed limbs) or by bearing from a husband and later being owned; her status is like a mudabbarah: she cannot be sold and is freed upon the master's death.

The Ruling of Umm Walad: Emancipation and Comparison with Mudabbarah
Explains the legal status of umm walad and its differences from mudabbarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on umm walad, identify its proof, and explain how it differs from a mudabbarah in terms of emancipation from the estate.

Core Idea
An umm walad is freed from the master's entire estate, while a mudabbarah is freed from one-third.

The matn declares that a slave woman who gives birth to her master's child becomes an umm walad with a ruling similar to a mudabbarah. However, the commentary reveals significant differences: the umm walad is freed from the master's entire estate upon his death and is not liable for his debts, unlike the mudabbarah. This lesson breaks down the core ruling, its proof, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key legal entities
The passage discusses two statuses: umm walad (mother of a child) and mudabbarah (slave whose freedom is delayed until death). Note the initial similarity: both are freed upon the master's death.
Umm walad arises from childbirth; mudabbarah is a declaration by the master.
2
Locate the dalil for umm walad
The sharh cites the hadith: "أعتقها ولدها" (Her child set her free) regarding the Prophet's umm walad Mariya. This is the textual proof for her emancipation.
The hadith is ahad, so it provides zanni proof.
3
Compare emancipation scope
The commentary explicitly states that the umm walad is freed from the master's entire estate and does not need to work for creditors. The mudabbarah is freed only from one-third and may be required to work.
This is the key difference in financial consequence.
4
Analyze the scenario of husband-owner
If a man marries another's slave woman, has a child with her, then later owns her, she becomes his umm walad. He must pay his partner's share if co-owned.
This scenario shows how umm walad status can arise after ownership.
5
List practical differences (thamarah al-khilaf)
The passage lists many differences: umm walad cannot be sold, cannot be made a mudabbarah, her child's lineage requires acknowledgment, etc.
Refer to the commentary for full list.
